Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
15 min
Rules of Riba in Sales: Equality, Istizad, and the Two 'Illa
Hanafi commentary on riba rules, conditions, and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two 'illa of riba in the Hanafi school and apply them to determine when excess (tafadul) and credit (nasia) are permissible or prohibited.

Core Idea
Riba in sales is prohibited when two 'illa coincide: same genus and both measurable/weighable; absence of either permits excess but may still prohibit credit.

Riba (usury) is not limited to loans; it also governs the exchange of specific commodities. This lesson explains the Hanafi classification of riba based on two effective causes ('illa): unity of genus (jins) and the property of being measurable or weighable (kail/wazn). You will learn the three scenarios that determine whether excess or deferred payment is allowed, supported by hadith proofs and a practical legal stratagem (hila).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core prohibition
The matn states that selling good quality for bad in ribawi items is only permissible if equal measure. Any increase (istizad) constitutes riba, and both parties are equally sinful.
2
Extract the two 'illa from the hadith
From the hadith of six commodities (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt), the Hanafi school derives two 'illa: unity of genus (jins) and the attribute of being measurable or weighable (kail/wazn). These are the effective causes triggering riba.
The Shafi'i school uses a different second 'illa (foodstuff or currency).
3
Classify the three scenarios
Based on the presence or absence of these 'illa, three cases arise: (a) both 'illa present — excess and credit haram; (b) both absent — both halal; (c) one present — excess halal, credit haram.
The text provides examples for each case, e.g., gold for silver (different genus, both weighable) => excess halal, credit haram.
4
Examine the legal stratagem (hila)
To avoid riba when exchanging same genus with excess, one can sell one commodity for dirhams (money) and then buy the other with those dirhams, even from the same person. This breaks the direct exchange.
The hila is based on the hadith of the Khaybar date trader.
5
Apply the rulings to new cases
Using the two 'illa, determine permissibility for transactions like wheat for barley (different genus, both weighable) or selling gold on credit for silver now.
Always check both 'illa before concluding.

چاہو جبکہ ہاتھوں ہاتھ ہو (ج) آپ نے فرمایا.. پس جب یہ صنف الگ الگ ہو جائیں تو بچو جیسے چاہو بشرطیکہ ہاتھوں ہاتھ ہو (ج) آپ نے سونا کو چاندی کے بدلے ادھار بیچنے سے روکا۔
[935] (4) It is not permissible to sell good quality for bad quality in what involves riba except equal measure. [936] (5) If he seeks increase, then he has committed riba; the taker and the giver are equal in it. (a) Muslim Sharif, chapter of sarf and selling gold for silver cash p.24 no.587; Tirmidhi Sharif, chapter on that grains are equal measure and dislike of excess; Abu Dawud Sharif, chapter on sarf p.119 no.3349. In this hadith it says: sell equal, then it is correct and permissible. And if you do excess, it is not permissible. Similarly, if it is cash, it is permissible; if deferred, it is not permissible. [935] (4) And it is not permissible to sell good with bad in what involves riba except equal. The things in which riba occurs, for example wheat, even if one sells good wheat for bad wheat, still it must be sold equal; otherwise it becomes riba. In these things, good and bad exist precisely because of that sale. So if excess were allowed, the door of riba would open. Therefore, quality high or low is not considered. It must be sold equal. And if one does not want to sell equal, he should do like: sell two kg of bad dates to the buyer for one pound, and then buy one kg of good dates from the same buyer for one pound. In this way, dates are not exchanged for dates, but rather two kg of bad dates are exchanged for a pound, and one kg of good dates is taken for a pound. Hence the pound is the price of the dates, so it is permissible. (2) The hadith prohibits selling good dates for bad dates with excess, and it teaches the method of selling dates for dirhams. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah appointed a man over Khaybar, and he brought good dates. The Prophet said: 'Are all the dates of Khaybar like this?' He said: 'No, by Allah, we take one sa' of this for two sa' and two for three.' The Prophet said: 'Do not do so; sell the mixed dates for dirhams, then buy good dates with those dirhams.' (b) (Bukhari, chapter when one wants to sell dates for better dates p.293 no.201; Muslim, chapter selling food equal measure p.24 no.4082/1593). From this hadith, it is understood that in ribawi items, quality is not considered; it must be sold equal, otherwise it is riba. (1936) (5) If both attributes are absent, i.e., genus and the meaning attached to it, then excess is halal and deferred payment is also halal. Margin note: (a) The Prophet said: Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, equal measure, hand to hand. So whoever increases or seeks increase has committed riba; the taker and giver are equal in sin. (b) The Prophet appointed a man over Khaybar, so he brought good dates. The Prophet said: 'Are all the dates of Khaybar like this?' He said: 'No, by Allah, we take one sa' for two sa' and two for three.' The Prophet said: 'Do not do so; sell the poor dates for dirhams, then buy good dates with dirhams.' When both attributes are absent, i.e., genus and the meaning attached to it, then excess is halal and deferred is halal. [937] (6) And when both are found, then excess and deferred are haram. [938] (7) And when one is found and the other is absent, then excess is halal and deferred is haram. [Commentary] There are two causes of riba. If these two are not present, then excess is halal and deferred payment is halal. Taking possession in the session of the commodity and price is not necessary. One cause of riba is that both commodity and price are the same thing, e.g., both wheat or both rice. The second cause is that both are measurable or weighable. So if one sells wheat for barley, he may sell with excess. Similarly, if he sells gold for silver, he may sell with excess. In a hadith from Abu Bakra: The Prophet forbade silver for silver and gold for gold except equal, and commanded us to buy gold with silver as we wish and silver with gold as we wish (a) (Bukhari, chapter selling gold for silver hand to hand p.291 no.2182). Muslim adds: 'So when these attributes differ, sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' (b) (Muslim, chapter of sarf p.24 no.1587; Tirmidhi no.1240). This hadith indicates that if the genus changes, i.e., not the same type, and also not measurable/weighable (meaning both different in kind and not measurable), then deferred is also permissible. [937] (6) And if both causes are present, then excess is haram and deferred is haram. That is, both same genus and both measurable/weighable, then excess is haram and deferred is haram. The proof has passed: such equality and hand to hand. [938] (7) And if one of the two causes is present and the other absent, then excess is halal and deferred is haram. For example, commodity and price are not same genus but are both measurable or both weighable. E.g., wheat for rice or gold for silver: excess is halal but deferred is haram. Taking possession in the session is necessary. In a hadith, 'Ubada ibn al-Samit said: The Messenger of Allah said: ... So when these types differ, sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' (c) (Muslim, p.44 no.4063/1587; Tirmidhi no.1240). In Bukhari: The Prophet forbade selling gold for silver on credit. (d) (Bukhari, chapter selling silver for gold p.291 no.2180). This hadith indicates that gold and silver are both weighable, so credit is haram even though excess is allowed. And if the commodity and price are not measurable/weighable but are of the same type, then excess is permissible but deferred is haram. For example... Margin note: (a) The Prophet forbade selling silver for silver, and gold for gold except equal, and commanded us to sell gold for silver as we wish and silver for gold as we wish. (b) So when these types differ, sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand. (c) The Prophet said... So when these types differ, sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand. (d) The Prophet forbade selling gold for silver on credit.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi commentary on the rules of riba in sales, explaining a matn (possibly from Quduri) with proofs from hadith and practical examples. The author begins with the prohibition of selling good quality for bad quality in ribawi items (those subject to riba) unless it is equal measure (misl bi misl). This is based on the hadith that forbids excess in such transactions, as any inequality opens the door to riba. A legal stratagem (hila) is provided: instead of directly exchanging dates for dates with excess, sell the lower quality dates for dirhams, then buy the higher quality dates with those dirhams, even from the same person. This makes the transaction permissible because it bypasses the direct exchange of ribawi items. The text then mentions that seeking increase (istizad) in ribawi transactions is itself riba, and both parties are equally sinful. The commentary introduces the two 'illa (effective causes) of riba: (1) unity of genus (jins) and (2) the attribute of being measurable or weighable (kail or wazn). Based on these, three cases arise: (a) If both 'illa are absent (neither same genus nor both measurable/weighable), then both excess (tafadul) and deferred payment (nasia) are halal. (b) If both 'illa are present (same genus and both measurable/weighable), then both excess and credit are haram. (c) If one 'illa is present and the other absent (e.g., same genus but not measurable/weighable, or different genus but both measurable/weighable), then excess is halal but credit is haram. The commentary supports these rulings with hadith, including the well-known hadith about six commodities and the instruction to sell hand to hand when types differ. The author emphasizes that in all cases, if credit is haram, possession must occur in the session. The passage is characteristic of the Hanafi school's rigorous tahlil (causal analysis) of riba.

Key Terms
ربوا (ribā): Unlawful increase in exchange of certain commodities, either in quantity or time.
تفاضل (tafāḍul): Excess in quantity when exchanging two ribawi items of the same genus.
نساء (nasā’): Deferred payment or credit in a sale; here it refers to delaying the exchange of both counter-values in a ribawi transaction.
علة (‘illa): The effective cause that triggers the prohibition of riba in a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if two ribawi items are of the same genus but not measurable or weighable (e.g., two different types of fruit that are sold by number), what is the ruling on selling them with excess and on credit?
A) Both excess and credit are haram.
B) Excess is halal, credit is haram.
C) Excess is haram, credit is halal.
D) Both excess and credit are halal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's two 'illa of riba—unity of genus and measurability/weighability—determine permissibility of excess and credit in sales, with hila available to avoid direct ribawi exchange.

The Two Causes of Riba and Their Three Scenarios
Explaining the two 'illat of riba and the three-case matrix

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two 'illat of riba and apply them to determine the ruling on excess (riba al-fadl) and deferred payment (riba al-nasi'ah) for any exchange.

Core Idea
Riba is triggered by two independent causes: same genus and measurement; their combination decides the permissibility of excess and credit.

This lesson introduces the foundational classification of riba in the Hanafi school. The two causes (jins and kayl/wazn) operate independently, generating three distinct scenarios with different rulings on excess and credit. Mastering this matrix is essential for all sales transactions involving ribawi items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two 'illat
Recognise that riba is caused by two independent attributes: same genus (jins) and measurement by volume (kayl) or weight (wazn).
Genus means belonging to the same species, e.g., wheat and wheat. Measurement includes all items customarily sold by volume or weight, such as grains, gold, silver.
2
Classify the transaction
For a given exchange, determine whether the two items are of the same genus and whether they are measured/weighed.
For example, wheat and barley: different genus, both kayl.
3
Apply the three-case matrix
Map the presence/absence of the two 'illat to the rulings: (1) both absent → excess and credit halal; (2) both present → both haram; (3) one present → excess halal, credit haram.
This matrix is the core of Hanafi riba law.
4
Practice with examples
Work through examples: wheat for barley (different genus, both kayl → excess halal, credit haram), gold for gold (same genus, both wazn → both haram), walnuts for walnuts (same genus, neither kayl/wazn → excess halal, credit haram).
Counted items like walnuts are not kayl/wazn.

تو کمی بیشی بھی حلال ہوگی اور ادھار لینا بھی حلال ہوگا۔ مجلس میں مبیع اور شمن پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری نہیں ہوگا۔ سود کی ایک علت تھی کہ دونوں مبیع اور شمن ایک ہی چیز ہوں ، مثلا دونوں گیہوں ہوں یا دونوں چاول نمبر ۲۱۸۲) مسلم شریف میں یہ جملہ زیادہ ہے فاذا اخـتـلـفـت هذه الاوصاف فبيعوا كيف شئتم اذا كان يدا بيد (ب) (مسلم شريف، باب الصرف وبيع الذهب بالورق نقد اص ۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۸۷ ار ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء ان الحطة بالحطة مثلا بمثل ص ۲۳۵ نمبر ۱۲۴۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنس بدل جائے یعنی دونوں ایک ہی قسم کی چیز نہ ہوں اور کیلی اور وزنی بھی نہ ہوں تو ادھار بھی جائز ہے۔ [۹۳۷] (۶) اور اگر دونوں منتیں پائی جائیں تو کمی بیشی بھی حرام اور ادھار بھی حرام ۔ ان دونوں ایک جنس کے ہوں اور دونوں کیلی اور وزنی ہوں تو کمی بیشی بھی حرام اور ادھار بھی حرام ہوگا۔ دلیل او پر گزرچکی ہے۔ مثلا بمثل اور یدا بید۔ [۹۳۸] (۷) اور اگر دو علتوں میں سے ایک پائی جائے اور دوسری نہ پائی جائے تو کمی بیشی حلال ہے اور ادھار حرام ہے۔ ا مثلا بیع اور مشن دونوں ایک جنس کے نہیں ہیں لیکن دونوں کیلی ہیں یا دونوں وزنی ہیں۔ مثلا گیہوں کے بدلے چاول ہے یا سونے کے بدلے چاندی ہے تو کمی بیشی بلال ہے لیکن ادھار حرام ہوگا۔ دونوں پر مجلس میں قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے، حسن عبادة بن سامت قال قال رسول الله الا الله ... فاذا اختلفت هذه الاصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم اذا كان يدا بيد ( ج) (مسلم شریف، باب الصرف وبيع الذهب بالورق نقد ا ص ۴۴ نمبر ۴۰۶۳/۱۵۸۷ ترمذی شریف، نمبر ۱۲۴۰) بخاری شریف میں ہے نھی رسول الله لا لا اله عن بيع الذهب بالورق دینا (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب بیع الورق بالذهب نسبتة ص ۲۹۱ نمبر ۲۱۸۰) اس حدیث میں سونا اور چاندی دونوں وزنی ہیں اس لئے ادھار حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اگر چہ کی زیادت کو جائز قرار دیا۔ اور اگر بیع اور شمن کیلی اور وزنی نہ ہوں البتہ ایک ہی قسم کی دونوں چیزیں ہوں تو کمی زیادتی جائز ہے۔ لیکن اس صورت میں ادھار حرام ہوگا۔ مثلا اخروٹ کے بدلے میں اخروٹ خریدے تو اخروٹ عددی ہے اس لئے ایک اخروٹ دیکر دو اخروٹ لے سکتا ہے۔ لیکن ادھار جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ مجلس میں قبضہ کرنا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دونوں طرف جنس ایک ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر قال جاء عبد فبايع النبي له على الهجرة ولم يشعر انه عبد فجاء سيده يريده فقال له النبي الا الله بعنيه فاشتراه بعبدین اسودين (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب جواز بیع الحيوان بالحيوان من جنسه متفاضلاص ۳۰ نمبر ۱۶۰۲ / بخاری شریف، باب بیع العبد والحیوان نسیه ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۲۲۲۸) اس حدیث میں ایک غلام کو دو غلاموں کے بدلے میں خریدا ہے۔ اور ادھار حرام ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن سمرة بن جندب عن النبي له انه نهى عن بيع الحيوان بالحيوان نسيئة (ب) (سنن البيهتی ، باب ما جاء في النهي عن بيع الحيوان بالحيوان نسمية ، ج خامس بص ۴۷۲، نمبر ۱۰۵۳۲) اس حدیث میں عددی چیزوں کی جنس ایک ہو تو ادھار بیچنا حرام قرار دیا۔ النت النساء : ادھار۔
The book of sales. If the two attributes (genus and measure) are absent, excess and deferred payment are permissible. (6) If both are present, excess and deferred payment are prohibited. (7) If one is present and the other absent, excess is permissible and deferred payment is prohibited. [Then Urdu explanation:] Riba has two causes: (1) both items are of the same genus, e.g., both wheat or both rice; (2) both are measured by volume (kayl) or by weight (wazn). If you sell wheat for barley, you may do so with excess; similarly selling gold for silver. Hadith from Abu Bakra: The Prophet prohibited selling silver for silver and gold for gold except equal for equal, and permitted us to sell gold for silver as we wished. In Muslim: When these descriptions differ, sell as you wish hand to hand. This hadith means if the genus is different and they are not measured by volume or weight, deferred payment is also permissible. (6) If both causes are present, both excess and deferred payment are prohibited. Evidence is from the same hadith: equal for equal and hand to hand. (7) If one cause is present and the other absent, excess is halal and deferred payment is haram, e.g., wheat for rice or gold for silver. Both must be taken possession of in the session. Hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit: When these categories differ, sell as you wish hand to hand. Another hadith prohibits selling gold for silver on credit, because both are weighed. If the items are not measured but of the same genus, e.g., walnuts for walnuts (counted items), exactly one walnut for two walnuts is permissible but not on credit; possession must be in the session. Hadith from Jabir: The Prophet bought a slave with two black slaves. Hadith from Samurah: The Prophet prohibited selling animals for animals on credit. Conclusion: deferred payment is prohibition.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the two causes ('illat) of riba and the resulting rulings. The author, following the Hanafi school, identifies two independent causes that trigger riba: (1) same genus (jins), and (2) measurement by volume (kayl) or weight (wazn). When both causes are absent (items of different genus and not kayl/wazn), both riba al-fadl (excess) and riba al-nasi'ah (deferred payment) are permissible. When both are present (same genus and both kayl/wazn), both types are prohibited. When only one is present, riba al-fadl is permissible but riba al-nasi'ah is prohibited. The text provides hadith proofs: the hadith of Abu Bakra establishes the prohibition when both causes are present; the hadith of Ubadah shows that when categories differ (different genus or different measure), excess is allowed only hand to hand; the hadith of Jabir and Samurah illustrate the prohibition of credit when genus is same but items are not kayl/wazn (like animals or counted items). The note 'النت النساء : ادھار' summarizes that the key issue in case of one 'illah is the prohibition of deferred payment.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The effective cause that legally justifies a ruling; in this context, the two 'illah of riba are same genus and measurement by volume/weight.
جنس (jins): Genus; monetary equivalence: items belonging to the same species or category for riba purposes, e.g., wheat and wheat, gold and gold.
كيل (kayl): Measurement by volume; a standard measure used in trade, e.g., bushels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person sells 1 kg of rice for 1.2 kg of rice with deferred payment, what is the ruling?
A) Both excess and deferred are permissible.
B) Excess is permissible, deferred is prohibited.
C) Both excess and deferred are prohibited.
D) Excess is prohibited, deferred is permissible.

Key Takeaway
Riba is governed by two independent causes: same genus and measurement; the presence of both prohibits excess and credit, while the presence of only one prohibits only credit.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
The Hadith Proofs for the Riba Rulings
Citing hadith evidence for the two-'illah matrix

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite the key hadiths that establish the Hanafi rulings on riba and explain how each hadith supports the two-'illah matrix.

Core Idea
The Hanafi two-'illah matrix is derived from a set of hadiths that distinguish between same genus, different genus, and measurement attributes.

This lesson delves into the primary textual evidence (dalil) used by the Hanafi school to establish the three-case matrix of riba. The hadiths of Abu Bakra, Ubadah ibn al-Samit, and Samurah directly address exchange of gold, silver, and food items, and the Hanafi school uses qiyas to extend these rulings to all measured and weighed items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key hadiths
The passage cites several hadiths: the hadith of Abu Bakra (prohibiting same genus with excess), the hadith of Ubadah (allowing excess when categories differ, but hand-to-hand), the hadith of Samurah (prohibiting deferred payment for animals of same genus), and the hadith of Jabir (permitting excess in slave exchange).
Also referenced: the hadith of 'gold for silver on credit' (Bukhari).
2
Analyse the hadith of Abu Bakra
In this hadith, the Prophet prohibits selling silver for silver or gold for gold except equal for equal (sa'wa bi sa'wa), but permits selling gold for silver as one wishes. This establishes that same genus + same measure triggers riba al-fadl.
The phrase 'ila sawa' bi sawa' indicates equality in quantity is required for same genus.
3
Analyse the hadith of Ubadah
The addition in Muslim: 'When these categories differ, sell as you wish hand to hand.' This shows that when genus or measure differ, excess is allowed but credit is not.
This is the proof for the third scenario (one 'illah present).
4
Understand the qiyas extension
The Hanafi school extends the rulings from the six specified items (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) to all items measured by volume (kayl) or weight (wazn) based on the common attribute of measurement.
This extension is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) because the 'illah of measurement is explicit.

Source Text

The book of sales. If the two attributes (genus and measure) are absent, excess and deferred payment are permissible. (6) If both are present, excess and deferred payment are prohibited. (7) If one is present and the other absent, excess is permissible and deferred payment is prohibited. [Then Urdu explanation:] Riba has two causes: (1) both items are of the same genus, e.g., both wheat or both rice; (2) both are measured by volume (kayl) or by weight (wazn). If you sell wheat for barley, you may do so with excess; similarly selling gold for silver. Hadith from Abu Bakra: The Prophet prohibited selling silver for silver and gold for gold except equal for equal, and permitted us to sell gold for silver as we wished. In Muslim: When these descriptions differ, sell as you wish hand to hand. This hadith means if the genus is different and they are not measured by volume or weight, deferred payment is also permissible. (6) If both causes are present, both excess and deferred payment are prohibited. Evidence is from the same hadith: equal for equal and hand to hand. (7) If one cause is present and the other absent, excess is halal and deferred payment is haram, e.g., wheat for rice or gold for silver. Both must be taken possession of in the session. Hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit: When these categories differ, sell as you wish hand to hand. Another hadith prohibits selling gold for silver on credit, because both are weighed. If the items are not measured but of the same genus, e.g., walnuts for walnuts (counted items), exactly one walnut for two walnuts is permissible but not on credit; possession must be in the session. Hadith from Jabir: The Prophet bought a slave with two black slaves. Hadith from Samurah: The Prophet prohibited selling animals for animals on credit. Conclusion: deferred payment is prohibition.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the two causes ('illat) of riba and the resulting rulings. The author, following the Hanafi school, identifies two independent causes that trigger riba: (1) same genus (jins), and (2) measurement by volume (kayl) or weight (wazn). When both causes are absent (items of different genus and not kayl/wazn), both riba al-fadl (excess) and riba al-nasi'ah (deferred payment) are permissible. When both are present (same genus and both kayl/wazn), both types are prohibited. When only one is present, riba al-fadl is permissible but riba al-nasi'ah is prohibited. The text provides hadith proofs: the hadith of Abu Bakra establishes the prohibition when both causes are present; the hadith of Ubadah shows that when categories differ (different genus or different measure), excess is allowed only hand to hand; the hadith of Jabir and Samurah illustrate the prohibition of credit when genus is same but items are not kayl/wazn (like animals or counted items). The note 'النت النساء : ادھار' summarizes that the key issue in case of one 'illah is the prohibition of deferred payment.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The effective cause that legally justifies a ruling; in this context, the two 'illah of riba are same genus and measurement by volume/weight.
حديث (hadith): A report of the words, actions, or tacit approvals of the Prophet Muhammad.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on the 'Illah of Riba
Comparing Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the 'illah of riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the 'illah of riba and evaluate the practical consequences of each position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school recognises two independent 'illat for riba (jins and kayl/wazn), while the Shafi'i school limits riba to specific textual categories, leading to different scopes of prohibition.

This lesson examines the inter-madhhab dispute on the definition of the cause ('illah) of riba. The Hanafi school, through qiyas, extends the prohibition to all items measured by volume or weight, while the Shafi'i school restricts it to the six items explicitly mentioned in the hadith (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt). Understanding this dispute clarifies why certain exchanges are ribawi in one school but not the other.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Hanafi: Riba is triggered by two independent 'illat: same genus (jins) and measurement (kayl/wazn). This extends to all items customarily sold by volume or weight, not just the six specified items.
This is based on qiyas: the common attribute of measurement.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i: Riba applies only to the six items mentioned in the hadith (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) and only when they are exchanged for the same genus. Measurement (kayl) is not an independent 'illah; it is a property of those specific items.
Shafi'i considers the 'illah for food items to be 'food that is measured by kayl' but only for those specific types.
3
Identify the evidence for each
Hanafi relies on the hadith of Abu Bakra and Ubadah and uses inductive reasoning (istiqra) to conclude that measurement is the 'illah. Shafi'i relies on the explicit mention of only six items in the hadith of Ubadah and does not extend via qiyas.
The dispute is methodological: Hanafi uses broader qiyas, Shafi'i limits to textual evidence.
4
Determine the practical difference
In Hanafi, any exchange of different genus but both kayl/wazn (e.g., wheat for rice) allows excess but not credit. In Shafi'i, such an exchange is not ribawi at all if both items are not among the six specified categories, so both excess and credit are permissible.
Example: selling 1 kg of rice for 1.2 kg of barley. Hanafi: excess halal, credit haram. Shafi'i: both halal if rice and barley are not specifically mentioned? Actually Shafi'i considers all food items measured by kayl to be ribawi only if same genus. Since rice and barley are different genus, no riba. So excess and credit both halal.

The book of sales. If the two attributes (genus and measure) are absent, excess and deferred payment are permissible. (6) If both are present, excess and deferred payment are prohibited. (7) If one is present and the other absent, excess is permissible and deferred payment is prohibited. [Then Urdu explanation:] Riba has two causes: (1) both items are of the same genus, e.g., both wheat or both rice; (2) both are measured by volume (kayl) or by weight (wazn). If you sell wheat for barley, you may do so with excess; similarly selling gold for silver. Hadith from Abu Bakra: The Prophet prohibited selling silver for silver and gold for gold except equal for equal, and permitted us to sell gold for silver as we wished. In Muslim: When these descriptions differ, sell as you wish hand to hand. This hadith means if the genus is different and they are not measured by volume or weight, deferred payment is also permissible. (6) If both causes are present, both excess and deferred payment are prohibited. Evidence is from the same hadith: equal for equal and hand to hand. (7) If one cause is present and the other absent, excess is halal and deferred payment is haram, e.g., wheat for rice or gold for silver. Both must be taken possession of in the session. Hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit: When these categories differ, sell as you wish hand to hand. Another hadith prohibits selling gold for silver on credit, because both are weighed. If the items are not measured but of the same genus, e.g., walnuts for walnuts (counted items), exactly one walnut for two walnuts is permissible but not on credit; possession must be in the session. Hadith from Jabir: The Prophet bought a slave with two black slaves. Hadith from Samurah: The Prophet prohibited selling animals for animals on credit. Conclusion: deferred payment is prohibition.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the two causes ('illat) of riba and the resulting rulings. The author, following the Hanafi school, identifies two independent causes that trigger riba: (1) same genus (jins), and (2) measurement by volume (kayl) or weight (wazn). When both causes are absent (items of different genus and not kayl/wazn), both riba al-fadl (excess) and riba al-nasi'ah (deferred payment) are permissible. When both are present (same genus and both kayl/wazn), both types are prohibited. When only one is present, riba al-fadl is permissible but riba al-nasi'ah is prohibited. The text provides hadith proofs: the hadith of Abu Bakra establishes the prohibition when both causes are present; the hadith of Ubadah shows that when categories differ (different genus or different measure), excess is allowed only hand to hand; the hadith of Jabir and Samurah illustrate the prohibition of credit when genus is same but items are not kayl/wazn (like animals or counted items). The note 'النت النساء : ادھار' summarizes that the key issue in case of one 'illah is the prohibition of deferred payment.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The effective cause that legally justifies a ruling; in this context, the two 'illah of riba are same genus and measurement by volume/weight.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.

Permanence of Kayl and Wazn Categories in Riba
Items categorized as kayl or wazn by the Prophet remain so forever regardless of later practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the Prophet's explicit categorization of an item as kayl or wazn is permanent and apply it to determine the riba ruling for a given item.

Core Idea
The Prophet's designation of kayl/wazn is eternal; later custom cannot change it.

This passage establishes a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: once the Prophet explicitly categorized an item as measured by volume (kayl) or weight (wazn) in the context of riba, that classification remains forever, regardless of changes in commercial practice. The ruling is supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar and the general principle that the Prophet's legislation is for all times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The author states that any item the Prophet explicitly mentioned as kayl or wazn in riba remains so forever. Identify the key terms: 'makil' and 'mawzun' and their permanence.
2
Recognize the evidence
The dalil is a hadith from Ibn Umar fixing the standards of weight and measure to Makkah and Madinah. This indicates the categories are Prophetic designations, not subject to change.
The hadith is ahad, but it is sufficient for this rule.
3
Apply to examples
Apply the rule to the given examples: wheat, barley, dates, salt (kayl); gold, silver (wazn). Confirm that even if today these are sold by a different method, the original classification stands.
4
Distinguish from other schools
Note that the Shafi'i school does not hold this permanence; they base the 'illah on being a staple food or gold/silver. Understand the practical difference.
This distinction is important for inter-madhhab comparisons.
5
Conclude the practical effect
For Hanafis, the riba ruling for these items is fixed. If a transaction involves unequal exchange by the original measure, it is riba regardless of current market practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحرم النساء [۹۳۹] (۸) وكل شيء نص رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على تحريم التفاضل فيه كيلا فهو مكيل ابدا وان ترك الناس فيه الكيل مثل الحنطة والشعير والتمر والملح. وكل شيء نص على تحريم التفاضل فيه وزنا فهو موزون ابدا وان ترك الناس فيه الوزن مثل الذهب والفضة. [ثم شرح بالأردية:] حضور کے زمانے میں جو چیزیں کیلی تھیں وہ قیامت تک کیلی ہی رہیں گی ۔ اور کمی بیشی کا اعتبار کیل کے اعتبار سے ہوگا۔ چاہے بعد میں لوگوں نے ان چیزوں کو کیل کرنا چھوڑ دیا ہو۔ مثلا گیہوں ، جو، کھجور اور نمک وغیرہ حضور کے زمانے میں کیل سے بیچے جاتے تھے اور حضور نے تصریح کی ہے کہ یہ کیلی ہیں اس لئے وہ ہمیشہ کیلی ہی رہیں گی۔ چاہے آج کل لوگوں نے ان چیزوں کو وزن کر کے بیچنا شروع کر دیا ہے۔ اور جو چیزیں حضور کے زمانے میں وزنی تھیں اور آپ نے تصریح فرمائی ہے کہ یہ وزنی ہیں تو وہ قیامت تک وزنی ہی کے اعتبار سے سود کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ مثلا سونا اور چاندی حضور کے زمانے میں وزنی تھے اور آپ نے تصریح فرمائی ہے کہ یہ وزنی ہیں اس لئے قیامت تک وزنی رہیں گے آپ کی حدیث قیامت تک کے لئے ہے اور آپ کا دین قیامت تک کے لئے ہے اس لئے آپ کی تصریح کا اعتبار بھی قیامت تک رہے گا۔ حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله الوزن وزن اهل مكة والمكيال مكيال اهل المدينه (ج) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی قول النبی ا الکسیال مکیال المدینی ص ۱۸ امبر ۳۳۴۰) اس حدیث میں اشارہ ہے کہ وزن میں اہل مکہ کا اعتبار ہے اور کیل میں اہل مدینہ کا اعتبار ہے۔
And prohibition of deferred payment. (8) Every item that the Messenger of Allah (may peace be upon him) explicitly mentioned the prohibition of excess in it as measured (by volume) remains measured forever, even if people abandon measuring it, like wheat, barley, dates, and salt. And every item that he explicitly mentioned the prohibition of excess in it as weighed remains weighed forever, even if people abandon weighing it, like gold and silver. [Urdu explanation:] Items that were measured by volume in the Prophet's time remain so until Judgement Day. The ruling of excess is based on the original measurement, regardless of later changes in practice. Items that were weighed remain weighed forever. A hadith from Ibn Umar: The Prophet said, 'The weight is the weight of the people of Makkah, and the measure is the measure of the people of Madinah.' This indicates that the standard of weight and measure is fixed.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the permanence of the categories of measurement (kayl and wazn) for riba purposes as set by the Prophet. The author argues that once the Prophet explicitly categorized an item as kayl or wazn in the context of riba, that categorization is eternal and cannot be altered by subsequent changes in commercial practice. For example, wheat, barley, dates, and salt were kayl in the Prophet's time; even if people begin selling them by weight today, they are still considered kayl for riba rulings. Similarly, gold and silver remain wazn. The proof is twofold: first, the hadith of Ibn Umar which fixes the standard of weight to the people of Makkah and measure to the people of Madinah, implying that these categories are established by the Prophet himself and are not subject to change; second, the general principle that the Prophet's legislation is for all times. The commentary emphasizes that the Prophet's explicit mention ('nass') is binding forever, and later custom cannot override it. This is a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: the 'illah of riba for these items is fixed by the Prophet's designation, not by contemporary market practices.

Key Terms
مكيل (makil): An item that is measured by volume (kayl); the Prophet's explicit categorization makes it permanently subject to kayl rulings for riba
موزون (mawzun): An item that is measured by weight (wazn); similarly permanent for riba purposes
نص (nass): Explicit textual statement from the Prophet that establishes a ruling; here it refers to the explicit mention of kayl/wazn for certain items

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wazn, because that is how it is now sold
B) Kayl, because it was kayl in the time of the Prophet
C) It depends on the region's custom
D) Neither, it is now counted

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's explicit categorization of an item as kayl or wazn for riba rulings is permanent and cannot be overridden by later custom.

Classification of Ribā Items: Fixed Nass vs Custom
Ruling on classification of ribā items as weighed or measured, with custom as determinant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between items whose classification as mawzūn or makīl is fixed by explicit sacred text and those determined by custom, and apply the Hanafi view on changing custom to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Items explicitly prohibited from disparity in weight are always weighed; all others follow the custom of the people.

This lesson addresses a critical question in Hanafi fiqh of transactions: how do we determine whether an item is considered weighed (mawzūn) or measured (makīl) for the rules of ribā al-faḍl? The source passage establishes two categories: items explicitly mentioned in sacred texts as subject to prohibition in weight are permanently weighed, regardless of later practice; all other items are classified based on the prevailing custom of the people. The passage also introduces an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a change in custom alters the classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the passage and separate items into (1) those explicitly mentioned in sacred texts as prohibited from disparity in weight, and (2) those not explicitly mentioned.
Examples of the first category include salt, gold, and silver (mentioned in hadith).
2
Understand the fixed nature of the first category
Note that items in the first category are considered weighed 'forever' (أبداً) even if people abandon weighing them. Their classification is permanent.
This is based on the explicit prohibition in the sacred text (nass).
3
Grasp the role of custom for the second category
For items not explicitly mentioned, the passage states they are 'carried upon the customs of the people' (محمول على عادات الناس). Their classification as weighed or measured depends on prevailing practice.
Custom ('urf) is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school for matters not regulated by nass.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on changing custom
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that if the custom changes, the ruling changes accordingly. For example, if people shift from selling wheat by measure to selling by weight, the ribā rules now apply based on weight.
This is a legitimate difference within the school; the operative position (muftā bihī) often follows Abu Yusuf.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a community where rice (not mentioned in explicit nass) is now sold by weight, determine its classification and the applicable ribā rules using the passage's framework.
Consider both the fixed custom view and the possibility of change per Abu Yusuf.

Salt and everything for which disparity in weight is explicitly prohibited, it is considered weighed forever, even if people abandon weighing it, like gold and silver. [940] (9) And whatever is not explicitly stated is carried upon the customs of the people. [941] (10) ... And a second point: that which the people of Medina declare to be measured is measured, and that which the people of Mecca declare to be weighed is weighed. In Mecca, your (the Prophet's) ruling also prevailed, so it is as if you declared something weighed, it is weighed, and what you declared measured, it is measured. Imam Abu Yusuf says: if custom has changed, then now judgment will be according to the new custom. For example, if people now sell wheat by kilogram instead of measure, then the basis for riba will be kilogram, not measure. In the Prophet's time, judgment was according to the custom of the people. So if custom changes, judgment changes. [1940] (9) And whatever is not explicitly stated is carried upon the custom of the people.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding how to determine whether an item is considered weighed (mawzūn) or measured (makīl) for the purposes of riba al-fadl. The first part states that any item explicitly mentioned in the sacred texts as being subject to prohibition of disparity in weight is always considered weighed, regardless of local practice. Examples include gold and silver. The second part clarifies that items not explicitly mentioned are determined by the prevailing custom ('urf) of the people. The commentary then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, if the custom changes, the ruling changes accordingly. For instance, if wheat was traditionally sold by measure (kayl) but people start selling by weight (kilogram), the riba consideration shifts to weight. This illustrates the Hanafi reliance on custom as a source of law in matters not explicitly regulated by nass.

Key Terms
موزون (mawzūn): An item that is customarily sold by weight, and for which disparity in weight is prohibited in riba transactions.
کیلی / مكيل (kaylī / makīl): An item that is customarily sold by measure (volume).
عادت (ʿādah): Custom or prevailing practice of the people in a particular region.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is always considered weighed.
B) It is always considered measured.
C) Its status is determined by the custom of the people.
D) It is not subject to riba rules.

Key Takeaway
The classification of riba items is either fixed by explicit nass or determined by custom, and custom can change over time according to Imam Abu Yusuf.

Contract of Sarf: Possession vs Specification in Ribawi Transactions
Defines sarf contract and condition of possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sarf contracts and explain why specification suffices for other ribawi items.

Core Idea
In sarf, hand-to-hand possession is required; for other ribawi goods, mere specification suffices under Hanafi law.

This passage defines the contract of sarf and lays out a key distinction: for gold and silver, possession must occur in the session, while for grains and other ribawi items, only specification (ta'yin) is needed. The proof is the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit, which the Hanafis interpret to allow specification. The Shafi'i school disagrees, requiring possession for all ribawi items. We will analyze the ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sarf contract—exchange of gold or silver. The ruling is that possession (qabd) of both countervalues in the session is a condition for validity.
Possession here means physical hand-to-hand delivery.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit from Sahih Muslim, which lists ribawi items and ends with 'specified for specified' (عينا بعين).
The full hadith is quoted in the passage.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'specified for specified' indicates that for these items, identification of the specific object suffices; it does not require 'hand to hand'. Hanafis apply this to grains and apply 'hand to hand' hadiths to gold/silver.
This is a reconciliation of different hadith wordings.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i requires possession for all ribawi items, including grains, based on hadiths with 'hand to hand'.
The practical difference: selling wheat for wheat by specification alone is valid in the Hanafi school, not in the Shafi'i school.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow wheat-for-wheat exchange with mere specification; Shafi'is require hand-to-hand delivery.
This affects contracts in marketplaces where physical exchange of grains is impractical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the contract of sarf – what occurs on the genus of prices (gold and silver) – possession of both countervalues in the session is considered. And other than that from the ribawi items, specification is considered, not hand-to-hand possession. [11942] And it is not permissible to sell wheat for flour, nor for sawiq, and likewise flour for sawiq. [942] The asl for prices – i.e., dirhams and dinars – are not specified by mere specification until possession is taken. (2) Grains and commodities are specified by specification. There is an indication of this in the hadith: 'Balaghah that Ubadah ibn al-Samit stood and said: I heard the Messenger of Allah prohibit selling gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, except equal for equal, specified for specified.' (Muslim) In this hadith, instead of 'hand to hand' it says 'specified for specified.' Its meaning is that the thing becomes specified and becomes a specific entity. Therefore, the Hanafis apply this hadith to grains and say that in grains, mere specification is sufficient to avoid deferred riba. And they apply 'hand to hand' to gold and silver. Imam al-Shafi'i considers possession necessary even for grains to avoid deferred riba. His proof is the hadiths that say 'hand to hand', meaning that possession is required.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof regarding the contract of sarf (exchange of gold and silver). The Hanafi position is that for sarf, hand-to-hand possession (qabd) of both countervalues must occur in the same session (majlis). For other ribawi items (e.g., grains), only specification (ta'yin) is required, not actual physical possession. The proof is the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit which uses the phrase 'specified for specified' (عينا بعين), indicating that for grains, mere identification of the specific item suffices. The Hanafis interpret 'hand to hand' (يدا بيد) found in other hadiths as applying specifically to gold and silver. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, requiring possession for all ribawi items. The passage then transitions to a separate ruling about selling wheat for flour or sawiq, which is prohibited due to lack of equality (since volume changes). The commentary also clarifies that for prices (gold/silver), possession is necessary for specification, while for other goods, specification alone suffices.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): The exchange of gold for gold, silver for silver, or gold for silver, i.e., the sale of one currency for another.
تعيين (ta'yīn): Specification of a particular item in a contract, e.g., pointing to a specific heap of wheat.
يقابض / تقابض (taqābuḍ): Hand-to-hand possession, i.e., physical receipt and delivery of the exchanged items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sarf contracts require hand-to-hand possession in the session; for other ribawi items, mere specification suffices to avoid riba, based on the hadith's wording 'specified for specified'.

Prohibition of Selling Wheat for Flour or Sawiq
Ruling on exchanging wheat for its derivatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging wheat for its derivatives and explain the evidenciary basis from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Wheat cannot be sold for flour or sawiq because equality of measure is impossible – the prophetic hadith on fresh dates proves the principle.

This lesson examines a classical ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the exchange of wheat for its processed derivatives such as flour or sawiq. The ruling is rooted in the principle of riba al-fadl (usury of surplus), which requires exact equality in weight or measure when exchanging items of the same genus. The passage provides both the ruling and its proof from the Sunnah and the practice of the early Muslims (athar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what transaction is being ruled upon and the legal classification (hukm). The act is selling wheat for flour or sawiq, and the ruling is haram (prohibited).
The same ruling applies to flour for sawiq.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is a hadith narrated by Sa'd (may Allah be pleased with him) in Sunan al-Daraqutni regarding the prohibition of selling fresh dates for dried dates. The hadith is cited because the illa (effective cause) applies to wheat and its derivatives.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain transmission), so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith demonstrates that when two items of the same genus are exchanged, they must be equal in measure. If one is fresh (moist) and the other dry, the volume changes upon drying, making equality uncertain. By analogy, wheat and its derivatives differ in density when measured by volume, leading to inequality in weight.
The Hanafi school relies on this analogy (qiyas) to extend the ruling to all processed forms of the same genus.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage indicates that other schools may allow such sales if the exchange is by weight rather than volume. The Hanafis, however, consider volume measurement problematic because the density difference inevitably causes inequality.
This is a valid scholarly difference; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Apply the tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith and the athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab who explicitly declared such a transaction as riba. Hence, the prohibition is established and relied upon in practice.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز بيع الحنطة بالدقيق ولا بالسويق وكذلك الدقيق بالسويق [11942] ولا يجوز بيع الحنطة بالدقيق ولا بالسويق وكذلك الدقيق بالسويق [942] ... گیہوں کو گیہوں کے آنے کے بدلے میں بیچے یا اس کے ستو کے بدلے میں بیچے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ کسی برتن میں ناپنے کے لئے گیہوں ڈالے گا تو مثلا ایک کیلوگیہوں آئے لیکن اسی برتن میں اس کا آٹا ڈالے گا تو سوا کیلو آئے گا۔ کیونکہ گیہوں ہلکے ہوتے ہیں اور بڑے بڑے دانے ہوتے ہیں۔ اور آٹا باریک ہونے کی وجہ سے دب جائے گا اور زیادہ آئے گا۔ تو برتن کے بھرنے کے اعتبار سے برابر ہے لیکن وزن کے اعتبار سے بہت فرق ہوگا ۔ اس لئے مساوات نہیں ہوئی اور دونوں ایک ہی قسم کی چیز اور جنس ہیں اس لئے مساوات اور برابری ضروری تھی اور وہ ہوئی نہیں اس لئے گیہوں کو آٹے کے بدلے یا ستو کے بدلے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بیچنا ہی ہو تو درہم اور پونڈ کے بدلے بیچے (۲) حدیث میں ایسی بیج سے منع فرمایا ہے قال سعد سمعت رسول الله سئل عمن اشترى التمر بالرطب فقال اينقض الرطب اذا يبس فقالوا نعم فهى عن ذلك (الف) (دار قطنی) اس حدیث میں تر کھجور اور خشک کھجور ایک جنس ہیں لیکن صاع اور برتن میں تر کھجور کم آئے گا اور اسی برتن میں خشک کھجور زیادہ آئے گا۔ اس لئے کیلو کے اعتبار سے مساوات نہیں ہوگی اس لئے آپ نے منع فرمایا۔ بلکہ پوچھا کیا تر کھجور بعد میں کم ہو جائے گا ؟ تو صحابہ نے فرمایا کہ ہاں ! بعد میں کم ہوگا تو آپ نے تر کھجور کو خشک کھجور کے بدلے بیچنے کو منع فرمایا ۔ یہی حال گیہوں اور اس کے آنے کا اور گیہوں اور اس کے ستو کا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن سعید بن مسيب في البر بالدقيق قال هو ربا (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ) گیہوں کا آٹا ہو اور گیہوں ہی کا ستو ہو تو بھی دونوں کو بیچنا جائز نہیں۔
And it is not permissible to sell wheat for flour, nor for sawiq, and likewise flour for sawiq. [11942] ... Selling wheat for flour or for sawiq is not permissible. If one puts wheat in a vessel to measure, say one kilo of wheat, but if he puts flour in the same vessel, it will be more than a kilo. Because wheat is light and has large grains, while flour is fine and will pack down, resulting in more. So in terms of volume, they are equal, but in weight there is a big difference. Therefore, equality is not achieved, and both are of the same type and genus, so equality was required. Since it is not achieved, selling wheat for flour or for sawiq is not permissible. If one must sell, let him sell for dirhams and pounds. (2) The hadith prohibits such a sale: Sa'd said: I heard the Messenger of Allah was asked about a person who bought fresh dates for dried dates. He said: 'Does the fresh dates' volume reduce when they dry?' They said yes, so he prohibited that. (Dar Qutni) In this hadith, fresh dates and dried dates are of the same genus, but in a measure, fresh dates will be less and dried dates more. So equality is not achieved in terms of volume, so he prohibited. This is the same case with wheat and its flour, and wheat and its sawiq. (2) There is an athar: From Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab regarding wheat for flour: he said it is riba. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) Whether it is wheat flour or wheat sawiq, selling them is not permissible.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage delivers a ruling with proof on the impermissibility of exchanging wheat for its derivatives (flour or sawiq) when they are of the same genus. The reason is the likely inequality in volume: when measured by the same container, wheat and its flour do not weigh the same due to differences in density. Since riba al-fadl requires exact equality in weight or measure for the same genus, this transaction results in uncertainty and potential excess. The proof is drawn from the prophetic hadith prohibiting the sale of fresh dates for dried dates because fresh dates shrink upon drying, causing inequality in volume. This is qiyas: the illa is the lack of certainty of equality. The passage also cites an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab declaring such a transaction riba. Hence, the Hanafi position is that such sales are not valid; instead, one should sell for a different genus (e.g., currency).

Key Terms
ربوا (ribā): Usury or prohibited increase in exchange of goods. Specifically riba al-fadl (surplus) and riba al-nasi'ah (delay).
حنطة (ḥinṭah): Wheat.
دقيق (daqīq): Flour, derived from wheat.
سويق (sawīq): A type of roasted barley or wheat meal, often mixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Wheat cannot be exchanged for its processed derivatives (flour or sawiq) because the required certainty of equality is absent, as proven by the prophetic hadith on fresh dates and the companion's ruling of riba.

Hanafi View on Hand-to-Hand Exchange in Grain Transactions
Inter-madhhab dispute on taqabud in ribawi items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the necessity of taqabud in grain transactions and identify the key proof that distinguishes grains from precious metals.

Core Idea
For grains, specification (ta'yin) suffices to prevent riba; only gold and silver require hand-to-hand exchange.

In this passage, the author addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether grains such as wheat require physical hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) to avoid riba. The passage explains that, according to Hanafis, specification (ta'yin) of the item in the contract is sufficient for grains and similar commodities. Only gold and silver (thaman) require actual possession. This distinction has significant implications for the validity of deferred sales of staple foods.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on grains vs. gold/silver
Identify the general rule: specification (ta'yin) suffices for grains; hand-to-hand (taqabud) is required for gold and silver. Note the exception for the two precious metals.
The passage states: 'The assembly and other than it that contains riba: specification is considered but hand-to-hand exchange is not considered.' Then it adds: 'As for the two precious metals, they are not specified by specification until possession is taken.'
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hand-to-hand exchange is necessary even in grains to avoid riba. His evidence is the hadiths requiring 'yadan bi-yad' (hand-to-hand).
The passage says: 'Imam Shafi'i considers possession necessary even in grains to avoid debt. His evidence is the hadith of 'hand to hand'.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis rely on a hadith that says 'eye to eye' (عيناً بعين) which they interpret as requiring specification, not hand-to-hand, for grains. They also cite the hadith of Sa'd about fresh and dry dates, which shows that inequality in weight/volume is the reason for prohibition, not lack of hand-to-hand exchange.
The passage explains: 'This hadith: 'eye to eye' instead of 'hand to hand' means the thing is specified. So Hanafis apply this hadith to grains.'
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
Shafi'is cite hadiths like 'yadan bi-yad'. Hanafis respond that those hadiths apply specifically to gold and silver (thaman), not to grains. They maintain that grains are governed by the 'eye to eye' hadith.
The Hanafi response: 'Those hadiths apply to gold and silver (thaman) only, not to grains.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If grains are sold without immediate physical exchange (e.g., deferred delivery), the sale is valid according to Hanafis (with ta'yin) but invalid according to Shafi'is. This affects everyday transactions like buying wheat for future delivery.
The madhhab dispute map states: 'If grains are sold without immediate exchange, it is valid according to Hanafis but invalid according to Shafi'is.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى
LA
كتاب البيوع
المجلس وماسواه مما فيه الربوا يعتبر فيه التعيين ولا يعتبر فيه التقابض [۱۱۹۴۲) ولا
يجوز بيع الحنطة بالدقيق ولا بالسويق وكذلك الدقيق بالسويق
باب الصرف ونبيع الذهب بالورق نقد اص ۲۳ نمبر ۱۵۸۷) اس حدیث میں یدا بید کے بجائے عینا بعین ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ چیز متعین ہو جائے اور عین شی ہو جائے۔ اس لئے حنفیہ اس حدیث کو غلہ جات پر محمول کرتے ہیں اور فرماتے ہیں کہ غلہ جات میں صرف تعین ہو جائے تو ادھار سے بچنے کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اور یدا بید کوشن پر محمول کرتے ہیں۔
امام شافعی غلہ جات میں بھی ادھار سے بچنے کے لئے قبضہ کرناضروری قرار دیتے ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل احادیث پیدا بید والی ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔
اصا اثمان یعنی درہم اور دنا نیر متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے جب تک کہ قبضہ نہ کر لئے جائیں (۲) غلہ جات اور سامان متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ [۱۹۴۲ (۱۱) اور نہیں جائز ہے گیہوں کی بیع آئے سے اور نہ ستو سے اور ایسے ہی آٹے کی بیع ستو سے۔ گیہوں کو گیہوں کے آنے کے بدلے میں بیچے یا اس کے ستو کے بدلے میں بیچے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔
کسی برتن میں ناپنے کے لئے گیہوں ڈالے گا تو مثلا ایک کیلوگیہوں آئے لیکن اسی برتن میں اس کا آٹا ڈالے گا تو سوا کیلو آئے گا۔ کیونکہ گیہوں ہلکے ہوتے ہیں اور بڑے بڑے دانے ہوتے ہیں۔ اور آٹا باریک ہونے کی وجہ سے دب جائے گا اور زیادہ آئے گا۔ تو برتن کے بھرنے کے اعتبار سے برابر ہے لیکن وزن کے اعتبار سے بہت فرق ہوگا ۔ اس لئے مساوات نہیں ہوئی اور دونوں ایک ہی قسم کی چیز اور جنس ہیں اس لئے مساوات اور برابری ضروری تھی اور وہ ہوئی نہیں اس لئے گیہوں کو آٹے کے بدلے یا ستو کے بدلے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بیچنا ہی ہو تو درہم اور پونڈ کے بدلے بیچے (۲) حدیث میں ایسی بیج سے منع فرمایا ہے قال سعد سمعت رسول الله سئل عمن اشترى التمر بالرطب فقال اينقض الرطب اذا يبس فقالوا نعم فهى عن ذلك (الف) (دار قطنی، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۴۴ نمبر ۲۹۷۶ سن للبیھقی ، باب ماجاء فی النھی عن بيع الرطب بالتمرج خاص ص ۲۹۴) اس حدیث میں تر کھجور اور خشک کھجور ایک جنس ہیں لیکن صاع اور برتن میں تر کھجور کم آئے گا اور اسی برتن میں خشک کھجور زیادہ آئے گا۔ اس لئے کیلو کے اعتبار سے مساوات نہیں ہوگی اس لئے آپ نے منع فرمایا۔ بلکہ پوچھا کیا تر کھجور بعد میں کم ہو جائے گا ؟ تو صحابہ نے فرمایا کہ ہاں ! بعد میں کم ہوگا تو آپ نے تر کھجور کو خشک کھجور کے بدلے بیچنے کو منع فرمایا ۔ یہی حال گیہوں اور اس کے آنے کا اور گیہوں اور اس کے ستو کا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن سعید بن مسيب في البر بالدقيق قال هو ربا (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۳۲ فی السویق بالحطة واشباهه من اجازه ج خامس ص ۳۴)
گیہوں کا آٹا ہو اور گیہوں ہی کا ستو ہو تو بھی دونوں کو بیچنا جائز نہیں۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے پوچھا اس آدمی سے جس نے کھجور کوتر کھجور کے بدلے میں خریدا فرمایا کیا تر کھجور کم ہو جاتا ہے جب خشک ہو جاتا ہے؟ لوگوں نے فرمایا
ہاں! پس آپ نے اس بیچ سے روکا ( ب ) حضرت سعید بن مسیب سے گیہوں کو آٹے کے بدلے میں بیچنے کے بارے میں پو چھا تو فرمایا یہ بوا ہے۔
The assembly and other than it that contains riba: specification is considered but hand-to-hand exchange is not considered. It is not permissible to sell wheat with flour nor with sawiq, and similarly flour with sawiq. Chapter of Sarf: We sell gold with silver hand-to-hand... This hadith: 'eye to eye' instead of 'hand to hand' means the thing is specified. So Hanafis apply this hadith to grains and say that in grains only specification is sufficient to avoid debt. And they apply 'hand to hand' to gold and silver. Imam Shafi'i considers possession necessary even in grains to avoid debt. His evidence is the hadith of 'hand to hand', meaning possession is necessary. As for the two precious metals (dirhams and dinars), they are not specified by specification until possession is taken. (2) Grains and commodities become specified by specification. (1942 (11)) And it is not permissible to sell wheat with its flour nor with its sawiq, and similarly selling flour with sawiq. ... The hadith of Sa'd: the Prophet asked about dates with fresh dates, he said: Does the fresh date shrink when it dries? They said yes, so he prohibited. This is the same for wheat and its flour and its sawiq. The effect of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab about wheat with flour: he said it is riba. The footnote explains.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with inter-madhhab dispute. It begins with the general principle that in ribawi items (commodities subject to riba), specification (ta'yin) of the item in the contract is sufficient to avoid debt (i.e., to make the transaction valid), and hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) is not required. However, an exception is made for gold and silver (thaman), which require physical possession. The passage then gives a specific application: selling wheat for its flour or sawiq is not permissible, even if both are measured by volume, because they are the same genus (wheat) but differ in weight when measured in the same container. The Hanafi school argues that for grains, specification alone prevents riba, unlike for silver and gold. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hand-to-hand possession is necessary even in grains, relying on hadiths emphasizing 'yadan bi-yad'. The passage provides proofs: a hadith about dates (fresh vs. dry) showing that inequality in volume/weight violates the condition of equality in same-genus exchanges, and an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab declaring wheat-for-flour trade as riba. The footnote explains the hadith. The passage thus clarifies the Hanafi position and refutes the Shafi'i view.

Key Terms
الربوا (al-ribā): Usury or excessive increase; prohibited in Islamic law.
التعيين (al-ta'yīn): Specification of the item in the contract, identifying it clearly.
التقابض (al-taqābuḍ): Hand-to-hand exchange, physical possession by both parties at the time of contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is selling wheat for its flour prohibited in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because flour is not a ribawi item.
B) Because the two are not of the same genus.
C) Because they differ in weight when measured in the same container, leading to inequality.
D) Because hand-to-hand exchange is not possible.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, for grains, specification alone prevents riba; the prohibition of wheat-for-flour stems from inevitable inequality in volume-weight, not from lack of hand-to-hand exchange.

Ruling on Selling Sawiq with Flour According to the Sahibayn
This passage presents a ruling of the Sahibayn on genus classification for sawiq and flour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the Sahibayn on exchanging sawiq for flour and explain why they are considered different genera.

Core Idea
Sawiq and flour are different genera because their purposes differ, so their exchange is permissible even if weight unequal.

In this lesson, we explore the ruling of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on selling sawiq (roasted barley porridge) in exchange for regular flour. The core issue is whether they are considered the same genus (jins) for ribawi transactions. The Sahibayn hold that despite both being derived from grains, their distinct purposes make them separate genera, thus permitting exchange without weight equality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and the issue
The case is selling sawiq in exchange for flour. The key question is whether they are the same genus (jins) for the purpose of ribawi rules.
2
Determine the genus relationship according to the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn rule that sawiq and flour are two different genera because their intended purposes differ: flour is for bread, sawiq is for drinking after mixing.
Purpose (maqsad) is a criterion for differentiating genera.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule for genus difference
When two items are from different genera, they may be exchanged without requirement of equality in weight or measure, as long as the exchange is not speculative on both sides.
This is a key exception to ribawi rules.
4
State the final ruling
Thus, selling sawiq for flour is permissible (mubah) even if the weights are unequal, according to the Sahibayn.
5
Contrast with the alternative view
If the genus were the same (e.g., wheat flour for wheat sawiq), equality would be required; otherwise the sale would be invalid due to riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ستو بھننے کے بعد ہلکا ہو جاتا ہے وہ برتن میں کم آئے گا اور آٹا بھونا ہوا نہیں ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس میں دباؤ ہوتا ہے اور وزنی ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان دونوں میں بھی مساوات نہیں ہوگی ، اور جنس ایک ہے۔ اس لئے بیع جائز نہیں ہوگی۔ جنس ایک ہو اور وزن میں برابری نہ ہو پاتی ہو تب بھی جائز نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ مثلا بمثل نہیں ہوا۔ و ایک اگر جنس بدل جائے۔ مثلا گیہوں کا آٹا ہو اور جو کے ستو ہو تو جائز ہوگا کیونکہ جنس بدل گئی۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک ستو اور آٹا دو جنس ہیں۔ ایک کا مقصد روٹی پکانا ہے اور دوسرے کا مقصد گھول کر کھانا ہے اس لئے ستو کو آٹے کے بدلے بیچنا جائز ہے۔ الدقيق : آتا۔ السويق : ستور
After roasting, sawiq becomes light, it will come less in the vessel, and flour is not roasted so it has density and weight. Therefore, between these two, there will not be equality, and the genus is one. So the sale is not permissible. If the genus is one and weight equality is not achieved, it is still not permissible because it is not like-for-like. But if the genus changes, for example, wheat flour and barley sawiq, then it is permissible because the genus changed. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), sawiq and flour are two different genera. The purpose of one is to make bread, and the purpose of the other is to drink after mixing. Therefore, selling sawiq in exchange for flour is permissible. Al-daqiq: flour. Al-sawiq: roasted barley porridge.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement presenting the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the permissibility of selling sawiq (roasted barley flour) in exchange for regular flour. The text first explains why selling flour for sawiq when both come from the same grain (e.g., both from wheat) is not permissible: because after roasting, sawiq becomes lighter in weight per volume, leading to inequality. Since they are the same genus, equality is required. However, if the genus differs, such as wheat flour with barley sawiq, it is permissible. Then the Sahibayn distinguish between sawiq and flour even when both are from the same grain: they consider them different genera because their purposes differ (one is for bread, the other for mixing with water as a drink). Therefore, selling sawiq for flour is permissible even with inequality in weight. This ruling shows how the Hanafi school uses differences in purpose (maqsad) to differentiate genera in ribawi transactions.

Key Terms
السويق (al-sawīq): Sawiq: roasted barley or wheat that is ground and eaten mixed with water or milk.
الدقيق (al-daqīq): Flour, finely ground grains used for baking bread.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is selling sawiq (roasted barley flour) in exchange for wheat flour permissible?
A) Because they are equal in weight.
B) Because they are different genera (jins) due to different purposes.
C) Because the Prophet permitted it explicitly.
D) Because they are both from the same grain.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's ruling that sawiq and flour are different genera based on purpose allows their exchange without weight equality, illustrating the Hanafi use of maqsad to define jins in ribawi transactions.

Ruling on Selling Meat for Animals: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling meat for a live animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf from that of Muhammad al-Shaybani on selling meat for a live animal, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Meat and live animals are different genres (weight vs count); hence inequality is allowed per the Shaykhayn.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the permissibility of exchanging cut meat for a live animal. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) deem it permissible unconditionally, while Muhammad al-Shaybani requires the cut meat to exceed the animal's meat. We will analyze their proofs and identify the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed ruling
What exactly is the legal question? Is it permissible to sell cut meat for a live animal with inequality in weight or count?
2
Identify the Shaykhayn's position and their reasoning
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow it even with inequality because meat is weighed and animals are counted, making them different genres (jins).
3
Identify Muhammad al-Shaybani's position and his evidence
Muhammad requires equality unless the cut meat is more, relying on the hadith prohibiting selling meat for an animal, implying same genus.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith
The Shaykhayn interpret the prohibition as relating to riba when both are the same genre, but here genres differ, so it is allowed.
5
Determine the relied-upon position
The view of the Shaykhayn is the mufta bihi, as it is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and considered stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز بيع اللحم بالحيوان عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى وقال محمد لا يجوز الا على وجه الاعتبار حتى يكون اللحم اكثر مما في الحيوان فيكون اللحم بمثل والزيادة بالسقط.
جائز ہے گوشت کی بیچ حیوان کے بدلے امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اور فرمایا امام محمد نے نہیں ضائز ہے مگر اس اعتبار سے کہ گوشت زیادہ ہو اس سے جو حیوان میں ہے تو گوشت گوشت کے بدلے میں اور زیادہ سقط کے بدلے میں۔ مثلا گائے کا گوشت ہو اور زندہ گائے کے بدلے میں بیچنا چاہتا ہے تو شیخین کے نزدیک جائز ہے چاہے گائے میں گوشت ساٹھ کیلو ہو اور کٹا ہوا گوشت نہیں کیلو ہو۔
گوشت وزنی ہے اس کو وزن سے ناپتے ہیں اور گائے عددی ہے اس کو وزن سے نہیں ناپتے ہیں بلکہ عدد سے بیچتے ہیں ۔ تو یہ دو جنس ہوئے ایک جنس نہیں ہوئے اس لئے کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے۔ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ جو کٹا ہوا گوشت ہے وہ اس گوشت سے زیادہ ہونا چاہئے جو زندہ گائے میں ہے تب بیچنا جائز ہوگا۔ مثلا زندہ گائے میں گوشت ساٹھ کیلو ہے تو کٹا ہوا گوشت ستر کیلو ہونا چاہئے ۔ تاکہ ساتھ کیلو ساٹھ کیلو کے برابر ہو جائے اور دس کیلو کٹا ہوا گوشت گائے کی کلیجی، گردہ اور سقط کے بدلے ہو جائے۔
وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ گائے کا کٹا ہوا گوشت اور زندہ گائے دونوں ایک جنس ہیں اس لئے مساوات اور برابری ضروری ہے (۲) ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن سهل بن سعيد قال نهى رسول الله لا ل ل له عن بيع اللحم بالحيوان (الف)(دارقطني ، كتاب البيوع ج ثالث ص ۵۹ نمبر ۳۰۳۷ سفن سیھتی ، باب بيع اللحم بالحيوان، ج خامس، ص ۲۸۳، نمبر ۱۰۵۶۹) اس حدیث میں گوشت کو حیوان کے بدلے میں بیچنے سے منع فرمایا گیا ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہی ہے کہ دونوں ایک جنس ہیں۔ تاہم گوشت زیادہ ہو اور مساوات کا اعتبار کریں تو جائز ہوجائیگی۔ السقط : ناکارہ چیز جیسے ہڈی اور سینگ وغیرہ۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے روکا گوشت کو حیوان کے بدلے بیچنے ہے۔
It is permissible to sell meat for an animal according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them). And Muhammad said: It is not permissible except by consideration, such that the meat is more than what is in the animal, so the (equal) meat is (exchanged) for the (equal) meat and the increase is for the waste. It is permissible to sell meat in exchange for an animal according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf. And Imam Muhammad said: It is not permissible except by consideration that the meat is more than what is in the animal, then the meat is (exchanged) for the meat and the excess is for the waste. For example, cow meat and a live cow: according to the two shaykhs it is permissible even if the cow has 60 kg of meat and the cut meat is not 60 kg. Meat is weighed, the cow is counted. So they are two different genera, not one genus, so selling with excess or deficit is permissible. Imam Muhammad says: The cut meat must be more than the meat in the live animal; then it becomes permissible. For example, if the live cow has 60 kg of meat, the cut meat should be 70 kg so that 60 kg equals 60 kg and 10 kg of cut meat is for the liver, kidneys, and waste. He says: The cut meat and the live cow are one genus, so equality is necessary. His evidence is the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited selling meat for an animal. In this hadith, selling meat for an animal is prohibited because both are one genus. However, if the meat is more and equality is considered, it becomes permissible. Al-saqat: useless things like bones and horns. Footnote: The Prophet prohibited selling meat for an animal.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the permissibility of selling meat for a live animal. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) consider it permissible even with inequality in weight, because meat is weighed (weight-based) while a live animal is counted (count-based), making them different genres. Thus, they do not require equality. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees: he considers both to be the same genus (meat from the animal) and requires equality. However, he allows it only if the cut meat exceeds the estimated meat in the live animal, so that the equal portion is for the meat and the excess is for the inedible parts (saqat). His evidence is the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd prohibiting selling meat for an animal. The passage explains that according to Muhammad, the prohibition is because they are the same genus, but if the meat is more, the ruling is relaxed. The two shaykhs rely on the difference in measurement method. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the two shaykhs.

Key Terms
اللحم (al-laḥm): Meat, especially cut meat that is sold by weight.
الحيوان (al-ḥayawān): Live animal, sold by count (not by weight).
السقط (al-saqṭ): Useless or inedible parts of an animal, such as bones, horns, liver, kidneys (in this context).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which position is most relied upon (mufta bihi) regarding selling meat for a live animal?
A) It is not permissible under any condition.
B) It is permissible only if the meat is more than the animal's meat.
C) It is permissible even with inequality, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
D) It is permissible only if both are equal in weight.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position allows selling meat for a live animal even with inequality because they are different genres due to measurement.

Selling Fresh Dates for Dried Dates: The Shrinkage Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on a riba-related sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa permits selling fresh dates for dried dates and evaluate the opposing view of the Sahibayn and Shafi'i based on the hadith and the principle of riba al-fadl.

Core Idea
Equal volume now does not guarantee equality later; future shrinkage violates like-for-like.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute about exchanging fresh dates for dried dates. At the heart is the principle of riba al-fadl: any exchange of same-genus ribawi goods must be equal in quantity at the time of contract. Abu Hanifa permits the sale if the initial volume is equal, but his students (the Sahibayn) and Imam al-Shafi'i object because fresh dates inevitably shrink when drying, leading to future inequality. We will explore each side's proof, the hadith cited, and the practical consequence for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: selling fresh dates (rutb) for dried dates (tamr) is permissible provided they are exchanged like-for-like by volume at the time of contract.
Abu Hanifa considers only immediate equality; future changes are irrelevant to contract validity.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that such a sale is not permissible. They argue that fresh dates shrink when dried, so equal volume now becomes unequal later, violating the condition of like-for-like.
This dispute exists within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa vs. his two leading students.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith cited by the Sahibayn: the Prophet asked 'Does fresh dates shrink when dried?' and upon hearing yes, forbade the sale. This directly addresses the issue of future inequality.
The hadith is narrated by Sa'd and recorded in Sunan Darqutni and Bayhaqi.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa interprets the hadith as a recommendation (not a binding prohibition) and argues that the contract is based on spot exchange; future shrinkage does not nullify the validity. He relies on the principle that riba is only triggered at the time of contract.
The Hanafi response also notes that if two different genera are considered, disparity is allowed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the sale is valid and binding. Under the Sahibayn and Shafi'i, the sale is invalid and the transaction must be unwound. The mufta bihi in later Hanafi fatwa is the prohibition to avoid riba.
Practically, one should avoid such exchanges or use a medium of currency.

Source Text
