ويجوز بيع الرطب بالتمر مثلا بمثل عند ابي حنيفة وكذلك العنب بالزبيب
جائز ہے تر کھجور کی بیع خشک کھجور کے بدلے برابر سرا بر امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور ایسے ہی انگور کی بیع کشمش کے بدلے۔ اتر کھجور کو خشک کے بدلے بیچنا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ دونوں کو صاع کے اعتبار سے برابر سرا بر نیچے۔ دونوں ہی کھجور ہیں اس لئے ایک جنس ہیں۔ اس لئے برتن میں بھر کر دونوں کو برابر کر کے بیچے تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ حدیث گزر چکی ہے مثلا بمثل ۔ اسی طرح انگور اور اس سے خشک ہو کر کشمش ایک ہی جنس ہیں اس لئے دونوں کو برتن میں بھر کر برابر کر دے اور نیچے تو جائز ہے۔ اور اگر دو جنس مان لیں تو کمی بیشی کر کے بھی بیچنا جائز ہوگا۔
ا صاحبین اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تر کھجور کو خشک کے بدلے بیچنا جائز نہیں۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں کی جنس ایک ہے اور برتن میں بھر کر بیچیں گے تو ابھی تو دونوں برابر ہو جائیں گے لیکن بعد میں تر کھجور خشک ہوگا تو اس کی مقدار کم ہو جائے گی تو بعد میں مساوات باقی نہیں رہے گی۔ اس لئے یہ مثلا مثل نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے تر کھجور کو خشک کھجور کے بدلے بیچنا جائز نہیں (۲) حدیث میں بھی منع فرمایا۔ وقال سعد سمعت رسول الله سئل عمن اشترى التمر بالرطب فقال اينقض الرطب اذا يس؟ فقالوا نعم فنهى عن ذلك (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۴۴ نمبر ۲۹۷۶ رسنن ابیھقی ، باب ما جاء في النھی عن بيع الرطب بالتمر ، ج خامس جس ۴۸۰، نمبر ۱۰۵۵۶) اس حدیث میں آپ نے پوچھا کہ کہ کیا تر کھجور خشک ہونے کے بعد کم ہو جاتا ہے؟ تو لوگوں نے کہا ہاں ! پس آپ نے تر کھجور کو خشک کھجور کے بدلے بیچنے سے منع فرمایا۔ اس لئے صاحبین اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک تر کھجور کو خشک کھجور کے بدلے بیچنا ممنوع ہے۔ الرطب : ترکھجور - العنب : انگور - الزبيب : کشمش ،سوکھے ہوئے انگور کوکشمش کہتے ہیں۔
It is permissible to sell fresh dates for dried dates like for like according to Abu Hanifa, and similarly grapes for raisins.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on exchanging fresh dates (rutb) for dried dates (tamr) and grapes (inab) for raisins (zabib). Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible provided the exchange is equal by volume (sa'a), because both are the same genus (dates are dates, grapes are grapes). He considers that at the time of exchange, equality is met, even though later the fresh will dry and shrink. The two teachers (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam Shafi'i disagree, arguing that since fresh dates shrink upon drying, equal volume now leads to inequality later, violating the principle of like-for-like (mithmil bi mithlin). They cite a hadith where the Prophet asked: 'Does fresh dates shrink when dried?' People said yes, so he forbade the sale. Thus, according to them, the sale is not permissible. The Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa) is that the sale is valid because the contract is based on immediate exchange; future shrinkage is not considered. However, the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school is actually from the students (Sahibayn) due to the hadith, unless the condition of immediate equality is ensured by weight. The text notes that if one considers them different genres, then inequality is allowed. The practical fatwa today is caution.

Key Terms
الرطب (al-rutb): Fresh, moist dates
التمر (al-tamr): Dried dates
مثلا بمثل (mithmil bi mithlin): Like for like in quantity (volume or weight)
العنب (al-'inab): Grapes
الزبيب (al-zabib): Raisins, dried grapes

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i prohibit selling fresh dates for dried dates?
A) Because fresh and dried dates are considered different genera in the Hanafi school.
B) Because fresh dates shrink when dried, causing future inequality even if the volumes are equal at the time of contract.
C) Because the Prophet never sold dates, so the ruling is based on later consensus.
D) Because the hadith about like-for-like does not apply to dried fruits.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position prohibits selling fresh dates for dried dates by volume due to future shrinkage, aligning with the hadith and the majority of scholars.

Selling Olives for Olive Oil and Sesame for Sesame Oil
Ruling with condition on selling fruit for its oil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for selling fruit for its extracted oil and apply the qiyas on same-genus exchange to avoid riba.

Core Idea
Exchange of fruit for its oil is like exchanging same genus with excess; the oil content must match.

This lesson addresses a nuanced area of sales law: exchanging olives for olive oil or sesame seeds for sesame oil. Since the oil is the valuable component, the Hanafi school treats the fruit and its oil as the same genus (jins) for riba purposes. The key ruling is that the exchange is permissible only if the extracted oil exceeds the oil contained in the fruit, so that the oil equivalent can be matched and the remaining oil compensates for the leftover solids (pulp/cake). The example clarifies how this condition ensures equality in the oil element.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and ruling
The transaction is selling olives/sesame in exchange for their respective oils. The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz) unless a condition is met.
2
Understand the condition
The extracted oil must be greater (akthar) than the oil inside the fruit. This ensures that the oil component of both sides is balanced.
Equality in oil avoids riba al-fadl.
3
Grasp the reasoning (ta'lil)
The oil is the effective cause (illa) for riba; the fruit is considered to contain oil. So the exchange is like exchanging oil for oil with excess, which is only allowed if the excess has a countervalue (the leftover solids).
This is qiyas: the ruling for oil-to-oil exchange is applied to fruit-to-oil exchange.
4
Apply the numerical example
Example: 2 kg oil for 6 kg olives (which contain 1.5 kg oil) is valid because 1.5 kg oil matches the oil in olives, and the extra 0.5 kg oil pays for the olive cake.
If extracted oil were less, the sale would be invalid due to inequality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز بيع الزيتون بالزيت والسمسم بالشيرج حتى يكون
نہیں جائز ہے زیتون کی بیع زیتون کے تیل کے ساتھ اور تل کی بیع تل کے تیل کے ساتھ یہاں تک کہ زیتون کا تیل اور تل کا تیل زیادہ ہو اس سے جو زیتون اور تل میں ہے۔ تاکہ تیل اس کے مثل کے بدلے ہو جائے اور زیادہ تیل کھلی کے بدلے میں ہو جائے۔ مثلا دو کیلوزیتون کا خالص تیل ہے اس کو چھ کیلوزیون پھل کے بدلے میں بیچنا چاہتا ہے۔ اور چھ کیلوز میتون میں ڈیڑھ کیلوتیل موجود ہے تو بیع جائز ہوگی۔ کیونکہ نکالا ہوا ڈیڑھ کیلوتیل اس تیل کے برابر ہو جائے گا جو زیتون کے پھل میں ڈیڑھ کیلو تیل ہے۔ اور باقی آدھا کیلو تیل زیتون کی کھلی کے مقابلے میں ہو جائے گا۔ اس طرح ڈیڑھ کیلو تیل ڈیرھ کیلو تیل کے مقابلے میں ہو گیا اور ایک جنس ہونے کی وجہ سے مساوات اور برابری ہو گئی اس لئے جائز ہو گیا۔ اور اگر زیتون کے پھل میں جتنا تیل ہے، نکالا ہوا تیل اس سے کم ہو تو بیع جائز نہیں ہوگی۔
It is not permissible to sell olives for oil and sesame for sesame oil until the oil (ez-zeyt and esh-shiraj) is more than what is in the olives and sesame.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage rules on selling fruit (olives, sesame seeds) in exchange for their extracted oil. Since the oil is the valuable part of the fruit, the two are considered the same genus (oil). Therefore, to avoid riba al-fadl, the exchange must be equal in the oil content. The condition stated is that the extracted oil must be greater than the oil contained in the fruit so that the equivalent oil matches and the excess is for the remaining solids (pulp, cake). The example given: If one has 2 kg of olive oil and sells it for 6 kg of whole olives, and the 6 kg of olives contain 1.5 kg of oil, then the sale is valid because the 2 kg oil includes 1.5 kg equivalent and 0.5 kg excess goes for the olive cake. If the extracted oil is less, it's invalid. The ruling is based on qiyas: Oil is the effective cause (illa) for riba, so equality must be maintained in oil, not in the whole fruit.

Key Terms
الزيتون (al-zaytun): Olive fruit
الزيت (al-zayt): Olive oil extracted from olives
الشيرج (al-shiraj): Sesame oil
السقط (al-saqt): Leftover solids (pulp, oil cake)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for the sale of olives for olive oil to be valid?
A) The amount of oil must be exactly equal to the oil in the olives.
B) The extracted oil must be greater than the oil in the olives.
C) The olives must be weighed not counted.
D) The exchange must be done immediately.

Key Takeaway
The sale of fruit for its oil is permissible only when the extracted oil exceeds the oil content of the fruit, ensuring riba-free equivalence.

Selling Olives for Olive Oil: The Condition of Excess to Avoid Riba
Ruling on selling olives for olive oil with condition of excess oil, with qiyas to hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling olives for olive oil, apply the condition of excess oil, and explain the qiyas to the hadith on selling meat for an animal.

Core Idea
Selling fruit for its oil is prohibited unless the oil exceeds the fruit's oil content to avoid riba.

The Hanafi school treats olive oil and olives as the same genus (jins) because the oil originates from the fruit. Exchanging them directly risks riba al-fadl unless the oil portion is equal. However, the fruit also contains pulp (shajir), a different substance, which allows the excess oil to be compensated by the pulp. This lesson unpacks the condition and the qiyas proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
State the initial prohibition of selling olives for olive oil and the condition that makes it permissible.
The passage says: 'It is not permissible... until the oil exceeds what is in the fruit.'
2
Understand the rational condition
Why must the oil offered exceed the oil in the fruit? To ensure the oil portion is exchanged like for like, and the excess corresponds to the pulp (a different substance).
The pulp (shajir) is considered a different genus, so the excess oil can be traded for it without riba.
3
Work through the example
Apply the condition to the numerical example: 2 kg oil for 6 kg olives containing 1.5 kg oil. See how the oil portion (1.5 kg) is equal and the extra 0.5 kg is for the pulp.
This demonstrates the mechanics of the condition.
4
Trace the qiyas proof
The hadith forbids selling meat for a live animal because they are the same genus. By qiyas, oil and olives are also same genus, so the same prohibition applies unless the oil portion is equal and excess is for a different component.
The illa (effective cause) is jins (same genus) and one being part of the other.
5
Conclude with the thamarah
The practical consequence: such a sale is permissible only with the excess condition. Without it, the transaction is invalid due to riba.
This ruling applies to both olives and sesame.

And it is not permissible to sell olives for olive oil, and sesame for sesame oil, unless the oil (zayt) and sesame oil (shiraj) exceed what is in the olives and sesame, so that the oil (fat) is for its like and the excess is for the pulp (shajir). [Urdu: And it is not permissible to sell olives for olive oil and sesame for sesame oil, until the olive oil and sesame oil are more than what is in the olives and sesame. So that the oil exchanges for its like, and the excess oil is in exchange for the pulp. For example: he has two kg of pure olive oil and wants to sell it for six kg of olives. In six kg of olives, there is one and a half kg of oil. Then the sale is permissible, because the one and a half kg of extracted oil equals the one and a half kg of oil in the olive fruit, and the remaining half kg of oil is in exchange for the olive pulp. Thus one and a half kg of oil equals one and a half kg of oil, and due to being same genus, equality is achieved, so it is permissible. If the extracted oil is less than the oil in the fruit, the sale is not permissible. It is approximately one genus, so without equality it is not permissible. (2) There is a reference in the hadith. From Sahl ibn Sa'd: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade the sale of meat for an animal. (al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi) In this hadith, he forbade selling meat for an animal because both are the same genus. Similarly, olive oil and olive fruit are the same genus, so it is not permissible unless the oil exceeds the oil inside the olives. If they are one genus, the commodity and price must be equal, otherwise it becomes riba.]
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on selling olives for olive oil and sesame for sesame oil. The passage type is a ruling with proof (qiyas). The ruling: such a sale is not permissible unless the quantity of oil offered exceeds the oil content naturally present in the fruit being exchanged. The reasoning: oil and the fruit are of the same genus (jins) because the oil is extracted from the fruit. Therefore, the exchange must be like for like (مثلا بمثل) for the oil portion to avoid riba. However, because the fruit also contains pulp (shajir ), which is a different substance, the excess oil can be considered in exchange for the pulp. The commentary provides an example: if someone has 2 kg of pure olive oil and wants to exchange it for 6 kg of olives, and the 6 kg of olives contain 1.5 kg of oil, then the sale is permissible if the amount of oil offered is 1.5 kg (equal to the oil in the fruit) and the remaining 0.5 kg of oil is considered in exchange for the fruit's pulp. The condition is that the quantity of oil offered must be more than the estimated oil content of the fruit; otherwise, the sale is invalid. The commentary also cites the hadith forbidding the sale of meat for a live animal, drawing an analogy: just as meat and the animal are of the same genus (so the sale is not permissible unless equality is observed or excess is for other parts), similarly oil and the fruit are of the same genus. The key principle: when two items are of one genus and one is a derivative of the other, exchange must be equal unless an excess corresponds to a different component.

Key Terms
الزيت (al-zayt): Olive oil, extracted from olives.
الشيرج (al-shīraj): Sesame oil, extracted from sesame seeds.
الشجير (al-shajīr): The pulp or residue of olives/sesame after oil extraction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the sale of olives for olive oil become permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) When both are measured by weight equally.
B) When the quantity of oil offered is greater than the estimated oil content of the olives.
C) When the exchange is hand to hand without any condition.
D) When the olives are crushed and the oil is not yet extracted.

Key Takeaway
Selling olives for olive oil is permissible only if the oil offered exceeds the oil in the fruit; the excess oil is considered in exchange for the pulp, achieving like-for-like for the oil portion.

Selling Different Meats with Disparity
Ruling on selling different meats with disparity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling different meats with disparity and identify the condition that permits disparity.

Core Idea
Different meats are different genera, so selling one for another with disparity is permissible.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental principle of Hanafi sales law: the exchange of different genera (ajnas). The rule is simple: when two items are from the same genus, equality is required to avoid riba al-fadl; but when they differ, disparity is allowed. The passage presents a ruling and a proof from the practice of Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being sold? Different types of meat (e.g., goat for cow). The ruling: it is permissible (jāʾiz) to sell with disparity.
2
Understand the rationale
Different animals are considered different genera. Goat and cow are separate, so riba rules requiring equality do not apply.
If same genus (e.g., goat for goat), equality would be required.
3
Examine the proof
An athar from Imam Malik permits selling fish meat for camel, cow, or goat meat with disparity.
This shows permissibility across different meat types.
4
Note the condition
The exchange must be spot (hand to hand). Deferred payment invalidates the transaction.
This is because both are weight-based ribawi items, and delay introduces riba al-nasi'ah.
5
Determine the exception
If meats are from the same genus (e.g., goat for goat), equality is required; disparity is prohibited.
This follows the general rule of riba al-fadl.

[۱۹۴۶ (۱۵) ويجوز بيع اللحمان المختلفة بعضها ببعض متفاضلا [۱۹۴۶ (۱۵) جائز ہے بیع مختلف گوشت کی بعض کو بعض کے ساتھ کمی بیشی کر کے۔ مثلا بکری کا گوشت گائے کے گوشت کے بدلے بیچے تو کمی بیشی کر کے بیچنا بھی جائز ہے۔ (1) بکری الگ جنس ہے اور گائے الگ جنس ہے۔ اور بکری کا گوشت بکری کی جنس سے ہوگا اسی طرح گائے کا گوشت گائے کی جنس سے اور اور کا کی ہوگا۔ اس لئے بکری کا گوشت گائے کے گوشت کے ساتھ کمی بیشی کر کے بیچنا جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دو الگ الگ جنس ہوئے (۲) اثر میں ہے قال مالك ولا بأس بلحم الحيتان بلحم الابل والبقر والغنم وما أشبه ذلك من الوحوش كلها اثنين بواحد واكثر من ذلك يدا بيد فان دخل في ذلك الاجل فلا خير فيه (ب) (موطا امام مالک، باب پیج اللحم بالهم ص ۵۹۳ ) اس اثر میں مچھلی کے گوشت کو بکری گائے کے گوشت کے ساتھ کمی بیشی کر کے بیچنا جائز قرار دیا بشرطیکہ نقد ہو ادھار نہ ہو اس لئے کہ دونوں وزنی ہیں۔ مختلف جنس ہوں تو کمی بیشی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے۔
And it is permissible to sell different meats, some for others, with disparity. [Urdu: It is permissible to sell different meats, some for others, with excess and deficiency. For example, if one sells goat meat for cow meat, selling with disparity is permissible. (1) Goat is a separate genus and cow is a separate genus. Goat meat belongs to the genus of goat, and cow meat belongs to the genus of cow. Therefore, selling goat meat for cow meat with disparity is permissible because they are two separate genera. (2) There is an athar: Malik said, 'There is no harm in selling fish meat for the meat of camels, cows, goats, and similar wild animals, two for one or more, hand to hand; if a term enters, then there is no good in it.' (Muwatta Imam Malik, Bab Bay' al-Lahm bil-Lahm, p. 593) In this athar, selling fish meat for goat and cow meat with disparity is declared permissible provided it is spot, not deferred, because both are weight-based items. If they are different genera, selling with disparity is permissible.]
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on selling different types of meat for one another. The passage type is a ruling with proof from the practice of Imam Malik (athar). The ruling: it is permissible to sell different meats with disparity in quantity (i.e., one can give more or less meat of one type for another). The reason is that different animals are considered different genera (ajnas). Goat meat and cow meat are separate genera, so the prohibition of riba (which requires equality for same genus) does not apply. The commentary cites a statement from Imam Malik in the Muwatta, where he permits selling fish meat for camel, cow, or goat meat, even two for one, provided the transaction is spot (hand to hand). This is because both are weighable items but of different genera. The key principle: when items are of different genera, disparity (tafadul) is allowed as long as the exchange is immediate (not deferred). The same principle applies to all meat types. The commentary adds that if the same genus (e.g., two types of goat meat) were exchanged, equality would be required.

Key Terms
اللحمان المختلفة (al-luḥūm al-mukhtalifah): Different types of meat from different animals.
متفاضلا (mutafāḍilan): With disparity, i.e., unequal quantities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling goat meat for cow meat with disparity (e.g., 2 kg goat for 1 kg cow) permissible?
A) Because both are same genus, but the hadith allows it.
B) Because goat and cow are different genera, so riba rules do not apply.
C) Because it is a spot transaction.
D) Because meat is not a ribawi item.

Key Takeaway
The sale of different meats with disparity is permissible provided the exchange is spot, because they are considered different genera.

Selling Milk of Different Animals with Disparity
Ruling on selling milk of different animals with disparity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on selling milk from different animals with disparity and explain why the genus of the animal is decisive.

Core Idea
Milk takes the genus of its animal — selling different milks with disparity is permissible.

This lesson addresses a specific application of the riba rules in exchange transactions. While exchanging like-for-like goods must be equal and spot, the Hanafi school distinguishes between genera. Milk is not a single genus; it follows the animal it comes from. Thus, camel milk and goat milk are different genera, allowing unequal exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction type
This is a sale (بيع) of two commodities that are ribawi (subject to riba rules). The commodities are milk from different animals. Determine the ruling for exchanging them with disparity (mutafāḍil).
Riba rules apply to same genus items measured by weight or volume.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The passage states it is permissible (jāʾiz) to sell camel milk for goat milk with disparity. The key condition is that the animals are different species.
This is an exception to the general rule for same-genus items.
3
Explain the rationale (ʿilla)
The ʿilla is that milk takes the genus (jins) of the animal. Since camel and goat are different genera, the milks are different genera, so the prohibition of disparity (tafāḍul) does not apply.
This is based on qiyas: like meat from different animals is different, milk is considered similar.
4
Confirm the requirement: spot exchange (yadan bi yad)
Even with different genera, the exchange must be hand-to-hand (spot). The hadith '…hand to hand' is referenced. So delay would be riba.
This is a general condition for all spot exchanges of ribawi items.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Camel's milk is of the genus of camel, so selling it for goat's milk with disparity is permissible, because goat's milk is of the genus of goat and separate from camel's milk. Therefore it is permissible. The athar of Imam Malik has passed, and the hadith has also passed: 'And sell barley for dates however you wish, hand to hand.' (Tirmidhi, Bab al-Buyu')]

Commentary
This passage extends the principle to milk. The passage type is a ruling statement supported by analogy to meat. The ruling: selling milk from different animals (camel, cow, goat) with disparity in quantity is permissible. The reason is that milk takes the genus of the animal it comes from. Therefore, camel milk and goat milk are different genera, so the riba restriction does not apply. The commentary references the earlier athar from Imam Malik and a hadith about selling barley for dates hand to hand, which is a general principle for different genera. The key takeaway: as long as the animals are of different species, their milk is considered different genera, allowing unequal exchange spot.

Key Terms
الالبان (al-albān): Milks from different animals.
متفاضل (mutafāḍil): With disparity, unequal.

Selling Oil for its Fruit: Same Genus and Riba al-Fadl
Ruling on exchange of oil for its source fruit with same genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of jins (same genus) to the exchange of oil for its source fruit and identify when riba al-fadl occurs.

Core Idea
Oil and its fruit are the same genus; disparity in exchange is riba al-fadl.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on the exchange of oil (olive or sesame) for the fruit it is extracted from. The passage uses a hadith on meat-for-animal as proof by analogy. We will work through the legal reasoning and its practical application to ensure riba-free transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is exchanging oil (olive or sesame) for its source fruit (olives or sesame). The Hanafi ruling: it is haram unless the exchange is equal in weight, because they belong to the same genus (jins).
Same genus means the underlying substance is identical in essence, even if form differs.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites a hadith from Sahl ibn Sa'd: the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of meat for a live animal. This hadith is used as proof that two items of the same genus cannot be exchanged with disparity.
The hadith is narrated by Dar Qutni and Bayhaqi; it is ahad in transmission.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The prohibition in the hadith is based on the fact that meat and animal are the same genus. By analogy (qiyas), oil (olive/sesame) and its fruit (olives/sesame) are also the same genus. Therefore, any disparity leads to riba al-fadl.
The illa (effective cause) is the identity of genus (jins).
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Other schools may consider oil and fruit as different genera (e.g., based on transformation), allowing disparity. The Hanafi school, however, treats them as same genus because the essence remains unchanged.
This ikhtilaf stems from differing definitions of 'jins' in riba.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school. The proof from the hadith is considered strong, and the analogy is consistent with the principle that riba applies to weighed/measured items of the same genus.
No explicit tarjih authority cited, but it aligns with Zahir al-Riwayah.

الزيت والشيرج اكثر مما في الزيتون والسمسم فيكون الدهن بمثله والزيادة بالشجير [ ۱۹۴۶ (۱۵)
تقریبا ایک جنس ہے اس لئے مثلا بمثل کے بغیر جائز نہیں (۲) حدیث میں اشارہ موجود ہے۔ عن سهل بن سعيد قال نھی رسول الله الا الله عن بيع اللحم بالحيوان (الف) ( دار قطنی، کتاب البیوع ص ۵۹ نمبر ۳۰۳۷ سفن البیھقی ، باب ربیع اللهم بالحيوان ، ج خامس ص ۲۴۸۳، نمبر ۱۰۵۶۹) اس حدیث میں گوشت کے حیوان کے بدلے بیچنے سے منع فرمایا۔ کیونکہ دونوں ایک ہی جنس ہیں۔ اسی طرح زیتون کا تیل اور زیتون کا پھل ایک ہی جنس ہیں اس لئے جائز نہیں جب تک کہ تیل زیتون کے اندر کے تیل سے زیادہ نہ ہو۔

Oil and sesame oil are more than what is in the olive and sesame, so the fat/oil is equal to it and the increase is by the shajir. [1946] (15) It is approximately one genus, so it is not permissible without like-for-like. (2) There is an indication in the hadith: from Sahl ibn Sa'd said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of meat for an animal. This hadith prohibits selling meat for an animal, because both are the same genus. Similarly, olive oil and the fruit of the olive are the same genus, so it is not permissible unless the oil is greater than the oil inside the olives. If they are one genus, the goods and price must be equal, otherwise it becomes riba. Definitions: الزيت: olive oil, السمسم: sesame, الشيرج: sesame oil, الدهن: oil, الشجير: [unclear].
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on exchanging oil (from olives or sesame) for the fruit itself (olives or sesame) when the oil content of the extracted oil exceeds that naturally present in the fruit. The legal classification: it is not permissible unless the exchange is equal in weight because they are the same genus (jins). The proof is a hadith forbidding the sale of meat for a live animal, analogized to oil for its source fruit. The commentary clarifies that if two items are the same genus, any disparity leads to riba al-fadl. Thus, the ruling: such exchange is prohibited unless equal (mithl bi mithl).

Key Terms
الزيت (az-zayt): Olive oil in this context
الشيرج (ash-shiraj): Sesame oil; a type of oil from sesame seeds
الدهن (ad-duhn): Oil or fat generally; here refers to the oil being exchanged
الشجير (ash-shajir): Unclear; possibly a corrupt word for the pressed residue (oil cake) or pulp
ربوا (riba): Usury; in this context, riba al-fadl (disparity in exchange of same genus)

C) Permissible only if the exchange is deferred.

Key Takeaway
Oil and its source fruit are the same genus in Hanafi law; exchange must be equal in weight/measure to avoid riba al-fadl.

Selling Different Meats and Milks with Disparity
Ruling on exchange of different meats and milks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging different types of meat or milk with disparity and explain the genus-based reasoning using the proof from the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd.

Core Idea
Different genera allow disparity; same genus requires equality.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari addresses a key question in riba law: can you exchange two items that are of the same type but from different sources? The Hanafi school answers by looking at the genus (jins) of the item, determined by its essence. The ruling permits exchanging different meats (e.g., goat for beef) or different milks (e.g., camel for goat) with disparity, provided the transaction is spot (hand-to-hand).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that selling different meats with disparity is permissible. Also, selling different milks (camel, cow, goat) with disparity is permissible. Identify that the hukm is ja'iz (permissible).
The ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the genus principle
The permissibility hinges on whether the items are from the same genus (jins) or different. Hanafis determine genus by essence (māhiyya) — e.g., goat and cattle are different genera, so goat meat and beef are different genera.
If same genus, disparity triggers riba al-fadl.
3
Examine the proof
The author cites a hadith from Sahl ibn Sa'd forbidding selling meat for a live animal — both are from the same genus. Conversely, the hadith 'Sell barley for dates as you wish' shows that different genera allow disparity.
Also the athar of Imam Malik permitting fish meat for other meats with disparity.
4
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i considers all meats as one genus because they all share the name 'meat'. Hanafis differentiate by source animal. This difference leads to different rulings in practice.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice: selling 1 kg of goat meat for 2 kg of beef spot is valid. Selling 1 liter of cow milk for 2 liters of goat milk spot is valid. But selling 1 kg of beef for 2 kg of beef from a different cut would require equality.
The transaction must be spot (hand-to-hand); credit invalidates.

And it is permissible to sell different meats, some with others, with disparity. [947] (16) And likewise, the milks of camels, cows, and goats, some with others, with disparity. Approximately one genus, so not permissible without like-for-like... [repeated text]... (1946) (15) It is permissible to sell different meats, some with others, with disparity. For example, goat meat for beef, it is permissible with disparity. (1) Goat is a different genus and cow is a different genus. Therefore, goat meat is from the genus of goat, similarly beef from the genus of cow. So selling goat meat for beef with disparity is permissible because they are two different genera. (2) There is an athar: Malik said, 'There is no harm in selling fish meat for camel, cow, goat meat, or similar from wild animals, two for one or more, hand to hand; if credit enters, then no good in it.' This athar allows selling fish meat for goat/beef with disparity provided it is spot cash, because both are weighed and different genera. (947) (16) Similarly, camel milk, cow milk, and goat milk, some with others, with disparity, is permissible. Camel milk is from the genus of camel, so selling it for goat milk with disparity is permissible because goat milk is from the genus of goat and separate from camel milk. The athar of Imam Malik has passed, and the hadith has passed: 'And sell barley for dates as you wish, hand to hand.'
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage rules on the permissibility of selling different types of meat (e.g., goat and beef) or different milks (e.g., camel and goat) with disparity (tafadul). The key principle: items of different genera (jins) can be exchanged with disparity, while items of the same genus require equality. The proof includes a hadith forbidding meat for animal (same genus) and an athar from Imam Malik allowing fish meat for other meats with disparity because they are different genera. For milks, the same logic applies: camel milk is a different genus from goat milk, so disparity is allowed. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is for spot transactions (yadan bi-yad); credit invalidates the transaction.

Key Terms
اللحمان (al-luhman): Meats (plural of lahm); different types of meat
الالبان (al-alban): Milks (plural of laban); different types of milk
متفاضلا (mutafadilan): With disparity; one item may be more or less than the other
جنس (jins): Genus; the legal category for riba determination

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it permissible to sell 1 kg of goat meat for 2 kg of beef spot?
A) No, because all meats are same genus
B) Yes, because goat and beef are different genera
C) No, unless equal in weight
D) Yes, only if goat meat is more than beef

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits exchanging different meats or milks with disparity if they are from different genera, based on the principle that genus is determined by the source animal, not the generic name.

Selling Vinegar of Dates for Grape Vinegar
Ruling on exchange of date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging date vinegar for grape vinegar and explain the principle of genus (jins) in riba transactions.

Core Idea
Date and grape vinegars are different genera; disparity is permissible even though both are called vinegar.

This passage addresses a specific transaction within the broader prohibitions of riba al-fadl. The key principle is that genus (jins) is determined by the source of the vinegar, not its final name or characteristics. Understanding this ruling clarifies when disparity between two vinegars is allowed.

The ruling is that disparity is permissible.

The passage states they are different genera because they come from different fruit sources.

Same genus would prohibit disparity under riba al-fadl.

Selling Bread for Wheat or Flour: Why Disparity is Allowed
Ruling on exchange of bread for wheat or flour with disparity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging bread for wheat or flour with disparity and explain the rationale based on genus classification.

Core Idea
Bread and wheat are different genera in Hanafi law, so disparity in exchange is allowed.

This lesson deals with a common transaction: exchanging bread (baked) for wheat or flour. Although bread is made from wheat, Hanafi fiqh treats them as separate types of property because of differences in how they are measured and consumed. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the concept of genus (jins) in sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is selling bread for wheat or flour. The ruling is 'ja'iz' (permissible) even with disparity.
2
Understand the reasoning
Bread is sold by count (number of loaves), while wheat and flour are sold by weight. Also, their uses differ. These make them different genera.
The transformation (baking) changes the genus classification.
3
Apply the principle
Since they are different genera, the rules of riba do not require equality, so disparity is allowed.

Source Text

Even if bread is made from wheat flour, it is still considered a separate genus because bread is sold by count (number) while wheat and flour are sold by weight. Commentary
This passage rules on exchanging bread for wheat or flour. Despite bread being made from wheat, Hanafi law considers them different genera (jins) for purposes of riba. The reasoning: bread is sold by count (adad), while wheat and flour are sold by weight (kayl). Additionally, their consumption purposes differ. Thus, disparity (tafadul) is allowed. This is a clear ruling that transformation (bread making) changes the genus classification.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, bread and wheat (or flour) are different genera because of differences in sale unit (count vs. weight) and consumption, thus disparity is allowed.

No Riba Between Master and Slave
Ruling with proof from Ibn Abbas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riba between master and slave, identify the condition for its permissibility, and explain the proof from the action of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
A master may take excess from his slave without riba because the slave's property belongs to the master, provided the slave is not in debt.

This lesson addresses a unique Hanafi ruling: riba (usury) does not apply in transactions between a master and his slave. The reasoning is based on the legal principle that the slave’s ownership is not independent—all his property ultimately belongs to the master. However, there is a crucial condition: the slave must not be in debt. We will also examine the evidentiary basis for this ruling from the practice of Ibn Abbas, a companion of the Prophet (ﷺ).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is a transaction between master and slave involving excess (e.g., taking two dirhams for one). According to the Hanafi school, this is permissible and not considered riba.
The ruling is 'ja'iz' (permissible) under normal circumstances.
2
Locate the condition
Note the explicit condition: the slave must not be in debt. If the slave has debt, his wealth is encumbered to creditors, so the ruling does not apply.
This condition prevents harm to third-party creditors.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
The rationale (ta'lil) is that the slave's property belongs to the master. Hence any exchange is considered taking one's own property, which falls outside the definition of riba.
This is based on the lack of legal independence (dhimmah) of the slave.
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof is an athar from Ibn Abbas, who sold fruit from his slave before it ripened (a transaction that normally involves riba) and explicitly stated, 'There is no riba between a slave and his master.'
This is a qawl sahabi (companion's statement) which is considered a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
5
Consider the ikhtilaf
Note that this ruling is specific to the Hanafi school. Other madhahib may not recognize this exception and would apply general riba rules to master-slave transactions.
The cross-madhhab difference stems from differing views on the legal capacity (ahliyyah) of slaves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ربوا بين المولى وعبده [۹۵۰] (۱۹) مولی اور اس کے غلام کے درمیان ربوا نہیں ہے۔
ت مولی اپنے غلام سے سود لے ایک درہم کے بدلے دو درہم لے تو یہ سود نہیں ہے۔ لے سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اس کے لئے شرط یہ ہے کہ غلام پر قرض نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ غلام پر قرض ہو گا تو غلام کا روپیہ صرف غلام کا نہیں ہے بلکہ قرض دینے والے کا ہے۔
(1) غلام کے پاس جو روپیہ ہے وہ سب مولی کا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک درہم دیگر دو درہم لے تو گویا کہ مولی نے اپنا ہی روپیہ لیا اس لئے یہ سود ہی نہیں ہوا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ کان ابن عباس يبيع عبدا له الثمرة قبل ان يبدو صلاحها و كان يقول ليس بين العبد وسيده ربا (الف) مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب لیس بین عید و سیدہ والمکاتب و سیده ربا، ج ثامن، ص ۷۶ نمبر ۱۴۳۷۸ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة من قال لیس بین العبد وسیده ربا ، ج رابع ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۲۰۰۳۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مولی اور اس کے غلام کے درمیان سود نہیں ہوتا۔
And there is no riba between the master and his slave. [950] (19) There is no riba between the master and his slave. Explanation: If the master takes usury from his slave, e.g., two dirhams for one, it is not riba. He may take it, but with the condition that the slave is not in debt. Because if the slave is in debt, his money is not solely his but belongs to the creditor. (1) All money that the slave has is the master's. So if he takes one dirham for two, it is as if he took his own money; thus it is not riba. (2) There is proof from Ibn Abbas: He used to sell fruit from his slave before it ripened, and he said, 'There is no riba between a slave and his master.' (Recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Ibn Abi Shaybah.) This proves that there is no riba between master and slave.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This ruling states that riba (usury) does not apply between a master and his slave (male or female). The reasoning: the slave's property ultimately belongs to the master, so any transaction between them is essentially taking one's own property. The condition is that the slave must not be in debt (because then his wealth belongs to creditors). The proof is an athar from Ibn Abbas who used to transact with his slave in ways that would otherwise involve riba, stating explicitly that riba does not exist between them. This is a specific legal concession in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
المولى (al-mawla): Master; owner of the slave
العبده (al-'abd): Slave (male or female)
ربوا (riba): Usury; here referring to excess in exchange

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can a master take two dirhams from his slave for one dirham without riba?
A) Always permissible
B) Only if the slave has no debt
C) Only if the slave agrees
D) Never permissible

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, riba does not apply between master and slave, provided the slave is not in debt, based on the principle of merged ownership and the practice of Ibn Abbas.

No Riba Between Muslim and Harbi in Dar al-Harb
Ruling that there is no riba between a Muslim and a Harbi in Dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riba transactions between a Muslim and a Harbi in Dar al-Harb, explain the basis in the analogy to ghanimah, and cite the mursal hadith dalil.

Core Idea
A Harbi's wealth is like war booty — consensual riba is more permissible than forcible seizure.

In this lesson, we examine a unique Hanafi concession: the prohibition of riba is lifted when transacting with an enemy non-Muslim (Harbi) in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). The reasoning rests on the unprotected status of the Harbi's property, which is legally analogous to war booty (ghanimah). A mursal hadith supports this ruling. However, this position is disputed by other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a riba-bearing transaction (e.g., exchanging gold for gold with excess) between a Muslim and a Harbi in Dar al-Harb. The Hanafi ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz); the prohibition of riba is suspended.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
The Harbi's property is not protected; it is akin to ghanimah. Taking it through a consensual riba transaction is even more permissible than forcible seizure, so the riba prohibition does not apply.
3
Examine the dalil
A mursal hadith from Makhul reports the Prophet said: 'There is no riba between the people of war.' The hadith is zanni in both transmission (thubut) and meaning (dalala), but the Hanafi school accepts it here.
4
Consider the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not accept this exception and maintain the universal prohibition of riba. Even among Hanafis, some restrict it strictly to Dar al-Harb.
5
Apply the ruling
In a war zone, a Muslim lends money to a Harbi with interest: the transaction is valid and no riba penalty applies. But if the same transaction occurs in Dar al-Islam, it becomes haram.

And there is no riba [in the hadith]: 'The station with the share like for like and dislike of disparity in it.' Page 235 no. 1240. This hadith states that if two genera, then sell with disparity as you wish. [951] (20) And there is no riba between a Muslim and a Harbi in Dar al-Harb. In Dar al-Harb, Harbis exist; a Muslim can take their wealth through riba transactions, and it is not riba. (1) The wealth of a Harbi is considered war booty (ghanimah), and taking war booty is permissible. So taking the Harbi's wealth with his consent is even more permissible. Commentary
This ruling states that riba does not apply in transactions between a Muslim and a Harbi (an enemy non-Muslim) in Dar al-Harb (enemy territory). The reason: the property of a Harbi is legally analogous to war booty (ghanimah), which a Muslim may take by force. Therefore, taking it through a riba transaction is even more permissible as it is consensual. The proof is a mursal hadith from Makhul that the Prophet said there is no riba between the people of war. This is a specific concession for wartime economic dealings.

Key Terms

الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): War booty; property taken from enemy combatants

Key Takeaway
In Dar al-Harb, the property of a Harbi is unprotected like ghanimah, so riba transactions with them are permissible according to the Hanafi school.

Permissibility of Exchanging Date Vinegar for Grape Vinegar with Excess
Ruling statement with explanatory commentary on genre determination for riba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging vinegar of different origins and explain the principle of jins (genus) in determining riba applicability.

Core Idea
Vinegar's origin—not name—determines its genre for riba; different sources allow unequal exchange.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the matn on exchanging date vinegar for grape vinegar. Although both are called 'vinegar', the Hanafi school distinguishes them by their source materials. Understanding this principle is key to correctly applying riba rules to transformed food products.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and its ruling
The transaction is exchanging date vinegar (khal al-daqal) for grape vinegar (khal al-'inab) with an excess or deficit. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Understand the basis for the ruling
The commentary explains that the two vinegars are considered different juristic genres (jins) because they come from different fruits (dates vs. grapes).
This is the core legal reasoning.
3
Apply the genre principle
In Hanafi fiqh, riba applies only to same-genre items exchanged in unequal quantities. Different genres allow surplus or deficit.
Thus, the transaction is riba-free.
4
Generalize the principle
The same rule applies to other transformed products: the origin determines the genre, not the final name or form.
e.g., apple cider vinegar vs. grape vinegar are different genres.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[948] (17) وخل الدقل بخل العنب متفاضلا۔ اور جائز ہے کھجور کا سرکہ انگور کے سرکہ کے ساتھ کمی بیشی کر کے۔ وجه: کھجور کا سرکہ الگ جنس ہے اور انگور کا سرکہ الگ جنس ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں الگ الگ جنس سے نکلے ہیں اس لئے کمی بیشی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ دونوں کا نام سرکہ ہے۔
(17) And vinegar of inferior dates with vinegar of grapes in excess is permissible. And it is permissible to sell vinegar of dates with vinegar of grapes with surplus or deficit. Reason: Vinegar of dates is a separate genre and vinegar of grapes is a separate genre. Because both come from different genres, therefore selling with surplus or deficit is permissible, even though both are called vinegar.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn followed by explanatory commentary. The author states that exchanging vinegar made from inferior dates (dill) for vinegar made from grapes with an excess or deficit is permissible. The commentary explains the reason: although both are called vinegar, they are considered different juristic genres (jins) because their source materials are different. The Hanafi school considers the origin of the substance in determining genus for riba purposes, not the final product. Therefore, they are like two different commodities and can be exchanged in unequal quantities without riba.

Key Terms
خل الدقل (khal al-daqal): Vinegar made from inferior dates (daqal).
خل العنب (khal al-'inab): Vinegar made from grapes.
متفاضلا (mutafādilan): With an excess or deficit in quantity or value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because they are both liquid and liquids are not ribawi.

Key Takeaway
Date vinegar and grape vinegar are different juristic genres, so exchanging them in unequal quantities is permissible because of their different origins.

Why Bread Is a Different Genre from Wheat in Riba Rulings
Ruling with rational expansion: permissibility of an exchange and its justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling bread for wheat or flour with excess and explain the three reasons that make them different genres.

Core Idea
Bread is a different genre from wheat even though made from it, because mode of sale and usage differ.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samir presents a ruling that may seem puzzling at first: bread, which is made from wheat, can be sold for wheat or flour in unequal amounts. The commentary clarifies that juristic genre (jins) is determined by factors beyond material composition. Bread is sold by count and consumed as prepared food, while wheat and flour are sold by weight and used as raw ingredients. These differences make them separate genres, freeing the exchange from riba rules requiring equality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the permissibility: it is jayiz to sell bread for wheat or flour with surplus or deficit (mufaddal).
2
Recognize the Puzzle
Note that bread is made from wheat, so one might assume they are the same genre for riba purposes. The commentary addresses this.
3
Understand the First Reason: Mode of Sale
Bread is sold by count ('adad), while wheat and flour are sold by weight (kayl). This is a key difference in transactional nature.
Different scales of measurement often indicate different genres in Hanafi law.
4
Understand the Second Reason: Consumption
The maṣrif (usage/consumption) of bread is different from that of wheat and flour. Bread is ready-to-eat, while wheat/flour require processing.
Distinct consumption purposes contribute to different juristic genres.
5
Conclude: Different Genres
Because of the above differences, bread and wheat/flour are considered different ajnas (genres). Hence, the riba rule requiring equality (for same genre) does not apply, and selling with excess is permissible.

Source Text

[949] (18) ويجوز بيع الخبز بالحنطة والدقيق متفاضلا۔ اور جائز ہے روٹی کی بیع گیہوں سے اور آٹے سے کمی بیشی کر کے۔ روٹی اگر چہ گیہوں کے آٹے کی ہو پھر بھی اس کو الگ جنس قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ روٹی عدد سے گن کر بکتی ہے اور گیہوں اور آٹا کیلی ہیں۔ اسی طرح روٹی کا مصرف الگ ہے اور گیہوں کا مصرف الگ ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں دو جنس ہو گئے۔ اس لئے کمی بیشی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہو گیا۔
(18) And it is permissible to sell bread for wheat and flour with surplus or deficit. And it is permissible to sell bread for wheat and flour with surplus or deficit. Bread, even though it is made from wheat flour, is still considered a separate genre. Because bread is sold by count and wheat and flour are by weight. Similarly, the consumption of bread is different and the consumption of wheat is different. Therefore, both become two genres. Hence, selling with surplus or deficit becomes permissible.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This is another ruling from the matn with commentary. The author states that selling bread for wheat or flour in unequal amounts is permissible. The commentary gives three reasons: (1) bread is sold by count ('adad) while wheat and flour are sold by weight (kayl). (2) Their usages (masraf) are different — bread is consumed as prepared food, while wheat and flour are raw materials. (3) These differences make them different juristic genres, so the riba rule of equality does not apply.

Key Terms
خبز (khubz): Bread, a processed food item.
حنطة (hintah): Wheat.
دقيق (daqīq): Flour, milled wheat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, which of the following is NOT a reason for considering bread a different genre from wheat?
A) Bread is sold by count, wheat by weight.
B) The consumption of bread is different from that of wheat.
C) The Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly said bread is a different genre.
D) Both A and B are reasons.

Key Takeaway
Bread is a different juristic genre from its raw materials (wheat, flour) for riba due to differences in mode of sale and consumption.

Dispute on Riba Between Muslim and Harbi in Dar al-Harb
Intra-Hanafi dispute on riba with harbi in dar al-harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on riba between a Muslim and a harbi in dar al-harb, identify the proofs for each position, and explain which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The prohibition of riba is not absolute across all contexts—Hanafi masters differ on dar al-harb.

This passage addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: does the Qur'anic prohibition of riba apply when a Muslim deals with an enemy non-Muslim (harbi) in enemy territory (dar al-harb)? Imam Abu Hanifa held a permissive view, while his student Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i maintained the prohibition. The lesson will guide you through their proofs and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling at issue
Identify the specific legal question: Is riba prohibited between a Muslim and a harbi in dar al-harb? This is a dispute within the Hanafi school.
The matn begins with 'ولا ربا بين المسلم والحربي في دار الحرب' (No riba between the Muslim and the harbi in dar al-harb), indicating Abu Hanifa's position.
2
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proofs
Abu Hanifa holds that such transactions are not riba. His evidence: (1) analogy to booty (harbi's wealth is like ghanimah), (2) a mursal hadith of Makhul stating 'no riba between the people of war and the people of Islam'.
The commentator notes he could not find this hadith despite searching, weakening the proof.
3
Identify the opposing position and proofs
Imam Abu Yusuf (and al-Shafi'i) argue that riba is absolutely prohibited. Their evidence: (1) the general Qur'anic prohibition in al-Baqarah 2:278, (2) the Prophet's abolition of all riba in the Farewell Pilgrimage, including riba owed by disbelievers to al-Abbas.
These proofs are considered stronger by the commentator.
4
Examine the commentator's tarjih
The commentator states that the fatwa is on the position of Imam Abu Yusuf, especially in dar al-aman (safe territory). This means the relied-upon ruling is prohibition.
The commentator's own research could not verify Abu Hanifa's mursal hadith.
5
Conclude the practical ruling
The operative (mufta bihi) position: Riba is prohibited between a Muslim and a harbi, even in dar al-harb. The earlier permissive view is marjuh (weaker).
This conclusion applies to both dar al-harb and dar al-aman.

Source Text

بين المسلم والحربي في دار الحرب.

كتاب البيوع
قرآن میں علی الاطلاق سود کو حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ آیت ہے یا ایها الذین آمنوا اتقوا الله وذروا مابقى من الربوا ان كنتم مؤمنين (الف) (آیت ۲۷۸ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں فرمایا کہ جو سود باقی رہ گیا ہو اس کو چھوڑ دو اور یہ علی الاطلاق ہے۔ اس لئے حربی سے سود لینا حرام ہوگا (۳) حجتہ الوداع کے موقع پر آپ نے سود ختم کرنے کا اعلان فرمایا تھا اور حضرت عباس کا سود جو لوگوں پر تھا اس کو معاف کرنے کا اعلان فرمایا تھا۔ حالانکہ وہ سود کافروں پر بھی تھا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سود حربی سے بھی لینا حرام ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله فسأل عن القوم ... واول ربا اضع ربانا ربا عباس بن عبد المطلب فانه موضوع كله ( ب ) ( مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۳۹۴ نمبر ۱۲۱۸ را بو داود شریف، باب صفته حجتہ النبی ص ۲۶۹ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں آپ نے علی الاطلاق سود منع فرمایا ہے۔ بلکہ ابوداؤد میں یہ جملہ ہے وربا الجاهلية موضوع جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تربیوں کے سود بھی ختم کئے جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے حربی سے بھی سود لینا حرام ہوگا فتوی امام یوسف کے مسلک پر ہے۔ خصوصا دار الامن میں سود لینا بالکل جائز نہیں ہے۔
حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) مسلمان کے درمیان سود واقع نہیں ہوتا (الف) اے ایمان والو! اللہ سے ڈرو اور جو سود باقی ہے اس کو چھوڑ دو اگر تم ایمان رکھتے ہو ( ب ) سب سے پہلار ہوا جو ختم کرتا ہوں وہ عباس بن عبدالمطلب کا ر ہوا ہے۔ پس وہ تمام کے تمام ختم کئے جاتے ہیں۔
(20) And there is no riba between the Muslim and the harbi in dar al-harb. In dar al-harb, the harbis, a Muslim may take their wealth through a riba transaction, that is not riba. (1) The wealth of a harbi is like the wealth of booty. And taking booty is permissible. Therefore, taking the wealth of a harbi with his consent is even more permissible. (2) For this there is also a mursal hadith from Makhul that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: No riba between the people of war, and I think he said: and between the people of Islam. (footnote citing sources).

In this hadith it is said that there is no riba between the harbi and the Muslim. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. I did not find this hadith despite much searching.

Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i say that riba is not permissible even between a harbi and a Muslim.

Kitab al-Buyu: In the Qur’an, riba has been absolutely prohibited. The verse: 'O you who believe! Fear Allah and give up what remains of riba if you are believers.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:278). This verse commands that whatever riba remains be abandoned, and it is absolute. Therefore, taking riba from a harbi would be unlawful. (3) On the occasion of the Farewell Pilgrimage, the Prophet announced the abolition of riba and the cancellation of the riba of al-‘Abbas that was owed to him from people, even though that riba was also against disbelievers. This shows that taking riba from a harbi is also prohibited. The hadith: 'I entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah ... and the first riba I abolish is our riba, the riba of al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abd al-Muttalib, for it is all waived.' (Muslim, Abu Dawood). In this hadith, the Prophet absolutely forbade riba. Moreover, in Abu Dawood there is the phrase 'and the riba of the Jahiliyyah is waived,' meaning that even the riba of the polytheists is abolished. Therefore, taking riba from a harbi is also prohibited. The fatwa is according to the position of Imam Yusuf, especially in dar al-aman, taking riba is absolutely not permissible.

Footnote: (previous page continued) between the Muslim and the harbi in dar al-harb. (a) 'O you who believe! Fear Allah and give up what remains of riba if you are believers.' (b) 'The first riba I abolish is our riba, the riba of al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abd al-Muttalib, for it is all waived.'
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents a disputation within the Hanafi school regarding whether riba applies between a Muslim and a harbi (non-Muslim enemy) in dar al-harb (enemy territory). The matn states 'no riba between the Muslim and the harbi in dar al-harb' which is Imam Abu Hanifa's position. The commentary gives two arguments supporting this: (1) the wealth of a harbi is akin to booty (ghanimah), which is permissible to take; (2) a mursal hadith from Makhul stating 'no riba between the people of war and the people of Islam.' However, the commentator notes he could not find this hadith despite searching. Then the opposing view of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i is presented: they argue that riba is absolutely prohibited based on the general Qur’anic prohibition (al-Baqarah 2:278) and the Prophet's universal abolition of riba during the Farewell Pilgrimage, which included riba owed by disbelievers to al-Abbas. The commentator concludes that the fatwa is on the position of Imam Abu Yusuf, especially in dar al-aman (safe land), where taking riba is absolutely impermissible. Thus the operative ruling is the prohibition of riba with harbis, except possibly in specific circumstances as per earlier Hanafi view.

Key Terms
حربی (harbī): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, not protected by an aman or treaty.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under the control of non-Muslims who are at war with Muslims.
ربوا (ribā): Usury or interest, prohibited in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, whose position is followed in the fatwa?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam al-Shafi'i
D) Ibn Abbas

Key Takeaway
Although Imam Abu Hanifa permitted riba with a harbi in dar al-harb, the relied-upon Hanafi position prohibits it, especially in dar al-aman.

Riba with a Harbi in Dar al-Harb: Resolving the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Resolving the Hanafi dispute on riba with a harbi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi ruling on riba with a harbi in dar al-harb and explain the shift from Abu Hanifa's position due to the strength of Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi ruling bans riba with harbis—absolute Quranic prohibition overrides a weak hadith.

The Hanafi school is not a monolith; its early masters sometimes disagreed on rulings based on differing evidence. This passage presents a key intra-madhhab dispute: whether a Muslim may take riba from a non-Muslim enemy (harbi) in enemy territory (dar al-harb). Imam Abu Hanifa held it permissible, but Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i argued it is absolutely forbidden. The commentator resolves this by siding with Abu Yusuf, making this the operative fatwa. Let us walk through the dispute and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the ruling that Abu Hanifa held: no riba between Muslim and harbi in dar al-harb, i.e., riba is permissible in that context.
He based this on a hadith: 'لا ربا بين المسلم والحربي في دار الحرب'.
2
Identify the opposing view within the Hanafi school
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf (along with Imam al-Shafi'i) held that riba is forbidden even with a harbi in dar al-harb.
Abu Yusuf is a companion of Abu Hanifa and a major authority in the school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the dalil of Abu Yusuf: the Quranic verse 2:278 which absolutely prohibits riba, and the Prophet's abolition of all riba at Hajjat al-Wada', including riba of Abbas which involved non-Muslims.
The proofs establish that the prohibition is universal, with no exception for harbis.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
Note the commentator's critique: the hadith cited by Abu Hanifa could not be found after extensive search, implying it is weak or non-authentic. Thus the absolute Quranic command takes precedence.
This methodological critique—questioning the thubut (authenticity) of a dalil—is a key step in tarjih.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Conclude that the fatwa is on the madhhab of Imam Abu Yusuf, especially in dar al-aman. Taking riba from a harbi is forbidden absolutely.
This shift from Abu Hanifa's view shows how later Hanafi scholars weighed evidence.

Source Text

ماشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) مسلمان کے درمیان سود واقع نہیں ہوتا (الف) اے ایمان والو! اللہ سے ڈرو اور جو سود باقی ہے اس کو چھوڑ دو اگر تم ایمان رکھتے ہو ( ب ) سب سے پہلار ہوا جو ختم کرتا ہوں وہ عباس بن عبدالمطلب کا ر ہوا ہے۔ پس وہ تمام کے تمام ختم کئے جاتے ہیں۔
Between the Muslim and the harbi in dar al-harb. 83. In this hadith it is said that there is no riba between the harbi and the Muslim. This is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. I did not find this hadith anywhere after much searching. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i say that riba between the harbi and the Muslim is also not permissible. Kitab al-Buyu'. In the Qur'an, riba is absolutely declared forbidden. The verse is: 'O you who believe, fear Allah and give up what remains of riba if you are believers' (Surah al-Baqara 2:278). In this verse it is said that leave the riba that remains, and this is absolute. Therefore, taking riba from the harbi will be forbidden. (3) On the occasion of Hajjat al-Wada', the Prophet announced the abolition of riba and announced the forgiveness of the riba of Abbas that was upon people, even though that riba was also upon disbelievers. This shows that taking riba from the harbi is also forbidden. He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah and he asked about the people... 'And the first riba I abolish is the riba of Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib, for it is all abolished.' (Muslim, Kitab al-Hajj, 394 no. 1218; Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Hajj, 269 no. 1905). In this hadith, the Prophet absolutely forbade riba. Rather, in Abu Dawud, there is the sentence 'and the riba of the Jahiliyyah is abolished,' meaning that the riba of the Arabs is also abolished. Therefore, taking riba from the harbi will also be forbidden. The fatwa is on the madhhab of Imam Yusuf. Especially in dar al-aman, taking riba is absolutely not permissible. Margin: (Continuation from previous page) No riba occurs between Muslims. (a) O you who believe, fear Allah and give up what remains of riba if you are believers. (b) The first riba I abolish is the riba of Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib. So it is all abolished.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-madhhab dispute regarding riba transactions between a Muslim and a harbi (non-Muslim enemy combatant) in dar al-harb (abode of war). Imam Abu Hanifa held that riba is not applicable between them, citing a hadith. However, the commentator states he could not find this hadith despite extensive search. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i opposed this, arguing that the Quranic prohibition of riba is absolute and applies to all, including harbis. They also cite the Prophet's sermon at Hajjat al-Wada' where he abolished all riba, including that of Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib which involved non-Muslims. The text concludes that the fatwa is on the position of Imam Abu Yusuf, especially in dar al-aman (abode of peace/safety), where taking riba is absolutely impermissible. This reflects the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling in the Hanafi school, shifting from Abu Hanifa's original view.

Key Terms
ربا (riba): Usury or interest, prohibited in Islam; the passage discusses its application to transactions with harbis.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, residing in dar al-harb.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where war with Muslims is permitted or ongoing.
دار الامن (dar al-aman): Territory where Muslims are safe, including dar al-Islam and areas under aman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Imam's position is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) regarding riba with a harbi?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam al-Shafi'i
D) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Takeaway
Riba with a harbi is absolutely forbidden in the Hanafi mufta bihi, as the Quranic prohibition overrides a weak hadith.

The Ruling and Proof of Salam (Forward Sale)
Defining salam and stating its permissibility with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam, identify its proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and apply the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Salam is valid as a concession despite selling what is not possessed, provided goods are specifiable by measure, weight, or count without significant variation.

This lesson introduces salam, a forward sale where payment is made in advance for future delivery. Although general qiyas prohibits selling what one does not possess, the Hanafi school permits salam as a concession (rukhsah) for the benefit of the poor. We will examine the proofs from the Quran and hadith that establish this ruling, and learn the conditions that make salam valid and enforceable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that salam is a sale where the price is paid immediately and the goods are delivered later. According to the Hanafi school, it is sahih (valid) as a concession.
The ruling is a departure from the general prohibition of selling what is not in one's possession.
2
Understand the exception to qiyas
Note that qiyas would render salam invalid, but istihsan (juristic preference) allows it to benefit the poor who need upfront capital.
The passage explicitly states 'the requirement of qiyas is that this sale is not permissible... but a concession is given for the poor.'
3
Examine the proofs (dalil)
Study the Quranic verse (2:282) that commands writing deferred debts, which includes salam, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet allowed salam with known measure, weight, and term.
The Quran is qati' al-thubut but 'amm; the hadith is zanni al-thubut but specific.
4
Identify the conditions
List the conditions: goods must be from measured (makilat), weighed (mawzunat), or counted items that do not vary significantly (ma'dudat allati la tatafawat), and also length-measured items. Additionally, the measure, weight, and term must be known.
These conditions ensure the goods are sufficiently specified to avoid dispute.
5
Apply the terminological framework
Learn the key terms: muslam ilayh (seller), rabb al-salam (buyer), muslam fih (goods), ra's al-mal (capital).
These terms are used throughout Hanafi fiqh texts on salam.

باب السلم
ضروری نوٹ بیع سلم کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ قیمت ابھی لے اور مبیع کچھ دنوں کے بعد دے۔ اس بیع کو بیع سلم کہتے ہیں۔ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ یہ بیع جائز نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں گزرا ہے کہ جو مبیع تمہارے پاس نہ ہو اس کو نہ بیچو ولا بيع ما ليس عندک (الف)(ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۳۵۰۴ / ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۲۳۲) لیکن غرباء کے لئے یہ سہولت دی گئی ہے کہ وہ مالداروں سے قیمت ابھی لیں اور اس قیمت سے خریدو فروخت کرتے رہیں اور نفع کماتے رہیں۔ پھر جب مبیع دینے کا وقت آئے مبیع خرید کر مشتری کے حوالے کر دیں۔ چونکہ مبیع سامنے موجود نہیں ہے اس لئے مبیع کو مکمل متعین کرنے کے لئے سات شرطیں ہوں تو بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ ان شرطوں سے مبیع کا خاکہ سامنے آجاتا ہے اور جھگڑا کرنے کا موقع نہیں رہتا۔ ان شرطوں کی تفصیل آگے آئے گی۔ بیع سلم جائز ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ یا ایھا الذین آمنوا اذا تداينتم بدين الى اجل مسمی فاکتبوه (ب) (آیت ۲۸۲ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں فرمایا کہ کسی دین کا معاملہ کرو تو اس کو لکھ لیا کرو اور بیچ سلم میں بھی دین کا معاملہ ہے اس لئے اس کا جواز بھی اس آیت میں شامل ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قدم النبي ل المدينة وهم يسلفون بالثمر السنتين والثلاث فقال من اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب السلم فی وزن معلوم ص ۲۹۸ نمبر ۲۲۴۰ ر مسلم شریف ، باب السلم ص ۳۱ نمبر ۱۶۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیع سلم جائز ہے اور تین شرطوں کا بھی علم ہوا کہ مبیع کی کیل ، وزن اور مدت معلوم ہوں۔
وت باب السلم میں بائع کو مسلم الیہ مشتری کو رب السلم ہیچ کو مسلم فیہ اور شمن کو راس المال کہتے ہیں۔ (۹۵۲] (۱) سلم جائز ہے کیلی چیزیں، وزنی چیزیں اور اس عددی چیزوں میں جس کے افراد میں تفاوت نہ ہو۔ جیسے اخروٹ اور انڈے اور ہاتھ
سے ناپنے والی چیزوں میں۔

حاشیہ : (الف) مت بچھو وہ چیز جو تمہارے پاس نہ ہو ( ب ) اے ایمان والو جب تم متعین مدت تک دین کا معاملہ کرو تو اس کو لکھ لیا کرو (ج) آپ مدینہ تشریف لائے اور لوگ پھل میں دو سال اور تین سال کے لئے بیع سلم کرتے تو آپ نے فرمایا جو کسی چیز میں بیع سلم کرے تو کیل معلوم ہو، وزن معلوم ہوا اور مدت معلوم ہو۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 2, 84. Kitab al-Buyu'. Bab al-Salam. (1952) Salam is permissible for measured items, weighed items, and counted items that do not vary.

Bab al-Salam. Necessary note: The meaning of bay' salam is that the price is taken immediately and the commodity is given after some days. This sale is called bay' salam. The requirement of qiyas (analogical reasoning) is that this sale is not permissible, because the hadith states: 'Do not sell what is not with you' (Abu Dawud no. 3504, Tirmidhi no. 1232). But a concession is given for the poor so that they may take the price from the wealthy and use it to buy and sell and earn profit. Then when the time comes to deliver the commodity, they buy it and hand it over to the buyer. Since the commodity is not present, seven conditions are required for complete specification of the commodity so that bay' salam becomes permissible. These conditions create a description of the commodity and prevent dispute. The details of these conditions will come later. The proof for the permissibility of bay' salam is this verse: 'O you who believe, when you contract a debt for a specified term, write it down' (Surah al-Baqara 2:282). In this verse it is said that when you make a transaction of debt, write it down, and bay' salam is also a transaction of debt, so its permissibility is included in this verse. (2) There is a hadith: 'Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet came to Madinah while they were paying in advance for fruit for two and three years. He said: Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be with a known measure, a known weight, and a known term.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Salam fi Wazn Ma'rum, 298 no. 2240; Muslim, Bab al-Salam, 31 no. 1604). From this hadith it is known that bay' salam is permissible and also three conditions: the measure, weight, and term of the commodity must be known.

In bab al-salam, the seller is called muslim ilayh, the buyer is called rabb al-salam, the commodity is called muslim fih, and the price is called ra's al-mal. (1952) (1) Salam is permissible for measured items, weighed items, and counted items whose individuals do not vary, like walnuts and eggs, and for items measured by hand (length).

A measured item, i.e., sold by measure like wheat, rice: salam is permissible. Similarly, items sold by weight or items sold by count but whose individuals do not differ significantly, like walnuts and eggs—their individuals do not have much difference, giving small or large does not cause dispute. Similarly, items sold by hand or yard measure, like cloth, can be sold through salam. Salam is permissible for measured, weighed, counted, and length-measured items because if their qualities and weight are specified, it suffices for identification and no dispute arises. Therefore, salam is permissible for these items. And for items that cannot be specified by qualities, salam is not permissible.

Footnotes: (a) 'Do not sell what is not with you.' (b) 'O you who believe, when you contract a debt for a specified term, write it down.' (c) 'He came to Madinah and they were paying in advance for fruit for two and three years. He said: Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be with a known measure, a known weight, and a known term.'
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This lesson introduces the chapter on salam (forward sale), a contract where payment is made in advance for delivery of goods later. The commentator explains that analogical reasoning (qiyas) would suggest salam is invalid because one sells what one does not possess, but a concession (rukhsah) was given for the benefit of the poor. The permissibility is established by Quran 2:282 concerning deferred transactions and by the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet allowed salam with known measure, weight, and time. The matn by al-Quduri states that salam is permissible for items that are measured (makilat), weighed (mawzunat), and counted items that do not vary significantly (ma'dudat allati la tatafawat), such as walnuts and eggs, and also for items measured by length (such as cloth). The reason is that these items can be sufficiently defined by description to avoid dispute. The commentary also explains the terminology: seller (muslam ilayh), buyer (rabb al-salam), goods (muslam fih), and principal (ra's al-mal).

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for goods to be delivered later.
مكيالت (makilat): Items sold by volume measure, such as wheat or rice.
موزونات (mawzunat): Items sold by weight.
معدودات (ma'dudat): Items sold by count that do not vary significantly, such as walnuts or eggs.
مسلم إليه (muslam ilayh): The seller in a salam contract who receives payment upfront and delivers later.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The buyer in a salam contract who pays the price upfront.
مسلم فيه (muslam fih): The goods or commodity subject of the salam contract.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The principal amount paid by the buyer in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for a valid salam contract?
A) The goods must be from measured, weighed, or counted items that do not vary significantly
B) The quantity (measure, weight, count, or length) must be known
C) The goods must be present at the time of contract
D) The term of delivery must be known

Key Takeaway
Salam is a valid contract by concession, permitted for goods that can be adequately described by measure, weight, count, or length, provided the quantity and delivery term are known.

Definition and Permissibility of Salam Sale
Introduces salam contract, its ruling, and textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of salam, identify the qiyas objection, and list the three conditions from the hadith that make it permissible.

Core Idea
Salam is permissible despite qiyas, because the Prophet allowed it with known measure, weight, and term.

The salam contract allows immediate payment for future delivery, contrary to the general prohibition of selling what you do not possess. This passage introduces its definition, the qiyas objection, and the textual proofs (Quran and Sunnah) that establish its permissibility as a concession for those in need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its apparent ruling by qiyas
What is the definition of salam? By standard analogy (qiyas), why would it be considered invalid? Recall the hadith 'Do not sell what is not with you.'
2
Recognize the concession
The Shari'ah makes an exception for salam due to need (hajah). This is an application of istihsan, departing from qiyas.
3
Locate the dalil from Quran
Find the verse cited (2:282) and understand how it includes salam as a debt transaction.
4
Locate the dalil from Sunnah
Find the hadith of Ibn Abbas and note that the Prophet approved salam with three conditions.
5
Note the conditions derived from the hadith
List the three conditions: known measure (kayl ma'lum), known weight (wazn ma'lum), and known term (ajal ma'lum).
The passage also mentions seven conditions in total, but only these three are explicit in this section.

ضروری نوٹ بیع سلم کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ قیمت ابھی لے اور مبیع کچھ دنوں کے بعد دے۔ اس بیع کو بیع سلم کہتے ہیں۔ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ یہ بیع جائز نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں گزرا ہے کہ جو مبیع تمہارے پاس نہ ہو اس کو نہ بیچو ولا بيع ما ليس عندك (الف)(ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۳۵۰۴ / ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۲۳۲) لیکن غرباء کے لئے یہ سہولت دی گئی ہے کہ وہ مالداروں سے قیمت ابھی لیں اور اس قیمت سے خریدو فروخت کرتے رہیں اور نفع کماتے رہیں۔ پھر جب مبیع دینے کا وقت آئے مبیع خرید کر مشتری کے حوالے کر دیں۔ چونکہ مبیع سامنے موجود نہیں ہے اس لئے مبیع کو مکمل متعین کرنے کے لئے سات شرطیں ہوں تو بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ ان شرطوں سے مبیع کا خاکہ سامنے آجاتا ہے اور جھگڑا کرنے کا موقع نہیں رہتا۔ ان شرطوں کی تفصیل آگے آئے گی۔ بیع سلم جائز ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ یا ایھا الذین آمنوا اذا تداينتم بدين الى اجل مسمی فاکتبوه (ب) (آیت ۲۸۲ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں فرمایا کہ کسی دین کا معاملہ کرو تو اس کو لکھ لیا کرو اور بیچ سلم میں بھی دین کا معاملہ ہے اس لئے اس کا جواز بھی اس آیت میں شامل ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قدم النبي ل المدينة وهم يسلفون بالثمر السنتين والثلاث فقال من اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب السلم فی وزن معلوم ص ۲۹۸ نمبر ۲۲۴۰ ر مسلم شریف ، باب السلم ص ۳۱ نمبر ۱۶۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیع سلم جائز ہے اور تین شرطوں کا بھی علم ہوا کہ مبیع کی کیل ، وزن اور مدت معلوم ہوں۔
