حاشیہ : (الف) مت بچھو وہ چیز جو تمہارے پاس نہ ہو ( ب ) اے ایمان والو جب تم متعین مدت تک دین کا معاملہ کرو تو اس کو لکھ لیا کرو (ج) آپ مدینہ تشریف لائے اور لوگ پھل میں دو سال اور تین سال کے لئے بیع سلم کرتے تو آپ نے فرمایا جو کسی چیز میں بیع سلم کرے تو کیل معلوم ہو، وزن معلوم ہوا اور مدت معلوم ہو۔
Chapter of Salam. Necessary note: The meaning of bay' salam is that the price is taken immediately and the commodity is given after some days. This sale is called bay' salam. Qiyas requires that this sale should not be permissible because in the hadith it occurred: 'Do not sell what is not with you' and 'The sale of what is not with you is not allowed.' However, for the poor this facility has been given that they take the price from the wealthy immediately and with that price they continue buying and selling and earning profit. Then when the time comes to deliver the commodity, they buy the commodity and hand it over to the buyer. Since the commodity is not present, for fully specifying the commodity, if seven conditions are met, then salam will be permissible. These conditions bring the description of the commodity before the eyes and no opportunity for dispute remains. The detail of these conditions will come later. The proof for the permissibility of salam is this verse: 'O you who believe, when you contract a debt for a fixed term, record it' (2:282). In this verse it is commanded that when you make a transaction of debt, write it down, and in salam there is also a transaction of debt, so its permissibility is included in this verse. (2) In the hadith: from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet came to Medina and they were giving salam in fruits for two and three years, so he said: Whoever gives salam in something, then let it be with a known measure, a known weight, and a known term.' (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is learned that salam is permissible and also three conditions are learned: the measure, weight, and term of the commodity must be known. And in the chapter of salam, the seller is called muslam ilayh, the buyer is called rabb al-salam, the commodity is called muslam fih, and the price is called ra's al-mal. Footnotes: (a) 'Do not sell what is not with you' (b) 'O believers, when you contract a debt for a fixed term, record it' (c) 'The Prophet came to Medina and they were giving salam in fruits for two and three years, so he said: Whoever gives salam in something, then let it be with a known measure, a known weight, and a known term.'
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on salam (forward sale) from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri. The author begins by defining salam: immediate payment for deferred delivery of a specific commodity. He notes that by qiyas (analogy) this contract should be invalid because it involves selling something not in one's possession, which is prohibited in the hadith 'Do not sell what is not with you.' However, the need of the poor led to a concession allowing them to secure capital upfront. The author then cites two primary proofs for the permissibility of salam: (1) the Qur'anic verse on recording debts (2:282), which includes salam as a debt transaction; and (2) the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet allowed salam in fruits with three conditions: known measure, known weight, and known term. The passage also introduces the technical terminology of salam: the seller (muslam ilayh), the buyer (rabb al-salam), the commodity (muslam fih), and the price (ra's al-mal). The commentary follows the author's order, first explaining the definition and qiyas objection, then the proofs, and finally the terminology.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A sale where the price is paid immediately and the commodity is delivered at a future date.
مسلم إليه (muslam ilayh): The seller in a salam contract who receives the price upfront and is obligated to deliver the commodity later.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The buyer in a salam contract who pays the price immediately and receives the commodity later.
مسلم فيه (muslam fih): The commodity to be delivered in the future in a salam contract.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The price paid upfront in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three conditions for salam mentioned in the hadith of Ibn Abbas?
A) Known price, known commodity, known seller
B) Known measure, known weight, known term
C) Known quantity, known quality, known delivery place
D) Known price, known term, known commodity

Key Takeaway
Salam is a valid exception to the prohibition of selling what is not possessed, based on Quran and Sunnah, requiring known measure, weight, and term.

Valid Commodities for Salam: The Four Categories and Their Proofs
Specifies types of goods in which salam is valid with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of commodities in which salam is valid according to the Hanafi school and apply the condition that the commodity must be specifiable by attributes to determine validity.

Core Idea
Salam is valid only for goods that can be precisely described to avoid uncertainty.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a special contract where payment is made upfront for delivery of a commodity later. To prevent disputes, the commodity must be determined exactly. The Hanafi school specifies four types of goods that can be sufficiently described: those measured by volume, weight, countable units with minimal variation, and length. This lesson will walk you through each category and the textual proofs that support them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the passage lists the types of commodities in which salam is permissible (ja'iz). The ruling is that salam is valid in makilat, mawzunat (excluding gold/silver), ma'dudat with negligible variation, and madhru'at.
The act is the salam contract; the ruling is permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas requiring 'known measure and known weight.' An athar extends this to length (madhru'at). The camel hadith analogizes for ma'dudat.
Hadith: 'من أسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم إلى أجل معلوم'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative to specify measure and weight implies that only goods that can be measured or weighed are eligible. The athar on cloth adds madhru'at. Ma'dudat are analogized from the camel hadith because counted items can also be specified by number and description.
The athar: 'إذا كان ذراع معلوم إلى أجل معلوم فلا بأس'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Even among mawzunat, gold and silver coins (thaman) are excluded because their value cannot be fixed by description. This is a specific exception within the Hanafi school.
Exception: 'وزنی میں درہم و دنانیر بھی ہیں... ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں'
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) agree on the categories but may have different conditions for ma'dudat.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text

ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ... فـقـال مـن اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب السلم فی وزن معلوم ص ۲۹۸ نمبر ۲۲۴۰) اس حدیث میں کیل معلوم سے پتہ چلا کہ چیز کیلی ہو، اور وزن معلوم سے پتہ چلا کہ چیز وزنی ہو۔ اور کپڑے کے بیع سلم کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابن عباس في السلف في الكرابيس قال اذا كان ذراع مـعـلـوم الـى اجل معلوم فلا بأس (ب) ( سنن البيهقي ، باب السلف في المحطة والشعير والزبيب والزيت والثياب وجميع ما يضبط بالصفة ج سادس ص ۴۲ نمبر ۱۱۲۳ار مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۷۳افی السلم بالثیاب، ج رابع ، ص ۳۹۸، نمبر۲۱۴۰۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کپڑا جو ہاتھ سے ناپا جاتا ہے اس کی بیع سلم ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور اس پر عددی چیزوں کو قیاس کر لیں ۔ عددی میں بیع سلم جائز ہونے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فكان يأخذ البعير بالبعيرين الى ابل الصدقة (ج) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب في الرخصة في ذلك یعنی باب في الحيوان بالحيوان نسی ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۳۳۵۷) اس حدیث میں آپ نے ایک اونٹ کو دو اونٹ کے بدلے لیا ہے۔ جس سے عددی چیزوں میں بیع سلم کا پتہ چلتا
وزنی میں درہم اور دنانی بھی ہیں۔ ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ ان کے صفات متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے ۔ اس لئے وزنی سے وہ چیزیں مراد ہیں جو وزن کی جاتی ہوں لیکن درہم اور دنا نیر نہ ہوں۔ جیسے لوہا وغیرہ۔
کپڑا۔
صفات متعین کرنے کے ذریعہ جو چیزیں متعین کی جاتی ہو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔ الجوز : اخروٹ ۔ البيض : انڈا۔ المزروعات : ذراع سے مشتق ہے، جو چیز ہاتھ سے ناپی جاتی ہو یا گز سے ناپی جاتی ہو جیسے
[952] (1) Salam is valid for things measured by volume (makilat), things weighed (mawzunat), and those countable things (ma'dudat) whose individual units do not differ, like walnuts, eggs, and things measured by the hand (madhru'at). A thing that is makil (measured by volume) like wheat, rice, then salam in it is valid. Similarly, things that are weighed or things that are counted but whose individual units do not differ significantly, like walnuts and eggs, because there is not much difference in their units, giving small or large ones does not cause dispute. Likewise, things that are measured by hand or cubit, like cloth, can be sold via salam. Salam in makilat, mawzunat, ma'dudat, and madhru'at is valid because if their attributes and weight are specified, sufficient determination occurs and no dispute will arise. For those things that cannot be specified by attributes, salam is not valid. There is proof for this in the hadith: from Ibn Abbas ... he said: 'Whoever gives salam in something, let it be with a known measure, known weight, and known term' (Bukhari). In this hadith, 'known measure' indicates the commodity should be makil, and 'known weight' indicates it should be mawzun. And for cloth, there is this athar: from Ibn Abbas regarding salam in cotton cloth: 'If it is with a known cubit and a known term, then there is no harm' (Baihaqi, Ibn Abi Shaybah). From this athar, it is learned that cloth which is measured by hand can be sold via salam. And on this, countable things are analogized. For the permissibility of salam in numbers, there is this hadith: 'He would take one camel for two camels until the camels of sadaqah came' (Abu Dawood). In this hadith, the Prophet took one camel for two camels, indicating salam in numbers. Among weighed things are dirhams and danani? Their salam is not valid because they cannot be specified by attributes. So by mawzunat are meant things that are weighed but not dirhams and danani? like iron etc. Cloth. Things that can be specified by attributes, salam in them is valid. al-jawz: walnuts. al-bayd: eggs. al-madhru'at: derived from dhira', something measured by hand or cubit, like cloth.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents the first ruling in Bab al-Salam: the types of commodities in which salam is valid. The author lists four categories: (1) makilat (things measured by volume, e.g., wheat, rice); (2) mawzunat (things weighed, e.g., iron, but excluding gold and silver coins like dirhams and dinars because they cannot be sufficiently specified by attributes); (3) ma'dudat (things counted, whose individual units do not vary significantly, e.g., walnuts, eggs); (4) madhru'at (things measured by length/cubit, e.g., cloth). The key principle is that salam is valid only for goods that can be precisely described through attributes (sifat) to eliminate uncertainty (gharar). The author provides proofs: the hadith of Ibn Abbas specifies measure and weight; an athar from Ibn Abbas allows salam in cloth with a known cubit; and a hadith about exchanging camels indicates Salam's permissibility in counted items. The exception of dirhams and dinars from mawzunat is highlighted because their value depends on intrinsic worth and cannot be fixed by description alone.

Key Terms
مكيلات (makilat): Commodities measured by volume (e.g., wheat, rice).
موزونات (mawzunat): Commodities weighed (e.g., iron), excluding gold and silver coins.
معدودات (ma'dudat): Countable items whose individual units do not differ significantly (e.g., walnuts, eggs).
مذروعات (madhru'at): Things measured by length/cubit (e.g., cloth).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are dirhams and dinars excluded from the mawzunat (weighed items) in which salam is valid?
A) Because they are not truly weighed.
B) Because their value cannot be sufficiently specified by attributes.
C) Because they are prohibited in all types of salam.
D) Because they are subject to riba.

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid in makilat, mawzunat (excluding gold/silver), ma'dudat with negligible variation, and madhru'at because these can be precisely described to avoid uncertainty.

Invalid Salam: Animals, Parts, and Skins
Prohibits salam in animals and animal parts due to difficulty in specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in animals and their parts, and explain the rational basis for its invalidity based on difficulty of specification.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is invalid because their intrinsic unquantifiable differences prevent full specification, leading to uncertainty.

In this lesson, we examine the second invalid category for salam contracts: animals, their body parts, and skins. The Hanafi school holds that such salam is impermissible due to the inherent variation among animals that cannot be adequately captured by attribute description. This ruling is based on a rational (aqlī) principle that salam requires precise specification to avoid future disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Transactions
Read the passage to recognize that salam in animals (hayawan), their body parts (atraf), and skins (khaal) is declared invalid.
Note that the prohibition extends to all these categories.
2
Locate the Rational Proof (Dalīl 'Aqlī)
Find the explanation: two cows that appear similar can differ in milk yield, offspring, etc. This demonstrates that specification by external attributes alone is insufficient.
This is the core argument: unquantifiable differences cause uncertainty (gharar).
3
Apply the Principle of Precise Specification
Understand that salam requires the subject matter to be fully specified by measure, weight, or count. Animals fail this condition.
Contrast with salam in uniform goods like grains or metals.
4
Recognize the Scope and Exceptions
Note that the ruling covers all animals, their parts, and skins. Also, selling a specific animal (ayn) is not salam and is permissible.
Salam is a forward contract for a generic liability, not for a specific item.

Source Text

[۹۵۳) (۲) اور نہیں جائز ہے سلم حیوان میں اور نہ اس کے اطراف میں اور نہ کھال میں گن کر ۔

قیمت ابھی ادا کرے اور حیوان کی ساری صفات متعین کر کے اس کو مثلا مہینہ بعد میں لے اور اس میں بیع سلم کرے۔ اسی طرح حیوان کے مثلا سر، پاؤں وغیرہ کی بیع سلم کرے یعنی اس کے صفات ابھی متعین کرے اور مہینہ بعد دینے کی بیع کرے یا اس کی کھال میں بیع سلم کرے تو حنفیہ کے نزدیک یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔
دو حیوانوں کے درمیان بہت فرق ہوتا ہے۔ بعض مرتبہ ظاہری طور پر دو گائے ایک جیسی ہو جائے گی لیکن ایک گائے زیادہ دودھ دے گی اور دوسری کم ، ایک زیادہ بچے دے گی اور دوسری کم ، اس اعتبار سے معنوی طور پر دو گائے میں بہت تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے جانور میں صفت متعین کرنا مشکل ہے۔ اسی طرح دو گالیوں کے سر اور پاؤں میں بھی بہت فرق رہتا ہے۔ اور اس کی کھال کے بڑے چھوٹے ہونے میں فرق
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے کسی چیز میں بیع سلم کی توکیل معلوم ہو، وزن معلوم ہو اور مدت معلوم ہو ( ب ) حضرت ابن عباس سے منقول ہے کہ سوت کے کپڑے میں مسلم کے بارے میں فرمایا اگرگز معلوم ہو اور مدت معلوم ہو تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ج) آپ نے ایک اونٹ دو اونٹ کے بدلے میں لیتے
صدقہ کے اونٹ آنے تک۔
[953] (2) And salam is not valid in animals (hayawan), nor in their body parts, nor in skins by count. He pays the price immediately and specifies all attributes of the animal to take it after a month, for example, and makes salam in it. Similarly, salam in the animal's head, feet, etc. means specifying attributes now and making a sale for delivery after a month, or salam in its skin, then according to the Hanafis this is not valid. There is a great difference between two animals. Sometimes two cows appear similar externally, but one cow gives more milk and the other less; one gives more offspring and the other less; in this respect, there is great disparity between two cows meaningfully. Therefore, specifying attributes in animals is difficult. Similarly, there is much difference in the heads and feet of two cows, and in the size of their skins. Footnotes: (a) The Prophet said: Whoever makes salam in something, let it be with known measure, known weight, and known term. (b) From Ibn Abbas regarding salam in cotton cloth: If it is with a known cubit and a known term, there is no harm. (c) He took one camel for two camels until the camels of sadaqah came.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents the second ruling: salam is invalid in animals (hayawan), their body parts (e.g., head, feet), and their skins, whether counted or not. The reasoning is rational: animals vary greatly in their intrinsic qualities (milk yield, fertility, size) such that even if external attributes are specified, significant unquantifiable differences remain, leading to potential dispute. Similarly, body parts and skins are subject to variation in size and quality that cannot be adequately described by attributes alone. The Hanafi position is that salam is only valid for goods that can be precisely defined through quantitative measures (volume, weight, length, or count for uniform items). Since animals and their parts do not satisfy this condition, salam in them is impermissible. The footnotes repeat the earlier hadith about salam with known measure and weight, reinforcing the principle.

Key Terms
حيوان (hayawan): Animal, including all types of livestock and other creatures.
اطراف (atraf): Body parts of an animal, such as head, feet, etc.
كھال (khaal): Skin of the animal, whether tanned or raw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is salam in animals invalid even if all external attributes are specified?
A) Because animals are not valued in weight.
B) Because animals cannot be counted.
C) Because animals have intrinsic, unquantifiable differences that prevent full specification.
D) Because animals are considered perishable goods.

Key Takeaway
Salam in animals is invalid because their intrinsic unquantifiable differences cause uncertainty, violating the requirement of precise specification in forward contracts.

Prohibition of Salam in Animals, Limbs, and Skins
Ruling with proof prohibiting salam in animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in animals and explain why it is prohibited, using the hadith of Samurah and the principle of gharar.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is void because they cannot be standardized, and the Prophet forbade credit sale of animals.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the Hanafi school on salam (forward sale) regarding animals, their limbs, and skins. The Hanafis hold that salam is impermissible in these items due to the inherent uncertainty in specifying their attributes. We will explore the textual evidence from the hadith of Samurah, the reasoning behind the ruling, and the contrasting view of Imam al-Shafi'i. By the end, you will understand the methodological basis for the Hanafi position and how it protects against contractual disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
The passage states that salam is not permissible in animals, their limbs (e.g., head, feet), or skins when counted. Note the three categories and understand they are all subject to the same prohibition due to common cause: difficulty in standardization.
The Arabic uses 'لا يجوز' indicating prohibition (makruh tahrimi).
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Samurah: the Prophet ﷺ forbade selling an animal for another animal on credit (nesi'ah). Since salam involves deferred delivery, it falls under this prohibition.
Reference: Sunan al-Tirmidhi no. 1237; Sunan Abi Dawud no. 3356.
3
Understand the Rationale (Gharar)
Beyond the text, the Hanafis reason that animals cannot be fully standardized by attributes. Even if you specify type, age, and color, intrinsic qualities (milk yield, temperament) remain unknown, leading to uncertainty (gharar) and potential disputes.
This is a core principle: items eligible for salam must be objectively measurable by weight, measure, or count.
4
Examine the Shafi'i Objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that animals can be sufficiently defined by attributes, and he cites the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet took one camel for two camels on credit as a precedent for salam in animals.
The Shafi'i position is that salam in animals is valid if all attributes are specified.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis respond that the hadith of Ibn Umar is a specific case of loan (qard) or istisna', not a general license for salam. The explicit prohibition from Samurah takes precedence. The school's position is mufta bihi due to stronger evidence and precaution against gharar.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis rule invalid; Shafi'is rule valid if attributes specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۵۳] (۲) ولا يجوز السلم فى الحيوان ولا في اطرافه ولا في الجلود عددا
ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ... فـقـال مـن اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب السلم فی وزن معلوم ص ۲۹۸ نمبر ۲۲۴۰) اس حدیث میں کیل معلوم سے پتہ چلا کہ چیز کیلی ہو، اور وزن معلوم سے پتہ چلا کہ چیز وزنی ہو۔ اور کپڑے کے بیع سلم کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابن عباس في السلف في الكرابيس قال اذا كان ذراع مـعـلـوم الـى اجل معلوم فلا بأس (ب) ( سنن البيهقي ، باب السلف في المحطة والشعير والزبيب والزيت والثياب وجميع ما يضبط بالصفة ج سادس ص ۴۲ نمبر ۱۱۲۳ار مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۷۳افی السلم بالثیاب، ج رابع ، ص ۳۹۸، نمبر۲۱۴۰۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کپڑا جو ہاتھ سے ناپا جاتا ہے اس کی بیع سلم ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور اس پر عددی چیزوں کو قیاس کر لیں ۔ عددی میں بیع سلم جائز ہونے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فكان يأخذ البعير بالبعيرين الى ابل الصدقة (ج) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب في الرخصة في ذلك یعنی باب في الحيوان بالحيوان نسی ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۳۳۵۷) اس حدیث میں آپ نے ایک اونٹ کو دو اونٹ کے بدلے لیا ہے۔ جس سے عددی چیزوں میں بیع سلم کا پتہ چلتا وزنی میں درہم اور دنانی بھی ہیں۔ ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ ان کے صفات متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے ۔ اس لئے وزنی سے وہ چیزیں مراد ہیں جو وزن کی جاتی ہوں لیکن درہم اور دنا نیر نہ ہوں۔ جیسے لوہا وغیرہ۔
کپڑا۔
صفات متعین کرنے کے ذریعہ جو چیزیں متعین کی جاتی ہو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔ الجوز : اخروٹ ۔ البيض : انڈا۔ المزروعات : ذراع سے مشتق ہے، جو چیز ہاتھ سے ناپی جاتی ہو یا گز سے ناپی جاتی ہو جیسے
[۹۵۳) (۲) اور نہیں جائز ہے سلم حیوان میں اور نہ اس کے اطراف میں اور نہ کھال میں گن کر ۔
قیمت ابھی ادا کرے اور حیوان کی ساری صفات متعین کر کے اس کو مثلا مہینہ بعد میں لے اور اس میں بیع سلم کرے۔ اسی طرح حیوان کے مثلا سر، پاؤں وغیرہ کی بیع سلم کرے یعنی اس کے صفات ابھی متعین کرے اور مہینہ بعد دینے کی بیع کرے یا اس کی کھال میں بیع سلم کرے تو حنفیہ کے نزدیک یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔
دو حیوانوں کے درمیان بہت فرق ہوتا ہے۔ بعض مرتبہ ظاہری طور پر دو گائے ایک جیسی ہو جائے گی لیکن ایک گائے زیادہ دودھ دے گی اور دوسری کم ، ایک زیادہ بچے دے گی اور دوسری کم ، اس اعتبار سے معنوی طور پر دو گائے میں بہت تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے جانور میں صفت متعین کرنا مشکل ہے۔ اسی طرح دو گالیوں کے سر اور پاؤں میں بھی بہت فرق رہتا ہے۔ اور اس کی کھال کے بڑے چھوٹے ہونے میں فرق حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے کسی چیز میں بیع سلم کی توکیل معلوم ہو، وزن معلوم ہو اور مدت معلوم ہو ( ب ) حضرت ابن عباس سے منقول ہے کہ سوت کے کپڑے میں مسلم کے بارے میں فرمایا اگرگز معلوم ہو اور مدت معلوم ہو تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ج) آپ نے ایک اونٹ دو اونٹ کے بدلے میں لیتے صدقہ کے اونٹ آنے تک۔
ولا في الجلود عددا [۹۵۴] (۳) ولا فى الحطب حزما ولا فى الرطبة جرزا [۹۵۵](۴) ہوتا ہے۔ اور نزاع کا خطرہ رہتا ہے۔ اس لئے جانور ، اس کے اعضاء اور اس کی کھال میں بیع سلم جائز نہیں (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن سمرة ان النبى الله نهي عن بيع الحيوان بالحيوان نسيئة (الف) (ترندى شريف، باب ما جاء فی کراہیتہ بیع الحیوان بالحيوان نسید یه ص ۲۳۳ نمبر ۱۲۳۷ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب الحيوان بالحیوان نسی یه ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۳۳۵۶) اس حدیث میں حیوان کو ادھار بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور بیع سلم ادھار ہوتی ہے اس لئے بیع سلم حیوان میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ چونکہ اس کے اعضاء اور اس کی کھال بھی حیوان کے اجزاء ہیں اس لئے ان میں بھی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔
اصول جن چیزوں کو صفات کے ذریعہ متعین نہیں کر سکتے ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک جانور کی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔
(۱) وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جانور کی تمام صفات اور عمر وغیرہ متعین کر دی جائیں تو کافی حد تک متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے جانور ، اس کے اعضاء اور کھال کی بیع سلم جائز ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد اللہ بن عمر ان رسول الله امره ان يجهز جيشا فنفدت الابل فامره ان يأخذ في قلاص الصدقة فكان يأخذ البعير بالبعيرين الى ابل الصدقة (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في الرخصة في ذلك ( ای فی بیع الحیوان بالحيوان نسیئة ) ص ۱۲۱، نمبر ۳۳۵۷ را بو داؤد ، باب فی حسن القضاء ص ۱۹ نمبر ۳۳۴۶) اس حدیث میں آپ نے ایک اونٹ کے بدلے دو اونٹ دیکر ادھار خریدا ہے جو بیع سلم کی شکل ہے اس لئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک حیوان میں بیع سلم جائز ہے اطراف : طرف کی جمع ہے اعضاء جلود : جلد کی جمع ہے کھال - عددا : گن کر ۔
And salam is not permissible in animals, nor in their limbs, nor in skins by count. [Understanding from hadith: Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet said: 'Whoever gives salam in something, then it must be in a known measure, known weight, up to a known term.' This hadith shows that the item must be measurable by weight or measure. For cloth, there is an athar from Ibn Abbas about salam in cotton cloth: 'If it is by a known cubit up to a known term, then there is no harm.' This shows salam is permissible in cloth measured by hand/cubit. Analogically, countable items are also permissible. The hadith 'He used to take a camel for two camels up to the camels of sadaqah' indicates salam in countable items. Among weighty items are dirhams and danaq; their salam is not permissible because specifying attributes does not sufficiently define them. So 'weighty' refers to things weighed but not dirhams and danaq, like iron. Cloth. Through specifying attributes, items that can be defined are permissible for salam. Al-jawz: walnuts; al-bayd: eggs; al-madhrurat: derived from dhira', meaning something measured by hand or yard like cloth. (2) And salam is not permissible in animals, nor in their limbs, nor in skins by count. The buyer pays the price now and specifies all attributes of the animal to be delivered after a month. Similarly, salam in the head, feet etc. of an animal, or in its skin, is not permissible according to the Hanafis. The difference between two animals is great; sometimes two cows appear similar but one gives more milk, the other less, so specifying attributes is difficult. Similarly, heads and feet of two sheep differ greatly, and skins vary in size. Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: 'If someone gives salam in something, then in a known measure, known weight, and known term.' (b) It is narrated from Ibn Abbas about salam in cotton cloth: 'If it is a known cubit and a known term, there is no problem.' (c) He took one camel for two camels until the camels of sadaqah came. And not in skins by count. (3) And not in firewood by bundles, nor in vegetables by bunches. [955] (4) ... There is risk of dispute. Therefore salam in animals, their parts, and their skins is not permissible. The proof is the hadith of Samurah: 'The Prophet forbade the sale of animal for animal on credit.' (Tirmidhi, no. 1237; Abu Dawud, no. 3356). This hadith prohibits selling animals on credit, and salam is a credit sale, so salam in animals is impermissible. Since limbs and skins are parts of the animal, their salam is also impermissible. Principle: Items that cannot be defined through attributes are not valid for salam. Imam Shafi'i holds that salam in animals is permissible: he argues that specifying all attributes and age sufficiently defines the animal, so salam in animals, limbs, and skins is permissible. His proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah ordered him to prepare an army, and the camels were exhausted, so he ordered him to take from the young camels of sadaqah, and he would take one camel for two camels until the camels of sadaqah arrived.' (Abu Dawud, no. 3357, 3346). In this hadith, he bought one camel on credit for two camels, which is a form of salam. Therefore, according to Imam Shafi'i, salam in animals is permissible. Atraf is plural of taraf, limbs; julud is plural of jild, skin; addadan: by count.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the Hanafi school prohibiting salam in animals, their limbs, and their skins. The reasoning is that the attributes of animals cannot be sufficiently standardized; two animals may look alike but differ in qualities like milk yield, strength, etc. The hadith of Samurah explicitly forbids selling animals on credit, and salam is a form of credit sale, so the prohibition applies. The passage also presents the Shafi'i position and its proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, but the Hanafi response is implicit: the hadith about taking a camel for two camels is interpreted as a specific loan, not a general authorization of salam in animals. The Hanafi principle is that salam is only valid in commodities that can be precisely defined by measure, weight, or count, excluding things like animals where standardization is impossible. This is a clear example of how the Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas, as the Shafi'i analogical reasoning is rejected due to the inherent uncertainty.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later, also known as bai' as-salam.
اطراف (atraf): Limbs of an animal, such as head, feet, etc.
جلود (julud): Skins of animals, counted by number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is salam in animals not permissible?
A) Because animals are not measured by weight or measure.
B) Because the Prophet forbade selling animals on credit.
C) Because animals cannot be fully standardized in attributes, leading to uncertainty.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis prohibit salam in animals due to the explicit hadith and the principle that objects of salam must be objectively measurable without significant uncertainty.

Salam in Firewood and Vegetables: The Requirement of Known Quantity
States the prohibition of salam for imprecise units.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in firewood by bundles and vegetables by bunches, and identify the condition that makes such salam invalid.

Core Idea
Salam requires precise knowledge of quantity; bundles and bunches are ambiguous, so salam is invalid.

In Hanafi fiqh, a salam contract (forward sale) is valid only when the subject matter is precisely specified, especially its quantity. This lesson examines two prohibited cases: firewood sold by bundles and vegetables sold by bunches. The reasoning is straightforward—these units lack consistent measurement, introducing uncertainty (gharar). We will also see an exception when items are machine-cut to uniformity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the passage. The act is salam (advance payment sale) in firewood by bundles (hazman) and in vegetables by bunches (jirzan). The ruling: it is not permissible (la yajuz).
The prohibition is clear and relates to the manner of sale, not the commodity itself.
2
Recall the general conditions of salam
Salam requires that the subject matter be specified in quantity (known weight or measure) and quality. The hadith cited requires 'known measure, known weight'.
This principle is well-established in Hanafi buyu' (sales) and is derived from Sahih Bukhari.
3
Apply the condition to the given items
Firewood bundles and vegetable bunches are not standard; a bundle may vary in size. Thus the quantity is unknown, and the condition fails. Therefore salam is invalid.
The ambiguity (jahalah) leads to gharar, which is prohibited.
4
Recognize the exception
The passage notes that if firewood is machine-cut into uniform pieces, then salam becomes valid because the quantity can be precisely determined (e.g., by count or weight).
This shows the ruling is based on the underlying cause ('illa): uncertainty in quantity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۵۴] (۳) ولا فى الحطب حزما ولا فى الرطبة جرزا [۹۵۵](۴) اور نہیں جائز ہے بیع سلم لکڑی کی گھر کے اعتبار سے اور نہ سبزیوں میں گڑیوں کے اعتبار سے۔ ا ایندھن کی لکڑیوں کا گھر بناتے ہیں اور بیچتے ہیں، بعض گھر میں زیادہ لکڑی ہوتی ہے اور بعض میں کم ۔ بالکل ایک طرح کا گھر نہیں بن پاتا اس لئے اس کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں۔ اسی طرح سبزیاں اور ساگ کا گڑا بناتے ہیں اس میں بھی سبزی کسی میں کم آتی ہے کسی میں زیادہ اس لئے اس کی بھی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اگر مشین سے ایک طرح کی لکڑی کائی جائے اور اس کی بیع سلم کرے تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ صفات کی تعیین ہوگئی ۔ اصول اور دلائل اوپر گزر گئے۔ حدیث میں تھا کہ کیل معلوم ، وزن معلوم ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۲۲۴۰) اور یہاں مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے کتنا ہے اس لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ الحطب : ایندھن کی لکڑی۔ حزما : گھر - الرطبة : سبزی- حرز : جمع ہے حرزہ کی گڈی۔۔
(3) And not in firewood by bundles, nor in vegetables by bunches. (4) Salam is not permissible in firewood by bundles and not in vegetables by bunches. Firewood is bundled and sold; some bundles have more wood, some less; an exact identical bundle cannot be made. Therefore salam in it is not permissible. Similarly, vegetables and greens are tied into bunches; some bunches have less, some more; therefore salam is not permissible. If machine-cut uniform pieces of wood are used, then salam is permissible because attributes are specified. The principles and proofs have passed earlier: the hadith states 'a known measure, a known weight' (Bukhari no. 2240), and here the quantity is not known exactly, so it is not permissible. Al-hatab: firewood; hazman: bundles; ar-ratbah: vegetables; jirz: plural of jirzah, a bunch.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school prohibiting salam in firewood sold by bundles and vegetables sold by bunches. The reasoning is that these are not precisely quantifiable; bundles and bunches vary in size and cannot be standardized. The underlying principle applied is that salam requires exact specification of quantity (known measure or weight). Since bundles and bunches do not provide that, salam is invalid. An exception is made if the items are machine-cut to uniform size, as then the quantity can be standardized. This ruling is derived from the general hadith requiring known measure and weight.

Key Terms
حطب (hatab): Firewood, fuel wood.
حزما (hazman): By bundles, referring to the manner of sale.
رطبة (ratbah): Fresh vegetables or greens.
جرزا (jirzan): By bunches, plural of jirzah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam in firewood by bundles invalid according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because firewood is not a common commodity.
B) Because the quantity cannot be precisely specified; bundles vary in size.
C) Because firewood is usually sold by weight.
D) Because the hadith prohibits salam in combustible materials.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires exact quantification; any uncertainty in the unit of sale renders the contract invalid.

Condition of Existence in Salam
States a condition for salam validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that the subject matter in salam must exist from contract to delivery and explain why non-existence at either point invalidates the contract.

Core Idea
Salam requires continuous existence of goods from contract to delivery — non-existence at any point invalidates the contract.

This lesson introduces a key condition for the validity of a salam contract: the goods (muslam fīh) must exist at the time the contract is made and continue to exist until delivery. This condition distinguishes salam from ordinary sales and prevents uncertainty (gharar). Understanding this rule will help you evaluate whether a given salam contract is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
First, recognise that salam is a forward sale where the price is paid now and the goods are delivered later. The condition stated is that the subject matter must exist from the moment of contract until delivery.
The condition is a shart (condition) of validity, not a pillar.
2
Understand the temporal scope
The existence must be continuous: at the time of contract (at the moment you pay) and at every moment until delivery. If the goods exist at contract but perish before delivery, the contract becomes invalid.
This prevents salam in goods that are not yet in existence (e.g., next season's crops) or are likely to perish.
3
Relate to the underlying rationale
The condition avoids gharar (uncertainty) because the buyer is paying upfront for something that must be deliverable. Without continuous existence, the buyer risks paying for something that may never materialise.
This is unique to salam; normal sales require existence only at delivery.
4
Apply the condition to scenarios
Now test the condition: salam in stored wheat is valid because it exists at contract and will continue to exist. Salam in next month's fruit harvest is invalid because the fruit does not exist at contract. Salam in factory-ordered goods that will be manufactured later is valid only if the raw materials already exist.
The existence condition also applies to the source of the goods (e.g., a mine that is operational).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۵۵] (۴) ولا يجوز سلم حتى يكون المسلم فيه موجودا من وقت العقد إلى وقت التسليم
اور نہیں جائز ہے سلم یہاں تک کہ مسلم فیہ موجود ہو عقد کے وقت سے دینے کے وقت تک۔
(4) And salam is not permissible unless the subject matter (al-muslam fīh) is existent from the time of contract to the time of delivery. And salam is not permissible until the subject matter is present from the time of contract to the time of delivery.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a ruling stating a fundamental condition of salam: the goods (muslam fīh) must exist from the moment the contract is made until the delivery date. This means that the goods cannot be something that is non-existent at the time of contract or will cease to exist before delivery. For example, salam in fruit that is not yet in season is invalid because it does not exist at contract time. The Hanafi school requires that the goods be available in the market at the time of delivery, but this condition specifically emphasizes continuous existence. This condition distinguishes salam from other contracts like istisna, where the goods are manufactured later.

Key Terms
مسلم فيه (muslam fīh): The subject matter of the salam contract, i.e., the goods to be delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following salam contracts would be invalid due to the condition of existence?
A) Salam in wheat that is already harvested and stored.
B) Salam in dates that will be harvested next season.
C) Salam in copper that is mined and in stock.
D) Salam in cloth that is in the merchant's warehouse.

Key Takeaway
The subject matter in salam must exist continuously from the moment of contract until delivery; non-existence at either point renders the contract invalid.

Salam in Animals: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on salam in animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi prohibition of salam in animals and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is invalid due to gharar; specification by attributes is insufficient in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of salam (advance payment sale) in animals, their body parts, and hides. The Hanafi school prohibits it based on the principle that animals cannot be sufficiently specified, leading to uncertainty. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if all attributes are detailed, the animal becomes adequately defined. Understanding this dispute reveals how different schools weigh textual evidence and legal principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school rules salam in animals, their parts, and hides as not permissible (invalid).
The ruling is based on the inability to fully specify the animal.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i permits salam in animals if all relevant attributes (species, age, color, etc.) are specified.
This is a direct opposition to the Hanafi view.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Examine the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, where the Prophet arranged an exchange of one camel for two camels on credit, which the Shafi'i school interprets as a salam transaction.
The Shafi'i school also relies on the principle that specification removes uncertainty.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand that the Hanafi school uses the hadith of Samurah prohibiting selling animals for animals on credit, and considers the Ibn Umar hadith as a loan (qard) or an exception, not a general permissibility.
The Hanafi school also invokes the principle of gharar (uncertainty).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: a Hanafi mufti would reject a salam contract for livestock, while a Shafi'i mufti would accept it if attributes are specified.
This difference impacts real estate, agriculture, and commerce practices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا في الجلود عددا [۹۵۴] (۳) ولا فى الحطب حزما ولا فى الرطبة جرزا (۹۵۵](۴) ہوتا ہے۔ اور نزاع کا خطرہ رہتا ہے۔ اس لئے جانور ، اس کے اعضاء اور اس کی کھال میں بیع سلم جائز نہیں (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن سمرة ان النبى الله نهي عن بيع الحيوان بالحيوان نسيئة (الف) (ترندى شريف، باب ما جاء فی کراہیتہ بیع الحیوان بالحيوان نسید یه ص ۲۳۳ نمبر ۱۲۳۷ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب الحيوان بالحیوان نسی یه ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۳۳۵۶) اس حدیث میں حیوان کو ادھار بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور بیع سلم ادھار ہوتی ہے اس لئے بیع سلم حیوان میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ چونکہ اس کے اعضاء اور اس کی کھال بھی حیوان کے اجزاء ہیں اس لئے ان میں بھی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔
اصول جن چیزوں کو صفات کے ذریعہ متعین نہیں کر سکتے ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک جانور کی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔
(۱) وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جانور کی تمام صفات اور عمر وغیرہ متعین کر دی جائیں تو کافی حد تک متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے جانور ، اس کے اعضاء اور کھال کی بیع سلم جائز ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد اللہ بن عمر ان رسول الله امره ان يجهز جيشا فنفدت الابل فامره ان يأخذ في قلاص الصدقة فكان يأخذ البعير بالبعيرين الى ابل الصدقة (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في الرخصة في ذلك ( ای فی بیع الحیوان بالحيوان نسیئة ) ص ۱۲۱، نمبر ۳۳۵۷ را بو داؤد ، باب فی حسن القضاء ص ۱۹ نمبر ۳۳۴۶) اس حدیث میں آپ نے ایک اونٹ کے بدلے دو اونٹ دیکر ادھار خریدا ہے جو بیع سلم کی شکل ہے اس لئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک حیوان میں بیع سلم جائز ہے اطراف : طرف کی جمع ہے اعضاء جلود : جلد کی جمع ہے کھال - عددا : گن کر ۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے روکا حیوان کو حیوان کی بیع سے ادھار (ب) آپ نے حکم دیا کہ لشکر تیار کرے۔ پس اونٹ ختم ہو گئے تو آپ نے حکم دیا کہ صدقہ کے جوان اونٹ لے لیں تو ایک اونٹ کو دو اونٹ کے بدلے لئے صدقہ کے اونٹ آنے تک۔
And not in hides by count. [954] (3) And not in firewood by bundle, nor in fresh greens by handful. [955] (4) There is a risk of dispute. Therefore, salam sale of an animal, its parts, and its skin is not permissible. (2) There is proof for this in the hadith: From Samurah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of an animal for an animal on credit. (a) (Tirmidhi, Bab...; Abu Dawud, Bab...) This hadith prohibits selling animals on credit. Since salam is a credit sale, salam in animals is not permissible. Because its parts and skin are also parts of the animal, salam in them is also not permissible.
The principle: Things that cannot be specified through attributes are not permissible in salam.
According to Imam al-Shafi'i, salam in animals is permissible.
(1) He says that if all the attributes of the animal, its age etc. are specified, it becomes sufficiently determined. Therefore, salam in animals, their parts, and hides is permissible. (2) There is proof in the hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered him to equip an army, and the camels were exhausted, so he ordered him to take from the young camels of sadaqah, and he would take one camel for two camels until the camels of sadaqah came. (b) (Abu Dawud, Bab...) In this hadith, he bought one camel for two camels on credit, which is a form of salam. Therefore, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, salam in animals is permissible.
Atraf: plural of taraf, meaning limbs. Julud: plural of jild, meaning hide. 'Adadan: by count.
Footnote (a): He prohibited the sale of an animal for an animal on credit. (b) He commanded to prepare an army. Then the camels were exhausted, so he commanded to take the young camels of sadaqah, and he took one camel for two camels until the camels of sadaqah came.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of salam (advance payment sale) in animals, their body parts, and hides. The author first states the Hanafi ruling: salam is not permissible in animals, their parts, or hides, based on a hadith from Samurah that prohibits selling animals for animals on credit. The underlying principle is that items that cannot be sufficiently specified by attributes cannot be sold via salam; animals have too many variables (age, health, size) that cannot be fully captured. Therefore, the Hanafi school extends this prohibition to the animal's parts and hide as they are part of the same category. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that if all relevant attributes and age are explicitly specified, the animal becomes adequately determined, making salam permissible. He supports his view with the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) arranged an exchange of one camel for two camels on credit, which resembles a salam transaction. The Hanafi response is not detailed here, but the text implies that the Hanafi school maintains the prohibition due to the general principle and the earlier hadith. The passage also clarifies the Arabic terms: 'atraf' (limbs), 'julud' (hides), and 'adadan' (by count).

Key Terms
سلم (salam): An advance payment sale where the price is paid immediately and the commodity is delivered later, also known as 'salam' or 'salaf'.
حیوان (hayawān): Animal; living creature. In this context, it refers to livestock or animals sold for their meat, milk, or hide.
جلود (julūd): Hides; plural of jild (skin). Refers to animal skins used for leather.
عددا (adadan): By count; specifying an item by number rather than weight or measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school prohibits salam in animals, as explained in the passage?
A) Animals are not considered property.
B) Animals cannot be fully specified by attributes, leading to gharar.
C) Salam is only for fungible goods.
D) The Prophet explicitly forbade salam in animals.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits salam in animals due to the inability to specify them fully, avoiding gharar, while the Shafi'i school permits it if attributes are detailed.

Salam in Firewood and Vegetables
Ruling that salam is invalid in firewood and vegetables due to lack of precise specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam for firewood sold by bundle and vegetables sold by handful, and identify the condition that makes salam valid (known quantity).

Core Idea
Salam requires a known quantity; bundles and handfuls are uncertain, so salam in them is invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on salam contracts for firewood and vegetables. The key issue is uncertainty (jahalah) in quantity. The passage explains why salam is impermissible in these cases and notes an exception when the wood is uniformly cut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a salam contract for firewood by bundle or vegetables by handful. The ruling is that such a salam is not permissible (jāʾiz nahī).
2
Identify the condition violated
The condition violated is that the quantity must be known exactly (by measure or weight). Bundles and handfuls vary, so the quantity is unknown at contract formation.
3
Note the exception
If firewood is machine-cut to uniform size, salam is permissible because the quantity can be specified.
The exception confirms that the issue is uncertainty, not the nature of the item.
4
Connect to the general principle
The requirement of known quantity is derived from the hadith: 'with a known measure, a known weight' (Bukhari no. 2240).

(1954) (3) And salam is not permissible for firewood by bundle, nor for vegetables by handful. They make bundles of firewood and sell them; some bundles have more wood and some less. They cannot be made completely uniform, so salam in them is not permissible. Similarly, they make handfuls of vegetables and greens; in some, there are more vegetables, in some less, so salam in them is also not permissible. If machine-cut uniform wood is used and salam is contracted for it, it is permissible because the attributes have been specified. The principles and proofs have preceded. The hadith stated: 'with a known measure, a known weight' (Bukhari no. 2240), and here the quantity is not known how much it is, so it is not permissible.
Al-hatab: firewood. Hazman: bundle. Ar-ratbah: vegetables. Hizr: plural of huzrah, meaning handful.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage states a ruling that salam is not permissible for firewood sold in bundles or vegetables sold in handfuls. The reason is that these items cannot be standardized; bundles and handfuls vary in quantity, leading to uncertainty (gharar). The author explains that some bundles/ handfuls contain more and some less, so the exact quantity is unknown at the time of contract. This violates the general principle recorded in a hadith (Bukhari) that salam requires a known measure or weight. An exception is noted: if firewood is machine-cut to uniform size, then salam becomes permissible because the attributes are precisely known. This ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) to the general rule that unknown quantities invalidate salam. The terms are defined: 'hatab' (firewood), 'hazm' (bundle), 'ratbah' (fresh greens), 'hizr' (handful).

Key Terms
حطب (hatab): Firewood; wood used for fuel.
حزمة (huzmah): Bundle; a collection of sticks tied together.
رطبة (ratbah): Fresh greens; vegetables, especially leafy ones.
جرزة (jurzah): Handful; a small amount grasped by the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Condition of Existence of Subject Matter in Salam
Ruling with proof that salam is only valid if the subject matter exists continuously.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the continuous existence of the subject matter in salam, apply it to determine contract validity, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-position.

Core Idea
In salam, the subject matter must exist continuously from contract to delivery or the contract is invalid.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of salam (advance payment sale) in Hanafi fiqh: the subject matter must be available in the market from the time the contract is made until the time of delivery. The ruling is grounded in a hadith of Ibn Umar and differs from the Shafi'i school. Understanding this condition is essential for structuring valid salam contracts and avoiding gharar (uncertainty).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states that salam is not permissible unless the subject matter (muslam fihi) exists from the time of contract until the time of delivery. This is a condition (shart) for validity.
The condition is about continuous market availability, not physical possession by the seller.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade salam in palm trees until the fruit's condition becomes apparent. This hadith is the primary evidence.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud, Bukhari, and Ibn Majah.
3
Derive the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's prohibition 'Do not make salam in palm trees until their good condition becomes apparent' implies that at the time of contract, the subject matter must be in a state that assures existence. If it is not yet apparent, the salam is invalid.
Hanafi jurists interpret this as requiring existence (at least potential) at contract time.
4
Contrast the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that existence at delivery is sufficient. The passage explains his reasoning: the purpose of salam is to deliver at a future date, so market availability at contract is not necessary.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Hanafi prohibits out-of-season salam; Shafi'i allows it.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario, determine validity using the Hanafi condition. For example, salam for wheat that is in season at contract is valid; salam for out-of-season fruit is invalid even if it will be in season later.
Always check if the commodity is available in the market throughout the period.

امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دینے کے وقت طبیع بازار میں ملتی ہو تب بھی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔

And salam is not permissible unless the subject matter (muslam fihi) exists from the time of the contract until the time of delivery. [956] (5) From here begins the explanation of the conditions for the validity of salam. One condition is that salam is permissible for something that is present in the market and available from the time of contract until the day the commodity is to be delivered. If that thing is not found in the market at all, then salam is not permissible. Or if it will be available at the time of delivery but is not present in the market now, and there is a strong possibility that it will disappear from the market in between, even then salam is not permissible. If one makes salam for something not available in the market, what will he give to the customer at the due time? And how will he make his money halal? Therefore, it is prohibited. (2) There is a hadith prohibiting salam for something that is not available in the market. From Ibn Umar: A man made salam with another concerning palm trees, but that year nothing came out. They complained to the Prophet (peace be upon him), who said, 'How will you make his property halal? Return his property.' Then he said, 'Do not make salam in palm trees until their good condition becomes apparent.' (a) (Abu Dawud, Bukhari, Ibn Majah) In this hadith, he said: if the original asset is not even present in the market, how will you sell? And how will you make the customer's property halal? Therefore, it is necessary that the property exists in the market. If the principal asset is at least available in the market, then salam will be permissible.
Imam al-Shafi'i says that if it is naturally available in the market at the time of delivery, then salam is permissible. It is sufficient that the commodity is present at the time of delivery, because it is at that time that the commodity is needed.
Al-muslam fihi: the commodity. Al-hill: the time of maturity, the time of delivery.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding a condition for the validity of salam: the subject matter (muslam fihi) must exist and be available in the market continuously from the time of contract until the time of delivery. The author explains the rationale: if the commodity is not available in the market, there is a risk that the seller will be unable to deliver, leading to uncertainty (gharar) and potential injustice. A hadith from Ibn Umar is cited: a man made salam for dates from a specific palm tree, but no fruit appeared that year. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the seller to return the money and forbade salam in such cases until the fruit's condition is clear (i.e., until it begins to ripen). This hadith is used as proof that the subject matter must exist (at least in the market) to avoid gambling with the customer's money. The passage also mentions a disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers it sufficient if the commodity is available at the time of delivery, even if not present at the time of contract. The Hanafi school insists on continuous availability to prevent potential failure to deliver. The terms 'muslam fihi' (subject matter) and 'hall' (time of maturity) are defined.

Key Terms
مسلم فيه (muslam fīhi): The subject matter of the salam contract; the commodity to be delivered in the future.
حل (محل) (hall / mahall): The time of maturity; the due date for delivery of the subject matter.
موجود (mawjūd): Existent; present in the market. The condition requires the commodity to be existent from contract to delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi salam, the subject matter must be available in the market from contract to delivery; otherwise, the contract is invalid due to gharar.

Conditions of Deferred Payment and Known Term in Salam
Ruling that salam must be deferred with a known term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a valid salam contract and distinguish the Hanafi position from Imam al-Shafi'i's view on the definition of salam.

Core Idea
Salam requires deferred delivery with a known term — without both, the contract is not salam.

Salam is a special forward sale essential for agricultural and trade needs. This passage clarifies two foundational conditions: that the delivery must be deferred (mu'ajjal) and the term must be known (ajal ma'loom). The author also notes a disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i on whether immediate delivery can be called salam. Understanding these conditions prevents disputes and ensures the contract's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two conditions
The act under discussion is the salam contract (forward sale). The passage states two conditions: the delivery must be deferred (mu'ajjal) and the term must be known (ajal ma'loom).
Without these conditions, the contract is not considered salam according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith 'ila ajalin ma'loom' (to a known term), reported by Bukhari and Muslim. This is the main textual evidence.
The hadith is ahad (singular) but its meaning is clear.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'to a known term' explicitly requires that the term be both fixed and known. This indicates that a salam contract without a specified term is invalid.
The imperative tone of the hadith implies necessity (wujub) of the condition.
4
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the word 'salam' is used, the contract can be considered salam even if delivery is immediate. The Hanafi school disagrees, stating that deferment is an essential characteristic.
The dispute revolves around the definition of salam: is it defined by form (utterance) or by substance (deferment)?
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, a contract with immediate delivery using the word 'salam' is treated as a regular spot sale (bay' al-'ayn). In the Shafi'i school, it remains a salam contract with zero term.
This difference affects rules like capital gains and risk allocation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصح السلم الا مؤجلا ولا يجوز الا باجل معلوم
بیع سلم کہتے ہی ہیں اس کو جس میں مبیع بعد میں دی جائے۔ اور اگر مبیع فوری دینے کی بات ہو تو اس کو بیع سلم نہیں کہیں گے۔ اس کو عام بیع اور بیع عین کہیں گے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مسلم کے الفاظ سے بیع کی ہو تو اس کو بھی بیع سلم کہہ سکتے ہیں۔ بیع سلم میں یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ مدت معلوم
(۱) ور نہ تو مشتری پہلے لینا چاہے گا اور بائع بعد میں دینا چاہے گا۔ اور جھگڑا ہو گا اس لئے مبیع دینے کی تاریخ طے ہونا ضروری ہے (۲)
حدیث میں گزرا الی اجل معلوم ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۲۲۴۰ ر مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۶۰۴) اس لئے مدت متعین ہونا ضروری ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی نے کھجور کے درخت کے بارے میں بیع سلم کی ۔ لیکن اس سال کوئی پھل نہیں آیا۔ تو دونوں حضور کے پاس جھگڑا لیکر آئے۔ آپ نے فرمایا اس کے مال کو کیسے حلال کرو گے؟ اس کے مال کو واپس کرو۔ پھر آپ نے فرمایا کھجور کے بارے میں بیع سلم نہ کرو جب تک کہ کار
آمد نہ ہو جائے۔
And salam is not valid except deferred, and it is not permissible except with a known term.
Salam is defined as a sale in which the commodity is delivered later. If the commodity is to be delivered immediately, it is not called salam; it is called a regular sale or spot sale.
Imam al-Shafi'i says that if the sale is made with the word 'salam', it can also be considered salam. In salam, it is also necessary that the term is known.
(1) Otherwise, the buyer will want to take early and the seller will want to deliver late, and there will be a dispute. Therefore, it is necessary to fix the date of delivery. (2) The hadith that passed: 'to a known term' (Bukhari no. 2240, Muslim no. 1604). Therefore, it is necessary to specify the term.
Footnote (a): Abdullah ibn Umar says that a man made salam with another concerning palm trees, but that year no fruit came. Both came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) with the dispute. He said, 'How will you make his property halal? Return his property.' Then he said, 'Do not make salam in palm trees until it becomes productive.'
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage states two related conditions: (1) salam must be a deferred sale (mu'ajjal), meaning the commodity is delivered later; if immediate delivery is intended, it is a regular sale, not salam. (2) The term of deferment must be known (ajal ma'loom) to avoid disputes. The author explains that if the term is not fixed, the buyer and seller may disagree on the delivery time, leading to conflict. Proof is provided from the hadith narrated by Bukhari and Muslim that salam is valid only 'to a known term' (ila ajalin ma'loom). A brief disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i is noted: al-Shafi'i considers that if the word 'salam' is used, even an immediate delivery sale might be called salam, but the Hanafi school restricts the term to deferred sales. The footnote repeats a hadith about palm trees, reinforcing the need for a known term and avoiding uncertainty.

Key Terms
مؤجلا (mu'ajjalan): Deferred; the delivery of the commodity is postponed to a future date.
أجل معلوم (ajal ma'lūm): A known, fixed term; the delivery date must be clearly specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is a necessary condition for the validity of a salam contract according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediate delivery of the commodity
B) The use of the word 'salam' in the contract
C) A known, fixed term for deferred delivery
D) The commodity must be gold or silver

Key Takeaway
Salam requires both deferred delivery and a known term; without these, the contract falls outside the definition of salam.

Continuous Availability of Commodity in Salam
Ruling on the continuous market availability of the muslam fih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of salam regarding commodity availability and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Salam requires the commodity to be available from contract to delivery; future availability alone is insufficient.

This lesson explains a key condition for the validity of a salam (forward sale) contract: the commodity (muslam fih) must be continuously available in the market from the time the contract is made until the delivery date. The Hanafi school considers this condition essential to avoid uncertainty (gharar) that could lead to disputes. We will examine the textual evidence from the hadith and the scholarly disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the subject is salam (forward sale) and the ruling is that it is invalid (fasid) if the commodity is not continuously available.
The ruling is not merely disliked but renders the contract defective.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith of Ibn Umar as the primary proof. Note its source and transmission.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but accepted in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Show how the Prophet's prohibition of salam in palm trees before they ripen proves that the commodity must exist and be ascertainable at contract time.
The key phrase is 'until they ripen' (حتى يبدو صلاحه) indicating the need for existence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds availability only at delivery is sufficient. Understand his reasoning.
The dispute is about the timing of availability, not the requirement itself.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is preferred: it prevents gharar and ensures the seller can guarantee delivery.
The Hanafi view is more precautionary and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز السلم حتى يكون المسلم فيه موجودا من حين العقد الى حين المحل
یہاں سے بیع سلم صحیح ہونے کے لئے اس کے شرائط کا بیان ہے۔ اس میں ایک شرط یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز کی بیع سلم جائز ہے جو عقد کے وقت سے جس دن مبیع مشتری کو دینا ہے اس وقت تک بازار میں موجود ہو اور ملتی ہو۔ اگر وہ چیز بازار میں بھی نہیں ملتی ہو تو بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ یا دینے کے دنوں ملے گی لیکن ابھی بازار میں نہیں ہے۔ درمیان میں بازار سے غائب ہونے کا قوی امکان ہے تب بھی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہوگی۔ جو چیز بازار میں ملتی نہیں ہے اس کی بیع سلم کر لیں تو وقت آنے پر مشتری کو کیا چیز دیں گے۔ اور کیسے اس کے روپے حلال کریں گے۔ اس لئے منع فرمایا (۲) حدیث میں ایسی چیز کی بیع سلم سے منع فرمایا جو بھی بازار میں نہیں ملتی ہو۔ عن ابن عمر ان رجلا اسلف رجلا في نخل فلم تخرج تلك السنة شيئا فاختصما الى النبي الا الله فقال بما تستحل ماله اردد عليه ماله ثم قال لا تسلفوا في النخل حتى يبدو صلاحه (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی السلم فی ثمرہ بعینها ص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۳۴۶۷ ر بخاری شریف ، باب السلم الی من لیس عنده اصل ص ۲۹۹ نمبر ۲۲۴۶ رابن ماجه شریف، باب اذا اسلم فی نخل بعینہ لم يطلع ص ۱۳۲۷ نمبر ۴ ۲۲۸) اس حدیث میں فرمایا کہ بازار میں بھی اصل موجود نہ ہو تو کیسے بیچ کرو گے؟ اور کیسے مشتری کے مال کو حلال کرو گے؟ اس لئے مال کا بازار میں ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اصول مال کم از کم بازار میں ملتا ہو تو بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دینے کے وقت طبیع بازار میں ملتی ہو تب بھی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔
دینے کے وقت مبیع موجود ہے اتنا ہی کافی ہے کیونکہ اسی وقت مبیع کی ضرورت پڑے گی۔
المسلم فیه : مبیع - الحل : مدت حلول ہونے کا وقت ہمبیع دینے کا وقت۔
Salam is not permissible unless the muslam fih exists from the time of contract until the time of delivery. From here begins the explanation of the conditions for a valid salam sale. One condition is that salam is only valid for a commodity that is available in the market from the time of contract until the day the commodity is to be delivered to the buyer. If that commodity is not found in the market at all, then salam is not valid. Or if it will become available at the time of delivery but is not currently in the market, and there is a strong possibility of it disappearing from the market in the interim, then also salam is not valid. If one makes a salam contract for something that is not available in the market, then at the time of delivery what will he give the buyer? And how will he make his money lawful? Therefore it is prohibited. (2) The hadith prohibits salam for something that is not available in the market. From Ibn Umar: A man gave a salam advance to another man regarding palm trees, but that year they produced nothing. They brought the dispute to the Prophet (PBUH). He said: 'How will you make his wealth lawful? Return his money.' Then he said: 'Do not give salam in palm trees until they ripen.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Salam fi Thamara bi'aynihā, p. 135 no. 3467; Bukhari, Bab al-Salam ilā man laysa 'indahu asl, p. 299 no. 2246; Ibn Majah, Bab idhā aslama fi nakhlin bi'aynihī lam yatla', p. 1327 no. 2284). In this hadith, it is said: if the commodity is not available in the market, how will you sell? And how will you make the buyer's wealth lawful? Therefore it is necessary for the commodity to be in the market. As long as the commodity is at least available in the market, salam will be valid. Imam al-Shafi'i says that if it is available in the market at the time of delivery, then also salam is valid. It is sufficient that the commodity exists at the time of delivery, because the need for the commodity arises only at that time. Muslam fih: the commodity; al-hall: the time when the term matures, the time of delivering the commodity.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage states a key condition for the validity of salam (forward sale): the commodity (muslam fih) must be continuously available in the market from the time of contract until the time of delivery. The author explains that if the commodity is not available at all, or if it will appear only later but is currently absent with a strong chance of being unavailable in between, the contract is invalid. The reasoning is practical: without availability, the seller cannot guarantee delivery, leading to uncertainty (gharar) and potential dispute. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) ordered the return of money when a salam contract on a specific palm tree failed to produce fruit, and he prohibited salam in palm trees until they ripen (meaning the fruit is clearly in existence). Imam al-Shafi'i differs: he holds it sufficient that the commodity is available at the time of delivery, arguing that the buyer's need is only at maturity. However, the Hanafi position requires continuous availability from contract to delivery to avoid speculation and ensure certainty. The glossary clarifies key terms: muslam fih is the commodity, and al-hall is the time of delivery.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later.
مسلم فيه (muslam fih): The commodity that is sold in a salam contract, delivered at a future date.
أجل (ajal): The fixed term or time of delivery in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It must be available only at the time of delivery.
B) It must be available continuously from the time of contract until delivery.
C) It does not need to be available at all if the seller is trustworthy.
D) It must be available at the time of contract, but not necessarily at delivery.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the muslam fih to be continuously available from contract to delivery; otherwise the salam contract is fasid.

Salam Must Be Deferred with a Known Term
Ruling that salam requires deferment and a known term, with scriptural proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential conditions for a valid salam contract in the Hanafi school and apply them to distinguish salam from a regular sale.

Core Idea
Salam is only valid if delivery is deferred and the term is known; immediate delivery makes it a regular sale.

Salam is a special sale where the price is paid upfront but the commodity is delivered later. This lesson establishes two non-negotiable conditions for its validity: deferment and a known term. Without these, the contract is fasid (voidable). We will examine the Hanafi position, the proof from hadith, and a brief disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'Salam is not valid except deferred and is not permissible except with a known term.' This is the ruling you must internalize.
The ruling is categorical: both conditions are necessary.
2
Understand the condition of deferment (mu'ajjal)
Salam must involve future delivery. If the commodity is delivered immediately, the contract is a regular sale (bay' 'ayn), not salam. This is the first condition.
The word 'mu'ajjal' means deferred.
3
Understand the condition of a known term (ajal ma'lum)
The delivery date must be fixed and known to both parties. An ambiguous term (e.g., 'when the ship comes') invalidates the contract because it leads to dispute.
The hadith 'to a known term' is the proof.
4
Examine the Shafi'i disagreement
Imam al-Shafi'i reportedly said that if the word 'salam' is used, the contract may still be called salam even if immediate delivery is intended. The Hanafi response is that the essence of salam is deferment; naming does not change the nature.
This ikhtilaf concerns terminology, not the underlying ruling for Hanafis.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a contract where the buyer pays now for wheat to be delivered in 3 months, this is valid salam if the term is specified. If the wheat is to be given immediately, it is not salam regardless of the name used.
Practice by creating your own scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصح السلم الا مؤجلا ولا يجوز الا باجل معلوم
[۹۵۶] (۵) اور نہیں جائز ہے سلم مگر مؤخر کر کے اور نہیں جائز ہے مگر معلوم مدت کے ساتھ۔
بیع سلم کہتے ہیں ہیں اس کو جس میں مبیع بعد میں دی جائے۔ اور اگر مبیع فوری دینے کی بات ہو تو اس کو بیع سلم نہیں کہیں گے۔ اس کو عام بیع اور بیع عین کہیں گے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مسلم کے الفاظ سے بیع کی ہو تو اس کو بھی بیع سلم کہہ سکتے ہیں۔ بیع سلم میں یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ مدت معلوم
(۱) ور نہ تو مشتری پہلے لینا چاہے گا اور بائع بعد میں دینا چاہے گا۔ اور جھگڑا ہو گا اس لئے مبیع دینے کی تاریخ طے ہونا ضروری ہے (۲)
حدیث میں گزرا الی اجل معلوم ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۲۲۴۰ ر مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۶۰۴) اس لئے مدت متعین ہونا ضروری ہے۔
Salam is not valid except deferred and is not permissible except with a known term. [956] (5) And salam is not permissible except deferred, and not permissible except with a known term. Salam is called that in which the commodity is given later. If the commodity is to be given immediately, it is not called salam; it is called a regular sale or spot sale. Imam al-Shafi'i says that if a sale is made using the word 'salam', it may also be called salam. In salam, it is also necessary that the term be known; otherwise the buyer would want to take earlier and the seller would want to give later, and there would be dispute. Therefore it is necessary to fix the delivery date. The hadith mentions 'to a known term' (Bukhari no. 2240, Muslim no. 1604). Therefore the term must be specified.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage establishes two essential elements of salam: (1) salam must be a deferred sale (mu'ajjal), meaning the commodity is delivered later, not immediately. If delivery is immediate, it is a regular sale (bay' 'ayn), not salam. (2) The term (ajal) must be known (ma'lum) to prevent dispute. The author notes that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the word 'salam' is used, it may still be considered salam even if the delivery is immediate? Actually, the text says Shafi'i allows calling it salam if the word is used, but this seems to be about the naming, not the ruling. The emphasis is on the necessity of a known term, supported by the hadith 'to a known term' which appears in Bukhari and Muslim. Without a known term, the parties might disagree on delivery time, leading to conflict. Thus, a fixed date or period is mandatory.

Key Terms
مؤجل (mu'ajjal): Deferred; delivery is postponed to a future date.
أجل معلوم (ajal ma'lum): A known and specified term for delivery.
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for deferred delivery of a described commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The contract is fasid (voidable) because of uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
For a salam contract to be valid in the Hanafi school, delivery must be deferred and the term must be known and specified; otherwise the contract is invalid.
