Standardized Measure Condition in Salam
Ruling prohibiting salam with personalized measures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that salam using a specific person's vessel or handspan is invalid and explain the underlying reason (gharar).

Core Idea
Salam requires a known public measure; a personalized measure causes uncertainty and invalidates the contract.

Salam (forward sale) allows payment in advance for goods to be delivered later. This flexibility is tied to precision: the quantity must be known beyond doubt. In this passage, the author clarifies that using a specific individual's measuring vessel or handspan fails that condition, because the exact capacity is unknown to others and may be lost if that person or vessel disappears.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is salam using a specific person's vessel (mikyāl) or hand (dhirā'). The ruling: it is not permissible – the contract is fasid (invalid).
2
Extract the legal reason (ʿilla)
Why is it invalid? Because the quantity is unknown and cannot be reliably reproduced if the specific measure is lost or the person dies or disappears. This introduces gharar (uncertainty).
3
Connect to the broader principle
This is an application of the prohibition of gharar in contracts. Salam must have precise, known specifications to avoid disputes.
4
Note the evidence
The author mentions that a hadith on this matter will follow. The proof is based on the general consensus that salam requires a known quantity, which is blocked by personalized measures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز السلم بمكيال رجل بعينه ولا بذراع رجل بعينه
[۹۵۷] (۶) کسی آدمی کے متعین مکیال سے بیع سلم جائز نہیں اور نہ کسی متعین آدمی کے ہاتھ سے۔ ایک آدمی کا متعین برتن ہے اور اس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے کہ کتنا کیلو اس میں آتا ہے۔ اب اس برتن کی ناپ سے بیع سلم کرنا جائز نہیں
مبیع مہینوں بعد ادا کرتا ہے اس لئے اگر وہ برتن گم ہو جائے تو کسی برتن سے ناپیں گے۔ اس کی مقدار تو معلوم نہیں ہے اس لئے کسی آدمی کے متعین برتن سے بیع سلم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح متعین آدمی کے ہاتھ سے بیع سلم کی اور وہ آدمی مرگیا یا کہیں چلا گیا تو کس آدمی کے ہاتھ سے کپڑانا ہیں گے۔ اس لئے کسی متعین آدمی کے ہاتھ سے بیع سلم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس بارے میں حدیث آگے آرہی ہے۔
Salam is not permissible with the measure of a specific person nor with the handspan of a specific person. [957] (6) Salam is not permissible with a specific person's measuring vessel, nor with a specific person's hand. A person has a specific vessel, and its capacity is unknown—how many kilos it holds. So salam using that vessel is not valid. Since the commodity is delivered months later, if that vessel is lost, with which vessel will they measure? Its capacity is unknown. Therefore salam with a specific person's vessels is not valid. Similarly, if salam is done with a specific person's hand, and that person dies or goes away, with whose hand will they measure the cloth? Therefore salam with a specific person's hand is not valid. A hadith on this matter is coming ahead.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage states another condition for valid salam: the measure, weight, or length used to specify the commodity must be a known standard, not tied to a specific person's individual vessel or handspan. If the measure is a particular person's container (mikyāl) whose capacity is not publicly known, or a person's hand (dhirā') which is not standardized, then the contract is invalid. The reasoning is that if that specific measure is lost or the person dies, there is no way to determine the exact quantity promised, leading to uncertainty (gharar). The author mentions that a hadith will be cited later; it appears in other books. This condition ensures that the subject matter of salam is precisely defined by standard measures.

Key Terms
مکیال (mikyāl): A measuring vessel used for measuring volume.
ذراع (dhirā'): A unit of length measured by the forearm; here it refers to a specific person's handspan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because it is considered gambling.
D) Because the seller might cheat.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires a public standard measure; a personalized measure invalidates the contract due to uncertainty.

Salam Not Valid for Specific Location or Specific Tree
Ruling prohibiting salam tied to specific location or tree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that salam is invalid when the commodity is specified to a particular village or tree, and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Salam tied to a specific source is invalid due to gharar (uncertainty of delivery).

In salam (advance payment for future delivery), the commodity must be described generically to ensure delivery is possible. Tying the commodity to a specific village or a specific tree introduces risk: if that source fails, the seller cannot fulfill the contract. The Hanafi school, based on hadith, rules such a contract invalid (fasid). This lesson examines the ruling, its rationale, and the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type and the prohibited specification
Salam is a forward sale where payment is made upfront and delivery deferred. The passage prohibits two specifications: tying the commodity to a specific village's grain or a specific tree's fruit. Note that the prohibition is not about the commodity itself but about linking it to a single source.
2
Understand the rationale: gharar (uncertainty)
If the specified source fails (crop failure, tree barren), the seller cannot deliver the exact commodity. This uncertainty makes the contract akin to gambling. The Hanafi school views such uncertainty as invalidating.
3
Examine the primary proof: hadith of Ibn Umar
The hadith narrates a man who made salam on a specific palm tree. When it bore no fruit, the Prophet ordered return of the money and prohibited salam on palm trees until they ripen. This shows that salam on a specific source is invalid due to risk of non-delivery.
4
Apply to analogous cases
Consider if a buyer specifies a particular field or a particular farmer's crop. The same ruling applies: the contract becomes fasid. The commodity must be described in a way that can be sourced from multiple places (e.g., 'wheat of a certain grade').

Nor in the food of a specific village, nor in the fruit of a specific palm tree. [958] (7) Salam is not permissible in the grain of a specific village, nor in the fruit of a specific tree. If one specifies: 'I make salam in the wheat of a certain village' or 'in the fruit of a specific tree of Zaid', then this salam is not valid. (1) If that village has no wheat production, what wheat will he give? And from where will he bring that type of wheat? Similarly, if the specific tree does not produce fruit, what fruit will he give? Therefore salam in a specific village or specific tree fruit is not permissible. However, if it is from anywhere, it is valid. (2) The proof is in the hadith: From Ibn Umar: a man gave salam in a palm tree, but it produced nothing that year. They brought the dispute to the Prophet (PBUH). He said: 'How will you make his wealth lawful? Return his money.' Then he said: 'Do not give salam in palm trees until they ripen.' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah). This hadith indicates that salam was done for a specific tree's fruit, and when it failed, the Prophet ordered return of money. Therefore salam in a specific village or specific tree is not valid. (2) Another hadith: Abdullah bin Salam said: 'Banu so-and-so' ... The Prophet said: 'No, O Jew.' Then Zaid bin Sa'nah said: 'O Muhammad, would you like to sell me known dates to a known term from the garden of Banu so-and-so?' He said: 'But I sell you known dates for such-and-such a term and do not name the garden of Banu so-and-so.' I said: 'Yes.' (Bayhaqi). Footnote (a): Ibn Umar's hadith repeated. Footnote (b): Zaid bin Sa'nah said: 'O Muhammad, do you want to sell me dates from the garden of Banu so-and-so?' He said: 'No, O Jew. But I sell you known dates for such a term and do not specify the garden of Banu so-and-so.' I said: 'Yes, i.e., I do not specify the garden. Rather I can sell any dates.'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage prohibits salam when the commodity is tied to a specific location (e.g., a village's wheat) or a specific tree (e.g., Zaid's palm tree). The reason is uncertainty: if that village's crop fails or that tree does not bear fruit, the seller cannot deliver. The contract becomes a risky transaction akin to gambling. The author provides two proofs: first, the hadith of Ibn Umar where salam on a specific palm tree failed and the Prophet ordered return of the money and prohibited salam in palm trees until they ripen. Second, a narration from Abdullah bin Salam (or Zaid bin Sa'nah) where the Prophet explicitly refused to specify a particular garden and instead sold dates without specifying the source, indicating that general description is acceptable but specific identification is not. The footnote clarifies that the Prophet did not name the garden; he kept the commodity generic. Thus for salam validity, the commodity must be described as a genus and type, not tied to a specific source that may fail.

Key Terms
طعام قرية (ta'ām qaryah): The grain or food product of a specific village.
ثمرة نخلة (thamarat nakhla): The fruit of a specific palm tree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam invalid when the commodity is tied to a specific village's crop?
A) Because the village may not want to sell.
B) Because the crop may fail, making delivery impossible.
C) Because it is considered usury.
D) Because the buyer must know the exact field.

Key Takeaway
Salam is only valid when the commodity is described generically, not tied to a specific location or source, because uncertainty in delivery invalidates the contract.

Prohibition of Salam with Uncertain Specifications
Ruling forbidding salam with uncertain specific items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam when the subject matter is tied to a specific measure, village, or tree, and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar and the incident with Zayd ibn Sa'na.

Core Idea
Salam contracts must avoid uncertainty: tying delivery to a specific tree or village invalidates the contract.

This lesson addresses a common pitfall in salam (forward sale) contracts: specifying a particular source that may fail to deliver. The Hanafi school forbids such specification based on clear prophetic guidance. We will examine the ruling and its proofs from the Sunnah, understanding why uncertainty (gharar) renders the contract invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited specifications
The source lists four prohibited specifications: a specific measuring container, a specific handspan, food from a specific village, and fruit from a specific palm tree. Recognise that each creates uncertainty in quantity or availability.
2
Examine the hadith of Ibn Umar
A man gave salam in a specific palm tree, but it bore no fruit that year. The Prophet (ﷺ) ordered the return of the capital and said, 'Do not give salam in palm trees until their goodness appears.' This shows that tying a salam to a specific tree is invalid.
3
Examine the hadith of Zayd ibn Sa'na
Zayd proposed a salam of dates from a specific garden. The Prophet (ﷺ) refused to name the garden, insisting on a general description. This confirms that specificity leading to uncertainty is prohibited.
4
Derive the illa (effective cause)
The common factor (illa) in all four cases is gharar (uncertainty) regarding the ability to deliver. The precise measure might be lost, the tree may fail, the village may not produce. This uncertainty invalidates the contract.
Hanafi scholars derive that any salam with such uncertainty is fasid (invalid).
5
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Any salam contract that ties the subject matter to a specific uncertain source (e.g. 'mangoes from tree X' or 'grain from field Y') falls under this prohibition. The contract must describe the commodity generically with known attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز السلم بمكيال رجل بعينه ولا بذراع رجل بعينه ولا في طعام قرية بعينها ولا في ثمرة نخلة بعينها. عن ابن عمر ان رجلا اسلف رجلا في نخل فلم تخرج تلك السنة شيئا فاختصما الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال بما تستحل ماله اردد عليه ماله ثم قال لا تسلفو في النخل حتى يبدو صلاحه. و حديث: قال زيد بن سعنه يا محمد هل لك ان تبيعني تمرا معلوما الى اجل معلوم من حائط بني فلان قال لا يا يهودي ولكن ابيعك تمرا معلوما الى كذا وكذا من الاجل ولا اسمي من حائط فلان فقلت نعم.
And salam is not permissible by the specific measure of a man nor by the specific handspan of a man, nor in the food of a specific village, nor in the fruit of a specific palm tree. From Ibn Umar: A man gave salam in palm trees, and that year nothing came out, so they brought the dispute to the Prophet (ﷺ). He said: 'By what do you make his wealth lawful? Return his wealth to him.' Then he said: 'Do not give salam in palm trees until their goodness appears.' And a hadith: Zayd ibn Sa'na said: 'O Muhammad, do you want to sell me known dates for a known term from the garden of Banu so-and-so?' He said: 'No, O Jew, but I will sell you known dates for such-and-such term and I will not specify the garden of so-and-so.' I said: 'Yes.'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the chapter of salam (forward sale). The author forbids salam when the subject matter is linked to a specific measure (like a particular person's container), a specific handspan, the produce of a specific village, or the fruit of a specific palm tree. The reason is that such specification introduces uncertainty (gharar) because the exact quantity or availability is unknown. If the measure is lost or the tree fails to yield, delivery becomes impossible, leading to dispute. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: a man gave salam in a specific palm tree, but it bore no fruit that year. The Prophet (ﷺ) ordered the return of the capital and prohibited salam in specific trees until fruit appears. Another hadith shows that the Prophet (ﷺ) refused to specify a particular garden when Zayd ibn Sa'na proposed salam, indicating that generality is required. Thus, salam contracts must avoid tying performance to a specific uncertain source.

Key Terms
مكيال رجل بعينه (mikyāl rajul bi-‘aynihi): A specific measuring container belonging to a particular person, whose capacity is not universally known.
طعام قرية بعينها (ṭa‘ām qaryah bi-‘aynihā): Food from a specific village, which may not be available if the village fails to produce.

Seven Conditions for Salam Contract
Listing seven conditions for salam contract with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions for a valid salam contract according to Imam Abu Hanifa, cite the supporting proofs, and explain why each condition is necessary to avoid gharar.

Core Idea
Salam requires seven known specifications; omission of any condition invalidates the contract due to uncertainty.

Imam Abu Hanifa set seven explicit conditions that must be mentioned in a salam contract. This exceptional sale of future goods requires full specification to prevent the forbidden uncertainty (gharar). The passage lists these conditions along with proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven conditions
Read the list: known genus, type, description, quantity, term, capital amount, and place of delivery. Memorize them in order.
Each condition is preceded by 'ma'lum' (known) to emphasize certainty.
2
Understand the legal rationale
For each condition, explain why it is needed to avoid gharar. For example, known genus prevents confusion about the commodity category.
Salam is a sale of a non-existent object; specification substitutes for sight.
3
Examine the proofs
The passage cites the hadith 'Whoever gives salam...', prohibition of gharar, prohibition of cheating, and companion practice. Connect each proof to the required conditions.
The hadith explicitly requires known measure/weight and known term.
4
Note cross-madhhab differences
Other schools may have fewer conditions. For example, the Shafi'i school does not require specification of the place of delivery.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and based on different interpretations of the proofs.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a salam contract for 100 kg of premium basmati rice to be delivered in 3 months at a specific warehouse. Verify all seven conditions are met.
If any condition is missing, the contract is fasid (invalid) according to Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصح السلم عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله الا بسبع شرائط تذكر في العقد جنس معلوم ونوع معلوم وصفة معلومة و مقدار معلوم واجل معلوم ومعرفة مقدار رأس مال و مكان التسليم. من اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم. عن ابي هريرة قال نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيع الغرر وبيع الحصاة. فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليس منا من غش. فقال ابن ابي اوفى: انا كنا نسلف على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وابي بكر وعمر في الحنطة والشعير والزبيب والتمر وسألت ابن ابزى فقال مثل ذلك.
And salam is not valid according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, except with seven conditions mentioned in the contract: known genus, known type, known description, known quantity, known term, knowledge of the amount of capital, and the place of delivery. 'Whoever gives salam in something, then in a known measure and known weight until a known term.' From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade the sale of gharar and the sale of pebbles. And the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'He is not from us who cheats.' And Ibn Abi Awfa said: 'We used to give salam in the time of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), Abu Bakr, and Umar in wheat, barley, raisins, and dates.' And I asked Ibn Abza and he said likewise.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents the seven conditions for a valid salam contract according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Salam is an exception to the general rule of selling what is not in one's possession, and therefore requires strict conditions to avoid gharar (uncertainty). The seven conditions are: (1) Known genus (jins) – e.g., wheat or dates; (2) Known type (naw') – e.g., red wheat; (3) Known description (sifah) – e.g., quality; (4) Known quantity (miqdar) – e.g., measure or weight; (5) Known term (ajal) – fixed future date; (6) Known amount of capital (ra's al-mal) – the price must be specified; (7) Designation of place of delivery (makan al-taslim) if transport cost is involved. The proofs include the hadith 'Whoever gives salam, then in known measure and weight until a known term' (Bukhari), the prohibition of gharar (Tirmidhi), and the prohibition of cheating (Abu Dawud). The practice of the Companions as narrated by Ibn Abi Awfa shows that salam was done for specific genera like wheat and dates. These conditions ensure that the contract is free from uncertainty and both parties know exactly what is owed.

Key Terms
جنس معلوم (jins ma‘lūm): The category of the commodity (e.g., wheat, dates) must be specified.
أجل معلوم (ajal ma‘lūm): A fixed future date for delivery.
نوع معلوم (naw‘ ma‘lūm): The specific variety within the genus (e.g., red wheat vs. white wheat).
صفة معلومة (ṣifah ma‘lūmah): The quality description (e.g., premium or standard).
مقدار معلوم (miqdār ma‘lūm): Known quantity by measure or weight.
معرفة مقدار رأس مال (ma‘rifat miqdār ra’s al-māl): Knowledge of the amount of capital paid upfront.
مكان التسليم (makān al-taslīm): The place where the commodity is to be delivered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Known amount of capital

Key Takeaway
For a valid salam contract under Abu Hanifa, all seven specifications must be explicitly mentioned to eliminate uncertainty; otherwise the contract is fasid.

Seven Conditions for Salam According to Abu Hanifa
Enumerates and proves the seven conditions for a valid salam contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions of salam according to Abu Hanifa and apply them to determine the validity of a salam contract.

Core Idea
Salam is valid only with seven specific conditions to eliminate gharar.

This passage enumerates the seven conditions that must be met for a salam (advance payment sale) contract to be valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Because salam involves paying for goods that do not yet exist, the law requires strict specification to prevent ambiguity and dispute. Each condition is derived from hadith and the principle of avoiding gharar (uncertainty).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is salam (advance sale). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) only when the seven conditions are present; otherwise it is invalid.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main evidence is the hadith: 'Whoever pays in advance for something, then for a known measure and known weight until a known term' (Bukhari no. 2240). Also, the practice of the Companions (athar) for specific genera.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but accepted in mu'amalat.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative phrase 'ففي كيل معلوم' indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul: the command to specify measure, weight, and term shows they are required.
Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
List the seven conditions
The seven conditions are: known genus, known type, known description, known quantity, known term, known amount of capital (price), and known place of delivery (if transportation cost involved).
Each condition is explained in detail in the commentary.
5
Understand the rationale behind each condition
Each condition eliminates a specific source of uncertainty (gharar) or potential dispute. For example, specifying genus prevents confusion about the kind of commodity; specifying type prevents dispute over variety; specifying description prevents quality disputes; specifying quantity prevents disagreement over amount; specifying term prevents delay disputes; specifying capital amount prevents return issues; specifying place prevents delivery location disputes.
Some conditions are derived from the hadith, others from the prohibition of gharar and cheating.

شرطیں پائی جائیں تو بيح سلم درست ہوگی اور نہ نہیں۔ سلم میں مبیع بعد میں دیگا اس لئے یہ چیزیں ابھی سے متعین ہو جائے تو نزاع نہیں ہوگا۔ اور مبیع کافی حد تک متعین ہو جائے گی۔ يه ساری شرطیں کچھ تو حدیث من اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم (الف) ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۲۲۴۰) سے مستنبط ہے اور کچھ شرطیں اس لئے لگائی گئی ہیں تا کہ مبيح میں دھو کہ نہ رہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيع الغرر وبيع الحصاة (ب) (ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی كراهية بيح الغررص ٢٣٢ نمبر ۱۲۳۰) اور حدیث فقال رسول الله ليس منا من غش (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب انھی عن الغش ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۳۴۵۲) کا خلاصہ ہے۔ تا كہ بائع کو اور مشتری کو کسی قسم کا دھو کہ نہ رہے۔ اس لئے یہ سات شرطیں لگائی گئی ہیں۔ اس میں ایک بات یہ بھی ہے کہ یہ بيح خلاف قیاس ہے اس لئے بھی کچھ شرطیں لگی ہیں۔ ہر شرط کی تفصیل اس طرح ہے۔ تری جنس معلوم ہو : یعنی یہ معلوم ہو کہ کس چیز کی بيح کر رہا ہے۔ گيهوں كی ، چاول کی یا کھجور کی ۔ اس سے چیز کا پتہ چلے گا کہ کیا چیز ہے؟ اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ فقال ابن ابی اوفی) انا كنا نسلف على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وابي بكر وعمر في الحنطة والشعير والزبيب والتمر وسألت ابن ابزى فقال مثل ذلك (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب السلم فی وزن معلوم ص ۲۹۸ نمبر ۲۲۴۲) اس اثر میں گيهوں، جو، کشمش اور کھجور الگ الگ جنس کا نام لیا ہے کہ ہم لوگ ان میں بيح سلم کرتے تھے ۔ اس لئے جنس معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) کسی نے کسی چیز میں بيح سلم کی تو کیل معلوم ہو، وزن معلوم ہو اور اجل معلوم ہو (ب) حضور نے روکا دھوکے کی بيح سے اور کنکری والی بيح سے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا ہم میں سے وہ نہیں ہے جو دھوکہ دیتا ہو ( د ) ابن ابی اوفی نے فرمایا ہم حضور کے زمانے میں بيح سلم کرتے تھے اور ابو بکر اور عمر کے زمانے میں گيهوں میں ، جو میں کشمش میں اور کھجور میں۔ اور ابن ابری سے پوچھا تو انہوں نے بھی اسی طرح فرمایا۔

المال اذا كان مما يتعلق العقد على قدره كالمكيل والموزون والمعدود وتسمية المكان نوع معلوم ہو : کیونکہ گيهوں بھی کئی قسم کے ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے یہ طے کرنا ہوگا کہ کس قسم کے گيهوں چاہئے یا کس قسم کے چاول چاہئے ۔ اس کو نوع معلوم کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت اس اثر میں ہے۔ عن عامر قال اذا اسلم فی ثوب يعرف ذرعه ورقعة فلا بأس (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شبيبه ۷۳ افی السلم بالثياب، ج رابع ص ۱۳۹۸، نمبر ۲۱۴۰۱) اس اثر میں ہے ورقعہ یعنی کس قسم کا کپڑا ہو۔ يہ معلوم ہو تو کپڑے میں بيح سلم جائز ہے۔
صفت معلوم ہو : یعنی یہ بھی طے ہو کہ عمدہ قسم کے گيهوں ہو یا ردی قسم کے۔ ورنہ مشتری عمدہ لینا چاہے گا اور بائع ردی دینا چاہے گا اور جھگڑا ہو گا۔ اس لئے صفت کا طے ہونا ضروری ہے۔
طبيع کی مقدار معلوم ہو: یعنی بھی کتنے کیلو ہوگی یا کتنے صاع ہوگی۔ تا كہ یہ نہ ہوکہ میں کیلو پر بات طے ہوئی تھی یا نہیں کیلو پر؟ حديث گزر چکی ہے فلي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم ۔
مدت معلوم ہو : یعنی کب مبیع دو گے۔ تا كہ یہ نہ ہو کہ بائع دیر کر کے دے اور مشتری جلدی مانگے جس سے نزاع ہو۔ حديث گزر چکی ہے الی اجل معلوم ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ۲۲۴۱)
رأس المال یعنی شمن کی مقدار معلوم ہو : یعنی وہ کتنے كيلو يا کتنے صاع یا کتنے عدد ہیں۔ کیونکہ مثلا بيح نہیں دے سکا اور شمن کو لوٹانے کی ضرورت پڑی تو اگر شمن کی مقدار معلوم نہیں تو کیسے لوٹائے گا۔ یا مثلا شمن میں کھوٹا پن ہے اور اس کو لوٹانے کی ضرورت پڑی تو کیسے لوٹائے گا۔ اس لئے اگر شمن کیلی ہو یا وزنی ہو یا عددی ہو تو شمن کی مقدار معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے۔ چاہے شمن کی طرف اشارہ کر کے بيح سلم طے کی ہو۔ ہاں اگر من ذراعی ہو مثلا کپڑا ہو تو کپڑوں میں ذراع صفت ہے اور صفت کے مقابلے میں کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی اس لئے ذراعی کی شکل میں کپڑا سامنے ہو تو کتنا گز ہے اس کو معلوم کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے وقال ابن عمر لابأس في الطعام الموصوف بسعر معلوم الى اجل معلوم (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب السلم الی اجل معلوم ص ۳۰۰ نمبر ۲۲۵۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بھاؤ معلوم ہو یعنی راس المال ثمن کی مقدار معلوم ہو۔ کے سپرد کرنے کی جگہ معلوم ہو : مسلم فیہ یعنی مبیع کو اٹھا کر لے جانے کا کرایہ لگتا ہو تو مبیع کو کس مقام پر مشتری کو دے گا اس جگہ کا تعین بھی ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر جگہ متعین نہ ہو تو بائع اپنے قریب مبیع دینا چاہے گا اور مشتری اپنے قریب لینا چاہے گا اور جھگڑا ہو گا۔ اس لئے مبع دینے کی جگہ کا متعین ہونا ضروری ہے۔ ہاں اگر مبیع کے اٹھانے کا کرایہ نہ ہو تو کسی جگہ بھی دیگا تو صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں جگہ کو متعین کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ صبيح سامنے نہ ہو تو اتنی شرطیں لگائی جائیں کہ مبیع کافی حد تک موجود کے درجے میں ہو جائے۔
عاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عامر نے فرمایا اگر کپڑے میں بيح سلم کرے تو اس کا گز اور اس کی قسم معلوم ہو تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ب) حضرت ابن عمر نے فرمایا کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے سلم کرنے میں صفات بیان کئے ہوئے کھانے میں بھاؤ معلوم ہو مدت معلوم ہوں
The Book of Sales. (8) Salam is not valid according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, except with seven conditions mentioned in the contract: known genus, known type, known description, known quantity, known term, and knowledge of the amount of capital—Salam is not valid until it is with its description known without attachment to a specific entity. (Then Urdu explanation: In this hadith, Zayd bin Sa'nah wanted to make a salam contract for the dates of a specific garden, but the Prophet refused and said, 'I will sell dates from any garden, not the dates of the garden of Banu so-and-so.' From this it is known that salam for the fruit of a specific garden or specific tree is not permissible. Also, salam for something whose existence is feared is not permissible.) (959)(8) Salam is not valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa except with seven conditions that are mentioned in the contract: (1) known genus, (2) known type, (3) known description, (4) known quantity of the subject matter, (5) known term, (6) known amount of the price if the price is such that it depends on its quantity, like measured, weighed, or counted items, (7) and specification of the place where the subject matter will be delivered if the subject matter has cost of transportation and rent. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if these seven conditions are present, the salam contract is valid, otherwise not. In salam, the subject matter will be delivered later, so these matters must be specified now to avoid dispute, and the subject matter will be sufficiently specified. All these conditions are partly derived from the hadith 'Whoever pays in advance for something, then for a known measure and known weight until a known term' (Bukhari no. 2240), and some conditions are placed to ensure the subject matter is free from deception, as summarized from the hadith 'The Prophet forbade the sale of gharar and the sale of pebbles' (Tirmidhi no. 1230) and the hadith 'He is not of us who cheats' (Abu Dawud no. 3452) so that there is no deception for the seller or buyer. Therefore these seven conditions are placed. Also, this sale is contrary to analogy, so some conditions are placed for that reason. The detail of each condition is as follows: 'Known genus' means it must be known what thing is being sold—wheat, rice, or dates. This indicates what the thing is. In the athar, Ibn Abi Awfa said: 'We used to make salam contracts during the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar for wheat, barley, raisins, and dates' (Bukhari no. 2242). In this athar, wheat, barley, raisins, and dates are mentioned separately as different genera, so knowing the genus is necessary. Footnote (a): 'Whoever pays in advance for something, then for a known measure, known weight, and known term.' (b): 'The Prophet forbade the sale of gharar and the sale of pebbles.' (c): 'He said: He is not of us who cheats.' (d): Ibn Abi Awfa said: 'We used to make salam contracts during the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar for wheat, barley, raisins, and dates. And I asked Ibn Abzi and he said likewise.' (Page 95) 'Known type': because wheat also has several varieties, so it must be decided which variety of wheat or rice is desired. This is called 'known type'. Its evidence is in the athar: 'Amir said: If one makes salam for a cloth whose yard and patch (the type of cloth) are known, there is no harm' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 21401). In this athar, 'patch' means what kind of cloth it is, so if that is known, salam for cloth is permissible. 'Known description': meaning it must also be decided whether it is fine quality wheat or low quality. Otherwise, the buyer wants fine and the seller wants to give low quality, leading to dispute. Therefore specifying the description is necessary. 'Known quantity of the subject matter': meaning how many kilograms or how many sa's will it be? So that it does not happen that the deal was agreed on one measure and not on another. The hadith has passed: 'For known measure and known weight.' 'Known term': meaning when will the subject matter be given? So that it does not happen that the seller delays and the buyer demands quickly, causing dispute. The hadith has passed: 'Until a known term' (Bukhari no. 2241). 'Capital i.e. known amount of price': meaning how many kilograms or how many sa's or how many units is it? Because if the seller cannot deliver and needs to return the price, if the amount of price is not known, how will he return it? Or if the price is defective and needs to be returned, how will he return it? Therefore, if the price is measured, weighed, or counted, its amount must be known, even if the salam was agreed by pointing to the price. However, if it is by measure of length, for example cloth, then in cloths, the yard is a description and there is no price in comparison to description; so if cloth is present in the form of measure of length, it is not necessary to know how many yards it is. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is this athar: 'Ibn Umar said: There is no harm in salam for described food with a known price until a known term' (Bukhari no. 2253). In this athar, the price being known means the amount of capital (price) is known. 'Place of delivery known': meaning the subject matter, if it has cost of transportation, then the place where the seller will deliver to the buyer must also be specified. Because if the place is not specified, the seller wants to deliver near himself and the buyer wants to receive near himself, causing dispute. Therefore specifying the place of delivery is necessary. However, if the subject matter has no cost of transportation, delivering at any place will be valid. In that case, specifying the place is not necessary. When the commodity is not present, so many conditions are placed that the subject matter reaches to a degree of being present. Footnotes: (a): 'Amir said: If one makes salam for a cloth, its yard and its type are known, then there is no harm.' (b): 'Ibn Umar said: There is no harm in salam for described food with a known price and a known term.'
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Al Sharh Ul Sameri' explaining the conditions for a valid salam (advance payment sale) according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The author begins by stating that salam is not valid except with seven specific conditions mentioned in the contract. These conditions are necessary because salam involves paying for goods that will be delivered later, so ambiguity must be eliminated to prevent dispute. The conditions are: (1) known genus, (2) known type, (3) known description, (4) known quantity, (5) known term, (6) known amount of capital (price), and (7) known place of delivery if transportation cost is involved. The author notes that these conditions are partly derived from the hadith 'Whoever pays in advance for something, then for a known measure and known weight until a known term' (Bukhari). Additional conditions are based on prohibitions of gharar (uncertainty) and cheating, as well as the fact that salam is contrary to qiyas (analogy) since it involves selling something not yet in existence. The author then explains each condition in detail: 'Jins' (genus) refers to the general category like wheat, barley, etc., citing the practice of the Companions. 'Naw' (type) refers to the specific variety, like fine vs. coarse wheat, with evidence from salam in cloth. 'Sifah' (description) refers to quality, such as high-grade or low-grade. 'Miqdar' (quantity) refers to measure, weight, or count. 'Ajal' (term) refers to the delivery date. 'Ras al-mal' (capital) refers to the amount of the advance payment, which must be known if it is measured, weighed, or counted. The final condition is 'makān' (place) for delivery if the goods require transportation costs. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence for the requirement of known capital is the athar of Ibn Umar allowing salam with a known price and term. The author also clarifies that if the goods are such that no transportation cost is involved (e.g., small items), specifying the place is not necessary. The overall purpose of these conditions is to make the salam contract as certain as possible, avoiding the gharar that would invalidate it.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A sale in which the price is paid in advance at the time of contract, and the goods are delivered later at a specified future date.
جنس (jins): The broader category of the commodity, such as wheat, barley, etc., as opposed to the specific type or variety.
نوع (naw): The specific variety or subtype of the genus, e.g., white wheat vs. red wheat, or fine cloth vs. coarse cloth.
صفة (sifah): The quality or grade of the commodity, e.g., high quality or low quality, which must be specified to avoid dispute.
مقدار (miqdar): The precise quantity by measurement, weight, or count.
أجل (ajal): The fixed future term for delivery of the goods in salam.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The advance payment (capital) in salam, the amount of which must be known.
مكان التسليم (makan al-taslim): The place where the subject matter is to be delivered; required if transportation cost is involved.
الغرر (al-gharar): Uncertainty or risk in a contract, prohibited in Islamic law. Salam is an exception with conditions to minimize gharar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how many conditions are required for a valid salam contract?
A) Five
B) Six
C) Seven
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
A valid salam contract requires seven specific conditions to eliminate gharar: known genus, type, description, quantity, term, capital amount, and place of delivery (if transport cost applies).

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Six Conditions for Validity of Salam
Lists the six required conditions for a valid salam contract with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for a valid salam contract and explain the Hanafi evidence for each, including intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Salam requires six conditions to avoid uncertainty; missing any may invalidate the contract.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a special contract where the price is paid upfront and the commodity is delivered later. To prevent disputes and gharar (uncertainty), the Hanafi school specifies six conditions that must be clearly defined. This lesson walks through each condition, its rationale, and the textual evidence from hadith and sahabi reports, along with notable differences between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
From the passage, list each condition: type (naw'), quality (sifah), quantity (miqdar), term (ajal), price quantity (ra's al-mal), and place of delivery (makan).
These are derived from the evidence cited.
2
Examine the dalil for each condition
For each condition, note the specific proof: hadith 'with known measure and known weight' for quantity, 'to a known term' for term, athar from Ibn 'Umar for price quantity, etc.
The passage provides both hadith and sahabi reports.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disputes
Two disputes: regarding price quantity if mu'ayyan (present) and measured by cubit, Imam Abu Hanifa does not require specification; regarding place, Abu Hanifa requires only if transport cost exists, while Sahibayn default to place of contract.
These disputes are noted in the passage.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a practical case (e.g., salam in wheat), verify each condition is met. If any is missing, the contract becomes fasid (defective).
This step tests understanding.

مدت معلوم ہو : یعنی کب مبیع دو گے۔ تا کہ یہ نہ ہو کہ بائع دیر کر کے دے اور مشتری جلدی مانگے جس سے نزاع ہو۔ حدیث گزر چکی ہے الی اجل معلوم ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ۲۲۴۱)
رأس المال یعنی شمن کی مقدار معلوم ہو : یعنی وہ کتنے کیلو یا کتنے صاع یا کتنے عدد ہیں۔
کیونکہ مثلا بیع نہیں دے سکا اور شمن کو لوٹانے کی ضرورت پڑی تو اگر شمن کی مقدار معلوم نہیں تو کیسے لوٹائے گا۔ یا مثلا شمن میں کھوٹا پن ہے اور اس کو لوٹانے کی ضرورت پڑی تو کیسے لوٹائے گا۔ اس لئے اگر شمن کیلی ہو یا وزنی ہو یا عددی ہو تو شمن کی مقدار معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے۔ چاہے شمن کی طرف اشارہ کر کے بیع سلم طے کی ہو۔ ہاں اگر من ذراعی ہو مثلا کپڑا ہو تو کپڑوں میں ذراع صفت ہے اور صفت کے مقابلے میں کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی اس لئے ذراعی کی شکل میں کپڑا سامنے ہو تو کتنا گز ہے اس کو معلوم کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے وقال ابن عمر لابأس في الطعام الموصوف بسعر معلوم الى اجل معلوم (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب السلم الی اجل معلوم ص ۳۰۰ نمبر ۲۲۵۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بھاؤ معلوم ہو یعنی راس المال ثمن کی مقدار معلوم ہو۔ کے سپرد کرنے کی جگہ معلوم ہو : مسلم فیہ یعنی مبیع کو اٹھا کر لے جانے کا کرایہ لگتا ہو تو مبیع کو کس مقام پر مشتری کو دے گا اس جگہ کا تعین بھی ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر جگہ متعین نہ ہو تو بائع اپنے قریب مبیع دینا چاہے گا اور مشتری اپنے قریب لینا چاہے گا اور جھگڑا ہو گا۔ اس لئے مبع دینے کی جگہ کا متعین ہونا ضروری ہے۔ ہاں اگر مبیع کے اٹھانے کا کرایہ نہ ہو تو کسی جگہ بھی دیگا تو صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں جگہ کو متعین کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ صبیح سامنے نہ ہو تو اتنی شرطیں لگائی جائیں کہ مبیع کافی حد تک موجود کے درجے میں ہو جائے۔
عاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عامر نے فرمایا اگر کپڑے میں بیع سلم کرے تو اس کا گز اور اس کی قسم معلوم ہو تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ب) حضرت ابن عمر نے فرمایا کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے سلم کرنے میں صفات بیان کئے ہوئے کھانے میں بھاؤ معلوم ہو مدت معلوم ہوں
If the commodity is of a type that the contract relates to its quantity, such as measured, weighed, or counted items, and the specification of the type must be known: because wheat also has many types. Therefore it must be decided which type of wheat is required or which type of rice. This is called known type. Its proof is in this athar: 'From 'Amir, he said: If one makes salam in a cloth, its length and type being known, there is no harm.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 73 fi al-Salam bi al-Thiyab, vol. 4, p. 1398, no. 21401). In this athar is 'and its type' i.e. what kind of cloth. If this is known, salam sale in cloth is permissible. The quality must be known: that is, it must be decided whether it is of good quality wheat or poor quality. Otherwise the buyer will want good quality and the seller will give poor quality and there will be dispute. Therefore determining quality is necessary. The quantity of the commodity must be known: i.e., how many kilograms or how many sa'? So that it is not disputed. The hadith has passed: 'with known measure and known weight.' The term must be known: i.e., when will you deliver the commodity. So that it does not happen that the seller delays and the buyer demands quickly, causing dispute. The hadith has passed: 'to a known term' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 2241). The capital, i.e., the price, its quantity must be known: i.e., how many kilograms, how many sa', or how many pieces. Because if, for example, the sale cannot go through and it becomes necessary to return the price, if the quantity of the price is not known, how will it be returned? Or if there is a defect in the price and it becomes necessary to return it, how will it be returned? Therefore, if the price is measured by weight or count, its quantity must be known, even if the contract was made by pointing to the price. However, if it is by cubit, e.g., cloth, then in cloth the cubit is a quality and there is no price in comparison to quality, so if the cloth in cubit form is present, there is no need to know how many yards. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifah is this athar: 'Ibn 'Umar said: There is no harm in food described with a known price to a known term' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab al-Salam ila Ajalin Ma'lum, p. 300, no. 2253). In this athar, that the price is known, i.e., the quantity of capital/price is known. The place of delivery must be known: if the commodity has a transport cost, then the place where the seller will give the commodity to the buyer must also be specified. Because if the place is not specified, the seller will want to give it near himself and the buyer will want to receive it near himself, causing dispute. Therefore specifying the place of delivery is necessary. However, if the commodity has no transport cost, then giving it anywhere will be valid. In that case, there is no need to specify the place. If the commodity is not present, such conditions are set so that the commodity becomes sufficiently similar to present.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage defines the six essential conditions for the validity of a salam contract (advance payment sale) according to the Hanafi school. The author lists each condition, explains its rationale, and provides textual evidence from hadith or athar. The conditions are: (1) specification of type (naw'), (2) specification of quality (sifah), (3) known quantity (miqdar), (4) known term (ajal), (5) known price quantity (ra's al-mal), and (6) known place of delivery. For each, the author cites proofs: for type, an athar from 'Amir regarding cloth; for quality, general necessity to avoid dispute; for quantity, the hadith 'with known measure and known weight'; for term, the hadith 'to a known term'; for price quantity, an athar from Ibn 'Umar; for delivery place, the ruling is conditional on whether transport costs exist. The passage also notes an exception for Imam Abu Hanifa regarding price quantity: if the price is physically present (mu'ayyan) and is of a type measured by cubit (e.g., cloth), then its exact measure need not be known. The commentary then explains that when the commodity is not present, conditions are set so that it is sufficiently determined.

Key Terms
نوع معلوم (naw' ma'lum): Known type, e.g., specific variety of wheat or rice, or specific type of cloth.
صفت معلوم (sifah ma'lumah): Known quality, e.g., good or bad grade of wheat.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital or price paid in advance in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith is cited in the passage to prove that the term (ajal) must be known in salam?
A) 'with known measure and known weight'
B) 'to a known term' (Bukhari no. 2241)
C) 'food described with a known price to a known term'
D) 'if one makes salam in a cloth, its length and type being known'

Key Takeaway
Salam requires six precise conditions (type, quality, quantity, term, price quantity, place if transport cost) to avoid gharar; missing any may cause the contract to be fasid.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Specification and Possession in Salam
Intra-Hanafi dispute and possession condition in salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding specification of capital and place in salam, and apply the ruling that possession of capital must be taken before separation.

Core Idea
In salam, the capital must be taken possession at the session; but specifying its quantity when present is waived by Sahibayn.

Salam is a forward sale where the price is paid upfront for future delivery of a described commodity. This passage addresses two key issues: whether the exact quantity of the capital must be specified when it is physically present, and whether the place of delivery must be stated. It also lays down a critical condition—possession of the capital must occur before the parties separate. These rulings prevent uncertainty (gharar) and the prohibited 'debt for debt' transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute on specification
Recognize that the passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa (implied) requires specifying the exact quantity of capital and the place of delivery, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say pointing suffices for present capital and the contract location is the default delivery place.
The dispute is only about mu'ayyan (present) capital; if absent, specification is always required.
2
Compare the two positions with their proofs
Understand that Abu Hanifa's position is based on avoiding dispute and the general requirement of known price (athar of Ibn 'Umar). The Sahibayn analogize to ordinary sales where pointing to a present object specifies it, and they argue the place of contract automatically becomes delivery place.
The text does not give Abu Hanifa's response; later Hanafi works often adopt Sahibayn's view for ease.
3
Extract the unconditional ruling on possession
Note that regardless of the dispute, the passage states salam is invalid unless the capital is taken possession before the parties separate. This is a condition (shart) for validity.
This ruling is unanimous among early Hanafi imams.
4
Connect possession ruling to the hadith
The reason is to avoid bai' al-kali bil kali (debt for debt), as the hadith forbids selling deferred for deferred. In salam, if capital is not taken immediately, both sides would be deferred.
The hadith is cited from Ibn 'Umar: النهى عن بيع الكالى بالكالى.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Imagine a salam contract for 100 kg of wheat where the buyer pays with a pile of wheat present in the seller's warehouse. Under the Sahibayn, pointing to the pile suffices; under Abu Hanifa, the exact weight must be stated. In both views, the buyer must physically take control of the pile before leaving the session.
Modern salam often uses bank transfers; possession is constructive, e.g., crediting the seller's account.

Which he delivers if there is transport and expense [960] (9) And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: There is no need to specify the capital if it is present, nor to specify the place of delivery, and he delivers it in the place of the contract. [961] (10) And salam is not valid until he takes possession of the capital before he separates. [962] (11) ... Transport and expense: carrying and its wage. (960) (9) And Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: There is no need to specify the capital if it is present, nor to specify the place of delivery. And he will deliver the commodity in the place of the contract. The Two Companions say: If the capital, i.e., the price, is present, then in general sales there is no need to know its quantity. Merely pointing specifies the price. Therefore in salam also, merely pointing to it will specify the price. There is no need to know its count, i.e., how many kilograms or how many sa'. Similarly, there is no need to specify the place of delivery, because the place where the sale was spoken will automatically be the place for delivery. Therefore there is no need to specify a separate place. However, if one does so, it is good. (10) And salam is not valid until he takes possession of the capital before they separate. After the salam contract is concluded, it is necessary to take possession of the price before the seller and buyer separate. If possession of the price is not taken, the salam is not valid. If both the commodity and the price are deferred, the hadith prohibits such. In general sales, the commodity is delivered in the session, so even if possession of the price is not taken, it is acceptable. But in salam, the commodity is necessarily given later, so at least possession of the price is necessary. Otherwise, the commodity would be deferred and the price deferred. But if both are conditionally deferred, the hadith prohibits this. From Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he forbade the sale of al-kali bil kali. The linguists said: it is deferred for deferred. (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 3, p. 60, no. 3022?; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Bai' al-Dayn bi al-Dayn, vol. 5, p. 474, no. 10536?) In this hadith, deferred sale with deferred is prohibited. Therefore according to the Hanafi school, it is necessary to take possession of the capital in the session. (11) And it is not permissible to dispose of the capital nor of the object of salam before taking possession. In salam, it is not permissible to dispose of the price before possession. Similarly, it is not permissible to dispose of the commodity before possession.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage contains three rulings: (9) an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether specifying the exact quantity of the capital (ra's al-mal) is needed when it is physically present (mu'ayyan), and whether the place of delivery must be specified. Abu Hanifa (implied from the earlier text) requires specification, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that if the capital is present, pointing to it suffices, and the place of contract automatically becomes the delivery place. (10) then states an unconditional ruling: salam is invalid unless the capital is taken possession before the parties separate. The reasoning is to avoid the prohibited 'debt for debt' (bai' al-kali bil kali) transaction. The hadith forbidding this is cited. (11) further prohibits disposal (tasarruf) of either the capital or the object of salam before possession. These rulings are specific to salam and prevent gharar and riba.

Key Terms
معين (mu'ayyan): Physically present and identifiable by pointing, such that no further specification is needed.
موضع العقد (mawdi' al-'aqd): The place where the contract is concluded.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In salam, taking possession of the capital before the parties separate is a binding condition; the dispute on specification of present capital is secondary and often resolved by adopting the Sahibayn's flexible view.

Sahibayn on Capital and Place Specification in Salam
Stating the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on capital and place specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the specification of capital and place in a salam contract and compare it with Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
In a salam contract, if the capital is physically determined, explicit measurement or weight is not required; the contract place suffices for delivery.

Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, sometimes differed on subtle conditions. This passage examines one such difference: whether the capital amount and delivery place must be explicitly specified in a salam contract. Understanding this intra-madhhab ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of the school's flexibility and the logic behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa requires explicit specification of the capital amount (by weight/measure) and the place of delivery. Without them, the contract is fasid due to gharar.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if the capital is determined (mu'ayyan) by sight or indication, specification of its quantity is unnecessary. Similarly, specifying the delivery place is not required; the contract place suffices.
3
Identify the underlying reasoning
The Sahibayn analogize to an ordinary sale where a present price is specified by pointing. Custom also establishes the contract place as the default delivery location.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, lack of specification invalidates the contract; under the Sahibayn, the contract is valid and delivery occurs at the contract place.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view for fatwa, making it the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله لا يحتاج الى تسمية رأس المال اذا كان معينا ولا الى مكان التسليم ويسلمه في موضع العقد
And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It is not necessary to specify the capital when it is determined, nor the place of delivery, and he delivers it at the place of the contract.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the view of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) regarding the conditions of a valid salam contract. According to them, if the capital (the price paid in advance) is physically present and determined by sight or indication, its explicit measurement or weight need not be stated. Similarly, specifying the place of delivery is not required; delivery occurs naturally at the location where the contract was made. This differs from Imam Abu Hanifa's view, who requires explicit specification of both capital amount and delivery place. The rationale is that in ordinary sales, a present price is specified by pointing, and the same applies to salam. Likewise, the contract place serves as the default delivery location. However, it is commendable to specify them for clarity.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra’s al-māl): The capital or price paid in advance in a salam contract.
مكان التسليم (makān al-taslīm): The place where the goods are to be delivered.
موضع العقد (mawḍi‘ al-‘aqd): The location where the contract is concluded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, when is it unnecessary to specify the amount of capital in a salam contract?
A) When the capital is determined (mu'ayyan) and physically present
B) When the capital is a known currency
C) When the capital is less than a specific amount
D) When the capital is given in cash

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn hold that in salam, explicit specification of capital amount and delivery place is unnecessary if the capital is determined and the contract place serves as default.

Possession of Capital Before Separation Required in Salam
Establishing the condition of capital possession before separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid salam contract regarding capital possession and explain how the hadith prohibiting kal'i bi kal'i supports this condition.

Core Idea
In salam, the price must be taken before separation to avoid the prohibited credit-for-credit sale.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of a salam (forward sale) contract: the buyer must take possession of the capital before the parties leave the contract session. The ruling is derived from a prophetic prohibition of 'kal'i bi kal'i', a transaction where both price and goods are deferred. Understanding this condition helps distinguish valid salam from prohibited forms of deferred exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The text states that salam is not valid until the capital is taken. The act is the salam contract, and the ruling is that it is invalid (batil) if the condition is not met.
The negation 'لا يصح' indicates invalidity.
2
State the condition
The condition is: the buyer must take possession of the capital before the parties separate from the contract session.
This is a shart (condition), not a rukn.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet forbade the sale of credit with credit (kal'i bi kal'i).
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of kal'i bi kal'i implies that both price and goods cannot be deferred. In salam, goods are deferred by nature; therefore the price must be immediate, i.e., taken before separation.
If both were deferred, it would fall under the prohibited category.
5
Note the khilaf
The Shafi'i school allows deferred capital in salam under certain conditions. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصح السلم حتى يقبض رأس المال قبل ان يفارقه. عن ابن عمر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم انه نهى عن بيع الكالى بالكالى قال اللغويون هو النسيئة بالنسيئة.
Salam is not valid until he takes possession of the capital before he separates [from the seller]. From Ibn Umar: The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of credit with credit; the linguists say it is the sale of deferred with deferred.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage states a condition for the validity of salam: the buyer must take possession of the capital (price) before the parties separate. The proof is the hadith forbidding the sale of one deferred payment for another. In salam, the price is advanced and the goods are delivered later. If both were deferred, it would fall under the prohibited 'kal'i bi kal'i'. Therefore, the capital must be delivered in the contract session. This differs from ordinary sales where possession of the price can be deferred.

Key Terms
الكالى بالكالى (al-kālī bi al-kālī): The sale of deferred payment for deferred delivery.
النسيئة بالنسيئة (al-nasī’ah bi al-nasī’ah): Sale of credit with credit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the capital be taken possession of before the parties separate in a salam contract?
A) Because the hadith prohibits the sale of credit with credit
B) Because the capital is not determined
C) Because the goods are not yet specified
D) Because it is a general rule in all contracts

Key Takeaway
In a salam contract, the buyer must take possession of the capital before the parties separate, as per the hadith prohibiting credit-for-credit sales.

Prohibition of Disposal Before Possession in Salam
Prohibiting any disposal of salam capital or goods before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of salam capital or muslam fihi before possession, and apply the hadith analogy to other commodities.

Core Idea
Disposal of salam capital or goods before possession is prohibited – the rule extends beyond food by analogy.

This lesson examines a key ruling in salam (advance payment) contracts. The text establishes that neither the capital paid nor the goods to be delivered can be sold or transferred before actual possession. The proof comes from a hadith forbidding the sale of food before receipt, which the companion Ibn Abbas extended to all commodities. This ensures the contract's stability and prevents risk.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is disposing (tasarruf) of the capital (ra's al-mal) and the muslam fihi before possession (qabl al-qabd). The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz), meaning it is haram.
Disposal includes sale, gift, or any transfer of ownership.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Ibn Abbas, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbids selling food before taking possession. Ibn Abbas then extends this prohibition by analogy to everything.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition on food (al-ta'am) is extended via qiyas (analogy) to all items because the underlying reason (illah) is the risk of non-delivery and gharar, which applies universally.
Ibn Abbas says: 'I do not think but that everything is like it.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school restricts the prohibition to food only, based on the literal wording of the hadith. They do not extend it via analogical reasoning.
The Hanafi school follows the broader application.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (extending to all goods) is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) due to the strength of the analogy and the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to harm).
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is relied upon in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز التصرف فى رأس المال ولا فى المسلم فيه قبل القبض. عن ابن عباس قال: سمعت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: أما الذي نهى عنه فهو الطعام أن يباع حتى يقبض. قال ابن عباس: ولا أحسب كل شيء إلا مثله.
It is not permissible to dispose of the capital nor of the object of salam before possession. From Ibn Abbas: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'What he forbade is that food be sold before it is taken possession of.' Ibn Abbas said: 'I do not think but that everything is like it.'
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage rules that any disposition (e.g., selling, gifting) of the capital (the price given) or the muslam fihi (the goods to be delivered) is not allowed before taking physical possession. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet forbade selling food before taking possession, and Ibn Abbas extended this analogy to all commodities. Since in salam, the capital is like the purchased item (it is given as advance), it cannot be transferred before actual receipt. The muslam fihi is the actual goods, so the same rule applies. This ensures that the seller can deliver and the buyer avoids risk.

Key Terms
المسلم فيه (al-muslam fīh): The goods to be delivered in a salam contract.
التصرف (al-taṣarruf): Disposal, including sale, gift, or any transfer of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what is the ruling on selling an item before taking possession?
A) It is impermissible for food only
B) It is impermissible for all items by analogy
C) It is allowed if the item is non-food
D) It is allowed on condition of immediate transfer

Key Takeaway
In salam contracts, neither the capital nor the goods can be disposed of before possession; the prohibition applies by analogy to all items.

Prohibition of Partnership and Assignment in Salam Before Possession
A ruling prohibiting two specific sales before possession in salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partnership and assignment in salam contracts before possession and distinguish these from other prohibited dispositions.

Core Idea
Partnership and assignment of muslam fihi before possession are prohibited — transferring ownership requires prior possession.

In salam contracts, the seller delivers goods at a future date, and the buyer pays in advance. A common error is assuming that the buyer can deal with the promised goods before receiving them. This lesson clarifies that partnership (shirkah) and assignment (tawliyah) are specifically prohibited before possession, even though other forms of sale are also generally prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the Arabic text and determine what act is being ruled upon. The text states that two specific acts are not permissible (la yajuz).
The ruling is a prohibition (haram).
2
Define key terms
Understand the terms 'shirkah' (partnership: selling a share) and 'tawliyah' (assignment: selling at cost price).
These are specific forms of disposition.
3
Identify the condition
The prohibition applies when the muslam fihi has not yet been taken possession of (qabl qabdihi).
Possession is a key condition for transfer.
4
Connect to general principle
Recognize that this is an application of the broader rule: disposition of an object before possession is generally prohibited in Hanafi fiqh.
The wisdom is that the buyer does not yet bear the risk of loss.
5
Apply to hypothetical
Consider a scenario: 'A buys 100 kg of dates via salam. Before delivery, he sells half to B (shirkah) or transfers the whole contract to B at cost (tawliyah).' Both are invalid.
The second contract would be void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز الشركة ولا التولية فى المسلم فيه قبل قبضه.
It is not permissible to enter into partnership nor assignment in the object of salam before taking possession of it.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This ruling specifies that two forms of disposition are particularly prohibited regarding the muslam fihi (goods to be delivered) before possession: shirkah (partnership, i.e., selling a share to someone else) and tawliyah (assignment, i.e., selling at cost price to someone else). Both are considered dispositions before possession, which is generally prohibited. The reasoning is that the buyer cannot transfer ownership or share something he has not yet physically received, as the risk of loss remains with the seller until delivery.

Key Terms
الشركة (al-shirkah): Partnership: selling a portion of the muslam fihi to another before possession.
التولية (al-tawliyah): Assignment: selling the muslam fihi to another at the same purchase price before possession.
المسلم فيه (al-muslam fihi): The object of a salam contract; goods to be delivered at a future date.
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT permissible in muslam fihi before taking possession?
A) Partnership (shirkah)
B) Assignment (tawliyah)
C) Both A and B
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
In salam contracts, partnership and assignment of the muslam fihi are prohibited before actual possession.
